Top-Tier Urban Devotion: The Boss Dotes Wildly on His Sweet Wife
(English translation — source folder: Top-Tier Urban Devotion The Boss Dotes Wildly on His Sweet Wife)

============================================================

Chapter 1 — Edge in the Rain
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626203.html

The instant Su Qingyuan pushed open the doors of the banquet hall, the entire room's clamor cut off as though someone had hit pause.

The brilliance of the crystal chandeliers poured down, falling on the washed-out white shirt she wore — and falling, too, on Su Yurou's carefully made-up face up on the stage. The gold trophy cradled in her stepsister's hands threw off a stabbing glint, and on the giant screen behind her, the design for "Fleeting Life" had been blown up to fill an entire wall.

That was her work. Every line, every choice of color, was three months of her own sleepless effort.

The hall was packed with the luminaries of the Capital's design scene — the front rows held the competition judges and sponsors, the middle was the media section, where a thicket of cameras and lenses pointed at the stage. Tonight was the awards gala of the Emerging Designers Competition, the design world's biggest event of the year in the Capital, broadcast live across every platform.

Su Yurou stood beneath the spotlight in a Chanel couture gown, her smile gentle and gracious. "...Thank you to the organizing committee for this recognition. The inspiration for 'Fleeting Life' came from my reflections on life itself — life is fleeting as a dream, and all we can do is hold true to our original heart..."

Before she could finish, the sound of the doors swinging open rang out, jarringly loud in the silence.

Su Qingyuan walked in.

Her appearance was like a drop of water splashed into boiling oil. People turned, one after another; some recognized her and began to whisper. In the front rows, Zhao Xiulan was the first to change color, shooting up from her seat, her expression a mix of shock and fury.

On the stage, Su Yurou saw her too. A flicker of panic crossed her eyes, but it was quickly suppressed, replaced by a look of innocence and wounded grievance.

"Sister?" There was just the right note of surprise in Su Yurou's voice. "What are you doing here? I... I sent you an invitation, but you said you weren't coming..."

Every gaze in the hall converged on Su Qingyuan.

She wore no gown — just a plain white shirt with black trousers, her hair carelessly tied back, utterly out of place in this setting. But her spine was ramrod straight, her steps unhurried, her gaze as calm as a deep, still pool.

Su Qingyuan walked to the foot of the stage, stopped, and lifted her head to look at her stepsister.

"Your trophy used my design draft. Your acceptance speech is my inspiration. Every second of applause you're soaking up on that stage should have been mine."

Her voice wasn't loud, yet it carried clearly through the entire banquet hall.

The room erupted.

The reporters' cameras swung toward her at once, flashes crackling into a wall of light. The live comment feed exploded instantly —

"Holy crap, what's going on? The sister's here to crash the party?"

"Didn't the trending topic a couple days ago say the sister was the one making false claims? When did it flip?"

"This sister is so badass — that aura is off the charts."

Su Yurou's eyes reddened in an instant, tears falling like beads off a broken string. "Sister, I know you've never liked me, because after Dad married Mom he had less attention to spare for you. I understand all of that... but 'Fleeting Life' is a piece I worked on painstakingly for most of a year. How can you say something like this..."

Her voice was choked and aggrieved, and paired with that pitiful, fragile face, the expressions of many in the room shifted at once from shock to sympathy.

A reporter pushed forward and asked, "Miss Su Qingyuan, you say the work is yours — do you have proof?"

Su Qingyuan glanced at the reporter, the corner of her mouth lifting slightly.

"I do."

She took her phone from her pocket, opened a recording, and pressed play.

Zhao Xiulan's voice came out of the phone, shrill and crystal-clear: "...Hand the original draft of 'Fleeting Life' over to Yurou. You won't be using it anyway. The family paid your entry fee for this competition — so what could you possibly use to prove anything to the committee? Listen to Mom, stop making trouble. When your sister does well, our whole family does well."

The hall fell dead silent.

Su Yurou's face went white.

Zhao Xiulan's face went green.

The recording played on, now in Su Qingyuan's voice: "This is a design I spent three months making myself. Why should I give it to her?"

Zhao Xiulan's voice turned even shriller: "You've eaten my food and drunk under my roof all these years to grow this big — what's the harm in letting your sister have one design? You ungrateful little wretch, I never should have let you set foot in this family in the first place!"

There the recording cut off abruptly.

Su Qingyuan put her phone away and looked toward the ashen-faced Su Yurou on the stage. "Do you need more proof? The submission IP records, the upload timeline, the creator information on the original files — I have all of it. Should I release them one by one?"

The air in the entire banquet hall seemed to have been sucked dry.

The comment feed had gone completely insane —

"Damn! She's even got a recording!!!"

"This stepmother is so disgusting — stealing one daughter's work for her own daughter?"

"The sister is so fierce, I love her!!!"

"Whoever just said the sister was making false claims, come out and take your beating!"

Su Yurou's lips trembled. Instinctively she looked toward Zhao Xiulan below the stage. Zhao Xiulan opened her mouth as if to say something, but the stares around her were too sharp, scraping over her like knives, and she couldn't get out a single word.

In the judges' seats up front, several judges' faces had already turned very ugly. Zhang Mingyuan, the director of the competition's organizing committee, stood up, his expression awkward and flustered. "Miss Su, this... this is something we'll still need to investigate. Please don't be upset, we'll definitely give you an explanation..."

"Director Zhang," Su Qingyuan said, looking him dead in the eye, "the submission's IP address traces back to the apartment registered under Su Yurou's name, and the upload time is two days later than the scan of my original handwritten draft. This data is recorded automatically by the server. It can't be altered."

Beads of sweat seeped out on Zhang Mingyuan's forehead.

At that very moment, the side door of the banquet hall was pushed open.

Every gaze in the room was drawn toward it.

A man walked in.

He wore a dark-gray bespoke suit, his frame strikingly tall — sharp brow bone, a high, straight nose, thin lips pressed lightly together. The whole of him was like a blade just drawn from its sheath, cold and dangerous. Only a single assistant trailed behind him, yet his presence felt like it came backed by an army a thousand strong.

The entire room went silent in an instant — quieter even than when Su Qingyuan had walked in.

When Zhang Mingyuan saw who had arrived, his expression changed drastically. He hurried out from behind the judges' table to greet him. "Mr. — Mr. Lu! What brings you here? We've had a small situation, but we'll have it sorted out right away..."

Lu Shiyan.

The sole heir of the Capital's Lu Group.

The young master of "Lu Global," the world's foremost reclusive conglomerate, holding half the kingdoms of finance, technology, luxury goods, and real estate in his grip. Twenty-eight years old, the business world called him "King Yama" — ruthless and absolute in his methods, leaving no room to spare, never once linked to any woman in a rumor, putting on gloves even before a handshake.

A man like that had no business, by any reckoning, showing up at the awards gala of a design competition.

Lu Shiyan didn't look at Zhang Mingyuan, didn't look at anyone, in fact.

His gaze cut through the crowd and landed on Su Qingyuan.

She stood in the shadow of the stage, her white shirt dotted with rainwater — it was raining outside. Everyone was watching her: some with sympathy, some gloating, some just there to enjoy the spectacle, the bigger the better. She stood there alone, facing an entire hall of strangers and the stepsister on the stage weeping like rain on pear blossoms.

She wasn't crying.

There was not a single tear in her eyes. Her spine was straight as a sword that would never break.

Lu Shiyan looked at her, and something in his chest felt as though it had been lightly plucked.

The feeling was strange. He had seen too many people, too many women — socialites, celebrities, daughters of great houses — not one of whom had ever made him spare a second glance. But this woman's eyes — he had looked only once, and he couldn't look away.

"Director Zhang." Lu Shiyan withdrew his gaze, his tone as light as a remark about the fine weather.

"Y-yes, here!" Zhang Mingyuan rushed over.

"A work plagiarized, the original creator's name stolen — this is the 'small situation' you spoke of?"

Cold sweat poured down Zhang Mingyuan's face. "Mr. Lu, we really are investigating. This came on so suddenly..."

"No need for your people to look into it." The chief assistant behind him, Qin Zhou, stepped forward and held out a tablet. "Submission IP records, upload timeline, edit logs — all retrieved in full. The submission's IP address traces back to the apartment registered under Su Yurou's name, and the upload time is two days later than the scan of Su Qingyuan's original handwritten draft. The creator information on the original files and the device serial numbers are all traceable. Furthermore, on Su Yurou's competition entry form, the signature in the 'advising instructor' field is a forgery."

When Qin Zhou finished, he stepped back, his expression professional and calm, as if he were reporting the day's itinerary.

The whole room sank into dead silence once more.

Su Yurou could no longer stay on her feet. She gripped the podium, her lips ghastly pale, tears still streaming — but this time not from grievance, from fear.

Lu Shiyan looked toward the judges' seats. "Do you need more proof?"

No one dared to speak.

The comment feed had already lagged the servers with its flood —

"Who is this man, I'm going to scream!!!"

"It's Lu Shiyan, sis! Lu Global! That Lu family, the richest in the world!!!"

"Why is he standing up for the sister? What's their relationship?"

"Whatever the relationship is, let me ship them first as a sign of respect!!!"

Su Yurou finally broke down. She flung the trophy aside, crouched on the stage, and wailed at the top of her lungs: "It wasn't me! My mom made me do it! She said Sister had lost her chance to compete anyway, so I might as well use the work! I didn't know it would turn out like this, boo hoo hoo..."

Zhao Xiulan's face collapsed entirely. She shrieked and charged onto the stage: "What nonsense are you spouting?! Shut your mouth!"

Mother and daughter started grappling on the stage, and the scene grew very ugly indeed.

The reporters mashed their shutters like mad, the flashes lighting the whole stage bright as day.

Su Qingyuan didn't spare them another glance.

She turned and walked toward the banquet hall doors.

Everything behind her — the wailing, the cursing, the apologizing, the camera flashes — had nothing more to do with her.

She had won, but it wasn't as satisfying as she'd imagined.

She just felt tired.

When she reached the doorway, a low voice called her back.

"Su Qingyuan."

She stopped and turned.

Lu Shiyan had, at some point, come up behind her, less than three steps away. The distance was too close — close enough that she could make out the grain of the black agate cufflink at his sleeve.

"Your work is very good," he said.

Six short words, and yet they made her nose sting.

It was the first time tonight that someone had genuinely, sincerely acknowledged her work — not out of sympathy, not out of guilt.

"...Thank you." Her voice came out a little hoarse.

Lu Shiyan looked at her reddened eyes, his throat bobbing slightly.

He very much wanted to reach out and wipe away the tear hanging at the corner of her eye, the one trembling on the verge of falling.

But he held himself back.

"I'll see you home," he said.

Not "would you like me to see you home," not "let me see you home," but "I'll see you home."

Su Qingyuan lifted her head and met those pitch-black eyes.

Those eyes were very deep, as if they held an entire universe. She couldn't see the bottom, but she saw her own reflection in them.

She didn't know this man.

But she was simply too tired — too tired to find the strength to refuse.

"...All right."

The corner of Lu Shiyan's mouth twitched ever so slightly.

The curve was so faint that, if Qin Zhou hadn't had a sharp eye, he wouldn't have noticed it at all.

Standing three steps away, Qin Zhou was already in inner turmoil.

He had been with Lu Shiyan for five years and had never once seen his boss say a single extra word to any woman. Once, at Paris Fashion Week, a supermodel had approached him to strike up a conversation at a gala; Lu Shiyan hadn't so much as glanced at her, just walked straight off.

And now this man was, of his own accord, saying "I'll see you home."

Qin Zhou drew a deep breath and quietly took out his phone, sending a message to the butler back home: Get things ready. Sir may be bringing someone back tonight.

After a moment's thought, he added another line: Prepare an extra set of women's toiletries. Size S, simple style.

The butler's reply was a single character: ?

Qin Zhou ignored him.

It was only when Su Qingyuan followed Lu Shiyan out of the hotel doors that she realized it was pouring outside.

Rain hammered down on the ground, kicking up a hazy white mist. The portico at the hotel entrance was crowded with people sheltering from the rain; taxis pulled away one after another, but there were never enough.

Su Qingyuan instinctively took half a step back, putting a little more distance between herself and Lu Shiyan.

She wasn't used to standing too close to anyone.

A black Maybach glided silently up to the entrance and stopped.

Qin Zhou trotted over to open the rear door and unfurled an enormous black umbrella.

Lu Shiyan didn't get in right away. Instead he turned his head and looked at Su Qingyuan.

"Get in."

Su Qingyuan hesitated for two seconds.

She didn't know this man. His name might sound impressive, and he might have just resolved a huge problem for her, but experience told her there was no such thing as kindness without a cause in this world. The lesson the Su family had taught her was that everyone who said "I'm doing this for your own good" had a bill behind it that they'd want her to pay back.

But she looked at the torrential rain outside, then looked at her own heel, the skin rubbed raw.

Forget it.

If she owed him, she owed him. She'd pay it back later.

She bent down and got into the car.

The interior of the Maybach was spacious, the leather seats so soft it was like sinking into a cloud. The car's sound system was off; there was only the muffled sound of rain on the roof, which, oddly, made her feel safe instead.

Lu Shiyan sat beside her, a person's width of space between them.

He didn't speak, didn't look at her. He kept his head down over his phone, the screen's blue light reflected on his sharply angled face.

Su Qingyuan leaned against the window, watching the rain trickle down the glass. The halos of the streetlights blurred and softened in the rain, like a watercolor painting soaked through with water.

It was very quiet inside the car — quiet enough that she could hear her own heartbeat.

The strange thing was, this quiet didn't make her feel awkward.

It was as if the two of them didn't need to say much of anything.

The Maybach drove smoothly through the rainy night, passing through the bustling city center and turning into ever narrower streets. The streetlights gradually grew sparse, the road more and more pitted; the tires rolled over standing water, throwing up splashes that struck the windows.

Qin Zhou glanced at Lu Shiyan's expression in the rearview mirror.

The boss didn't look happy.

Not because he was angry — because of this terrible road.

The young master of the Lu Group had probably never in his life traveled a road this rough.

"You can stop up ahead at the intersection," Su Qingyuan finally spoke.

Lu Shiyan raised his eyes and looked at her.

"Where do you live?" he asked.

"Up ahead, at the intersection."

"Su Qingyuan."

When he said her name, his voice was neither high nor low, as though it held a piece of warm jade.

"Where do you live?"

Su Qingyuan pressed her lips together and gave an address.

Qin Zhou silently entered the address into the navigation, and when he saw the photo of the destination, his composure nearly cracked.

It was an old residential complex, as old as old could be, the buildings looking to be more than thirty years old. The exterior paint was mottled and peeling, half the lights in the stairwells were probably broken, and the complex didn't even have a proper gate.

When the Maybach finally stopped beneath that building, Lu Shiyan looked through the window at the dilapidated residential block and fell silent for three seconds.

Su Qingyuan said thank you and pushed open the car door.

Cold wind, laced with rain, gusted in and lifted her hair.

She was about to dash out into the rain when an umbrella was held out in front of her.

Lu Shiyan's hand was sharply knuckled, gripping the black long-handled umbrella, his slender fingers closed around the handle, his posture as casual as if he were doing something trivial.

Su Qingyuan looked at the umbrella, then looked at him.

The rain was heavy; it was probably twenty steps from here to the stairwell entrance. She had no umbrella — her bag had been lost somewhere in the earlier chaos.

"I'll return it tomorrow." She took the umbrella.

"No need to return it."

"..."

Su Qingyuan didn't bother with any more polite refusals. She opened the umbrella and walked into the rain, her high heels stepping into the standing water, the splashes wetting the hems of her trousers.

Lu Shiyan sat in the car, watching her through the rain-blurred window. She didn't walk fast, but every step was steady. The umbrella was held perfectly straight, her spine perfectly upright.

When she reached the stairwell entrance, she paused.

Then she turned around and looked, from a distance, at the Maybach.

Through layer upon layer of rain, Lu Shiyan couldn't make out her expression, but he could feel that gaze land on him, light and thin as a feather.

She turned and went up the stairs.

The sound-activated lights in the stairwell came on floor by floor; her footsteps grew more and more distant, and the lights went out one by one.

It was only when the light on the sixth floor came on and then went dark that Lu Shiyan finally withdrew his gaze.

Qin Zhou asked cautiously, "Mr. Lu, where to?"

Lu Shiyan didn't answer right away.

He leaned back against the seat, his fingers unconsciously tapping the armrest twice. It was a small habit he had only when he was thinking.

"Look into who owns the property rights to that building."

Qin Zhou: "...You're thinking of?"

"Buy it. Renovate it."

Qin Zhou drew a deep breath.

He had been with Lu Shiyan for five years. He'd seen the boss take an entire commercial street with several hundred million, seen him force an opponent at the negotiating table to sign an unequal treaty, seen him cut an entire business division without batting an eye.

But he had never seen the boss buy a building for a woman he'd known for less than an hour.

"Yes, Mr. Lu." Without a flicker on his face, Qin Zhou took out his phone and sent a message to the legal department.

Then he sent another message to the butler: Not coming back tonight. Hold on to that set of women's toiletries for now.

The butler replied: So is he bringing someone or not?

Qin Zhou thought it over and replied: Soon.

He didn't actually know how long "soon" was, but he had a feeling.

That woman called Su Qingyuan was different from everyone before her.

By the time Su Qingyuan got back to her rented room, she was more than half soaked through.

The umbrella was large, but the wind was too strong, and the rain had been coming down at a slant.

The rented room was thirty square meters, the furniture old and worn, the wallpaper peeling up in a few places, the kitchen faucet that wouldn't shut off all the way, dripping endlessly. In one corner sat her drawing tools and materials, and the walls were covered with the design drafts she'd accumulated over the years.

She changed out of her wet clothes, toweled her hair dry, then sat on the edge of the bed and looked at the avalanche of messages on her phone.

The trending topics had already blown up.

#EmergingDesignersCompetitionPlagiarismScandal# had broken five hundred million views and a million comments. Su Yurou's social media account had been picked apart down to its bones; netizens had discovered that several of her past award-winning works bore a striking resemblance to practice drafts Su Qingyuan had once posted publicly.

Zhao Xiulan's phone number had been dug up by netizens and was reportedly already ringing off the hook.

Su Guoliang's silence was being read as "complicity," and the comment section under his company's official account was nothing but a torrent of abuse.

Su Qingyuan's social media account had gained five hundred thousand followers overnight.

She looked at those numbers, her expression calm.

This sort of heat came fast and went fast. Tomorrow everyone would forget her and go chasing the next hot topic. What she needed wasn't fleeting sympathy — it was genuine ability.

And just then, a cold, mechanical voice exploded in her mind.

[Ding — Omnipotent Counterattack System successfully bound. Detecting that the host is currently in a state of extreme adversity, triggering the Beginner's Gift Pack.]

Su Qingyuan sat bolt upright.

"...Who's there?"

========================================

Chapter 2 — A Promise in the Palm of His Hand
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626204.html

[Ding—the All-Around Comeback System has been successfully bound.]
The voice didn't come from her phone, nor from any direction at all. It simply rang inside Su Qingyuan's head, as though something deep in her consciousness had just been switched on.
Su Qingyuan's fingers clenched the bedsheet, her spine drawing taut into a straight line.
"Who's speaking?"
[This unit is an all-around growth-assistance system, serial number 0731. It has detected that the host meets the binding conditions and has automatically established a neural link. The host need not be alarmed; this unit is merely an auxiliary program and possesses no independent consciousness.]
Su Qingyuan was silent for three seconds.
In those three seconds, countless thoughts raced through her mind—was she so exhausted she was hallucinating? Had someone drugged her? Was this…
Outside the window the rain still fell, the faucet still dripped, and her fingers, pinching her own thigh, hurt.
This wasn't a dream.
"Why me?" she asked.
[Host's composite scores: Appearance 87, Intelligence 92, Talent 65, Business 23, Medicine 0, Combat 12. Overall rating: C-minus. Potential assessment: SSS-plus. This unit automatically screens for the individual with the highest potential worldwide who is also in a state of extreme adversity. The host ranks first.]
A string of data unfolded before her eyes, like a translucent screen of light appearing out of nowhere.
Su Qingyuan blinked. The screen was still there.
She reached out to touch it; her fingers passed straight through the emptiness.
[The host cannot currently make physical contact with the system interface. Please operate it by thought.]
Su Qingyuan tried thinking the word "close" in her mind, and the screen really did vanish.
She thought "open" again, and the screen reappeared.
She drew in a deep breath.
Stay calm. Whatever this thing was, it didn't seem hostile, at least for now. And if what it said was true, this might be the greatest turning point of her entire life.
"This starter package you mentioned—what is it?"
The screen lit up again, lines of text floating into view.
[Starter Package Contents:
1. Top-Tier Design Talent (activated)
2. Photographic Memory (activated)
3. Basic Self-Defense (activated)
4. Startup Capital: 100,000 yuan (deposited)]
Her phone buzzed.
Su Qingyuan picked it up and looked: a bank text. A deposit of 100,000.00 yuan had been credited to the account ending in your number; balance 103,247.50 yuan.
She stared at that string of figures for five seconds.
In twenty-three years of living, her bank balance had never once cracked five digits.
[Side quest triggered: The Battle to Clear Your Name.
Quest description: Current public sentiment holds short-term sympathy for the host, but most people still see the host as "the pitiable woman whose work was stolen" rather than "a truly gifted designer." Within 72 hours, please create a top-tier design work, unveil it publicly, and make everyone remember your name—not your misfortune.
Quest reward: Appearance +3, Intelligence +2, unlocks Intermediate Design Talent, unlocks new skill: Piano (Beginner).
Failure penalty: None. (This unit has no penalty mechanism; it merely advises the host to seize the opportunity.)]
Su Qingyuan looked at the quest description, the corner of her mouth curving up faintly.
No penalty mechanism.
This system was rather reasonable.
She glanced at the time on her phone—1:17 a.m. Seventy-two hours, which meant before 1:17 a.m. three days from now.
Three days to create, from scratch, a work that could "make everyone remember her name."
The Su Qingyuan of yesterday would have called it a pipe dream.
But right now, lines, colors, and structures were already surging through her mind—like a flock of birds caged for far too long, suddenly released, all of them scrambling over one another to burst free.
She knew it wasn't a hallucination.
That so-called "top-tier design talent" was real.
Su Qingyuan rolled out of bed, switched on the old desk lamp in the corner, set up her drawing board, and picked up a pencil.
She didn't start sketching right away. Instead, she closed her eyes.
A building took shape in her mind.
Not a building that actually existed—one she had traced over and over in her imagination through countless sleepless nights, a dream. An art museum built by the sea, white from end to end, its curves rising and falling like ocean waves, its glass curtain walls mirroring sky and water until you couldn't tell where the architecture ended and nature began.
She had never been able to draw it before. She could never quite handle those curves, and there was always some structural contradiction she couldn't resolve.
But now, everything was different.
She opened her eyes. The pencil touched the paper.
Shhk, shhk, shhk—
The lines poured out as smoothly as water. She didn't even need to think; her hand simply knew what to draw. Every technical problem that had plagued her for years suddenly had an answer—and not just one answer, but dozens, hundreds, each one exquisite, each one quickening her pulse.
Minute by minute, second by second, time slipped past.
At some point the rain outside had stopped.
The lamplight cast her hunched silhouette against the mottled wall, the pencil flying across the paper—one sheet, two sheets, three…
By four in the morning, she had finished the first draft.
By six, she had drawn rendering views from three angles.
By eight, she had refined it down to the structural joints.
Su Qingyuan set down her pencil, rubbed her aching wrist, and looked at the stack of drawings spread before her, her eyes growing a little hot.
This wasn't the "pretty good" level she used to work at.
This was a height she had never reached. No—not just her. She dared say there weren't more than a handful of people in the entire Capital design scene who could reach this standard.
[Ding—creation progress: 35%. Please be sure to rest, host; excessive fatigue will affect the quality of your work.]
Only then did Su Qingyuan notice that day had broken.
When she stood, her knee gave a sharp click and her head swam a little. She hadn't eaten anything since last night; her stomach had been starving for so long that it had gone past the point of feeling it.
She opened the fridge. Inside there was only half a carton of expired milk and two wilted cucumbers.
She checked the milk's expiration date—five days past.
Without batting an eye, Su Qingyuan put the milk back and picked up her phone to order delivery. But the moment she opened the app, she saw a text from an unknown number, sent at 2 a.m.
"Hello, Miss Su, this is Qin Zhou, Mr. Lu's personal assistant. Mr. Lu asked me to pass along a message: the area in the north of the city has only fair public safety at night, so please take care of yourself. Also, tomorrow at ten in the morning, someone will come to replace your door lock and install security fixtures. You may wait at home at that time, or you may authorize us to handle it directly. If you need anything at all, please feel free to contact this number."
Su Qingyuan paused.
Mr. Lu?
Lu Shiyan?
Into her mind came the image of the man standing at the hotel entrance the night before—holding an umbrella, extraordinarily tall, his gaze very deep.
She looked down at the old wooden door of her rented room—the lock was rusted; one hard kick would open it. She had lived here two years and had never once thought of changing the lock. Not that she hadn't wanted to—she simply hadn't had the money.
This man—how had he thought of even this?
She considered it, then replied: "Thank you, but there's no need to trouble yourselves. I'll be home during the day."
After sending it she felt something was off—why on earth had she told him she'd be home during the day?
Never mind. She was too tired to think about it.
She read the text again and caught a detail: "Mr. Lu asked me to pass along a message"—he had told his assistant to text her at 2 a.m., reminding her to stay safe.
Su Qingyuan set her phone face-down on the table and pressed a hand over her heart.
It was beating a little fast.
Not the fast of fear. Another kind.
She decided not to dwell on it.
At that same moment, in the top-floor office of the tallest building in the Capital's CBD, Lu Shiyan was signing documents.
He had been working for nearly twenty hours straight. After returning from the awards banquet the night before, he had come straight to the company. At one point Qin Zhou had wanted to remind his boss that he ought to rest, but meeting those eyes that betrayed no emotion whatsoever, he swallowed the words back down.
"Mr. Lu," Qin Zhou said, knocking and stepping in, "Miss Su has replied."
Lu Shiyan's pen paused.
"What did she say?"
Qin Zhou glanced at his phone. "She said, 'Thank you, but there's no need to trouble yourselves. I'll be home during the day.'"
The office went quiet for two seconds.
Lu Shiyan set down his pen, leaned back against his chair, and tapped his long fingers twice against the armrest.
"Is she saying not to bother," Qin Zhou ventured, "or is she just being polite?"
Lu Shiyan shot him a look.
Qin Zhou immediately said, "Understood. The security fixtures proceed as planned, the door lock gets swapped for a smart fingerprint lock, a video doorbell goes in, and I've already arranged with property management to replace the motion-sensor lights in the stairwell."
Lu Shiyan said nothing, which counted as tacit approval.
Qin Zhou turned to leave, then was called back.
"That building she lives in—have you looked into the ownership?"
"I have. The building is called No. 6 Xinhua Lane, built in 1992, seven stories, four units per floor, twenty-eight units in all. Ownership belongs to a small company called Hongda Properties, whose actual controller is a local businessman named Liu Jianguo. At present sixty percent of the residents are tenants and forty percent are longtime owner-occupants. The whole building has no elevator; its exterior walls and pipes are severely deteriorated, and over the past three years it's received two condemned-building rectification notices."
"Make an offer. Buy the whole building." Lu Shiyan's tone was the same as if he were saying buy a cup of coffee. "Relocation and resettlement fees for all residents at double the market rate; we'll cover the breach penalties for tenants ending their leases early. Once the acquisition is complete, demolish and rebuild the entire structure to high-end boutique-apartment standards."
Qin Zhou quickly ran the budget for this plan in his head.
Inside the Capital's Second Ring Road, buying a whole old building plus demolition plus reconstruction…
Conservatively, half a billion to start.
"Yes, Mr. Lu." Qin Zhou jotted it down without changing expression. "There's one problem, though. Liu Jianguo isn't an easy man to deal with. A developer once wanted to buy that building of his, and he jacked the price up fivefold on the spot. In the end the deal fell through."
Lu Shiyan picked his pen back up and went on signing.
"Then tell him that if he won't sell, his company will go bankrupt within a month. By then he won't even get that fivefold rock-bottom price."
Qin Zhou: "…"
Yes, boss.
He silently lit a candle for Liu Jianguo in his heart.
In the end Su Qingyuan did order delivery, ate a bowl of congee, then took a shower and slept.
She set an alarm to sleep for only three hours.
When she woke, there were over a dozen missed calls and several dozen messages on her phone. She didn't go through them one by one, just picked out the few that mattered most.
The message from her best friend, Wen Ruan, jumped out the most: "Qingyuan, do you even know you're trending?!! I saw it on set and lost my mind!!! Who is that man?!! Insanely handsome!!! What's your relationship?!! Tell me right now!!!"
Su Qingyuan smiled and replied with two words: "No relationship."
Wen Ruan shot back instantly: "Tell that to someone who'll believe you."
Su Qingyuan didn't reply again and looked at the other messages.
There were sympathies from a few college classmates, feelers from peers in the design circle, and several job offers from headhunters—it seemed someone had already taken note of her name.
She was about to turn off her phone when a new message popped up.
Unknown number. Its contents: a single image.
The image was a scan of a design contract. The client party was "Lu Global Real Estate Group," the project name was "Yunlan Bay Seaside Art Center," and in the line for the design fee was written, in plain sight: eight million yuan.
Below it was a line of text: "Miss Su, Mr. Lu says that if you're interested, this contract can be signed at any time. The project is not on a tight schedule; you may complete it at your own pace. Mr. Lu says, 'She deserves the finest stage.'"
The hand holding her phone trembled slightly.
Eight million.
Not eighty thousand, not eight hundred thousand—eight million.
The most money she had ever seen in her life was the hundred thousand that had landed in her bank account just yesterday.
She knew Lu Shiyan was very rich. At the banquet last night, the way everyone had treated him said it all. But why would he hand her an eight-million-yuan project? Just because she'd drawn one good draft? There were plenty of people in this world who drew well; eight million could hire the most top-tier designers on earth.
Unless…
Su Qingyuan didn't dare let the thought go further.
She put down her phone, took three deep breaths, and let her heartbeat return to normal.
Then she walked to the drawing board and picked up her pencil again.
Whatever that man meant, whether this money was goodwill or a trap, there was only one thing that mattered right now: getting that work onto paper.
Prove herself.
Not to Lu Shiyan, and not to the Su family.
To prove it to herself.
She could do this.
At three in the afternoon, the doorbell rang.
Su Qingyuan lifted her head from her drawings, rubbed her sore, swollen eyes, and went to open the door.
Two men in work uniforms stood outside, one carrying a toolbox, the other holding a cardboard box printed with the logo of a well-known brand.
"Hello, Miss Su, we were sent by Mr. Lu to change your lock and install security fixtures." The one with the toolbox politely presented his work ID.
Su Qingyuan glanced at what was in the cardboard box—a fingerprint lock, a video doorbell, door-and-window sensors, all top brands on the market, some she had never even seen, probably some kind of high-end custom models.
"Come in." She stepped aside.
The two workers moved quickly and worked cleanly; in under an hour they had everything installed and tested. Before they left, they even patched the chunk of wall that had flaked off the door frame with filler, then sanded it smooth, so that you couldn't tell there had been any repair at all unless you looked closely.
Su Qingyuan closed the door and tried out the new fingerprint lock—a light touch of her finger and the door opened, as silky-smooth as running her hand over satin.
She stood at the doorway, stunned for quite a while.
This door, all of a sudden, was completely out of place with the rest of the room.
She looked again at the eight-million contract on her phone, closed her eyes, and drove all those tangled thoughts out of her head.
Draw.
Focus on drawing.
She returned to the drawing board and got back to work.
Minute by minute, second by second, time slipped away.
By six in the evening, she had completed another full set of elevation drawings.
By nine at night, she had finished the section drawings and detailed joints.
At one in the morning, she finally set down her pencil.
Spread before her were forty-two drawings in all. From conceptual sketch to rendering, from floor plan to structural detail, from material selection to lighting design—everything was there, internally consistent, seamlessly whole.
It was an art museum built by the sea.
It had a name—when she finished the last drawing, Su Qingyuan quietly spoke that name in her heart—
"Listening to the Sea."
[Ding—creation progress: 100%. Composite work rating: SSS class. Far exceeds the gold-medal standard of the current top global design competitions.]
The instant the system's chime sounded, the doorbell rang too.
Su Qingyuan started, then walked to the door and glanced at the video doorbell's screen.
A man stood in the stairwell.
Not a worker, not a courier, not a delivery driver.
It was Lu Shiyan.
He wore a dark-gray overcoat, one hand tucked into his pocket, the other just lifted away from the doorbell button. The stairwell's sensor light was on, its dim yellow glow falling over him, plating his whole figure in a layer of warmth.
It was one in the morning.
A light rain was falling outside.
He had come alone—no assistant, no driver—the damp, cold air clinging to him palpable even through the screen.
Su Qingyuan's heart lurched into a faster beat.
She drew in a deep breath and opened the door.

========================================

Chapter 3 — Devotion in Silence
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626205.html

The instant Su Qingyuan opened the door, the motion-sensor light in the corridor flickered and dimmed—then blazed back to life just as Lu Shiyan lifted his head.

The dim yellow light fell across his face. Rainwater slid down the shoulder line of his overcoat, gathering into droplets at his cuffs that dripped soundlessly onto the worn cement floor.

The corridor of this building was far too narrow. Standing there, he seemed to take up the entire space. He was too tall—the crown of his head nearly grazed the bare fluorescent tube overhead—and the whole of him clashed with this shabby backdrop, like a high-end magazine ad that had been Photoshopped onto a demolition notice in some old slum district.

Su Qingyuan looked at him, opened her mouth, and for a moment found she had no idea what to say.

It was one in the morning. Rain fell outside. This man was dressed as though he had just stepped away from some corporate gala—a dark gray cashmere overcoat, a black turtleneck sweater beneath it, crisp and immaculate, not a single crease. But the shoulders of his coat were damp, and fine droplets clung to his hair; clearly he had stood in the rain for more than a moment.

"How did you know where I live?" she asked.

The words were barely out before she felt she'd asked something stupid.

He was prepared to buy the entire building and renovate it from scratch. Knowing which floor and which unit she lived in was nothing to him.

Lu Shiyan didn't answer the question. Instead he lowered his eyes slightly and looked at her.

She had finished showering not long ago; her hair still hung half-damp around her shoulders. She wore an old hoodie, black sweatpants below, and a pair of pilled cotton slippers on her feet. Her face was bare of makeup, her skin so pale it was almost translucent, faint shadows of blue-black beneath her eyes—the mark left by nights spent drafting.

She was a different person entirely from the woman bristling with thorns at the banquet the night before.

Right now she was soft, like a crumpled sheet of paper.

"Finished?" he asked.

Su Qingyuan was startled.

How did he know she'd been painting?

In the next instant she felt that question was also rather foolish. This man knew exactly what time she went to bed; the fact that she had spent the entire day drafting in her rented room had no doubt long since been reported to him by Qin Zhou.

"Mm," she said. "Finished."

"May I see it?"

Su Qingyuan hesitated.

It wasn't that she didn't want to show him. Quite the opposite—she very much wanted to show it to someone. This piece had cost her every ounce of her energy; she had never produced work this good. She wanted someone to know, wanted to hear someone say, "You really painted this beautifully," wanted to see the light kindle in someone's eyes because of her work.

But the drafts were scattered all over the room, strewn in a mess across the table, the floor, the bed. The curtains were a dull yellow striped cloth she'd dug up from a secondhand market, boxes of instant noodles were piled in the corner, and the whole room reeked of cheap laundry detergent.

She didn't want him to see any of this.

Not out of vanity—but because… never mind. She didn't know why either.

"The place is a bit of a mess," she said.

Lu Shiyan glanced at her, his gaze as calm as a still pool.

"It's all right."

He didn't say "I don't mind." He said "It's all right."

Su Qingyuan felt there was a subtle difference between the two. "I don't mind" implied he had noticed her embarrassment but chose to be tolerant of it. "It's all right" implied he didn't regard it as anything at all—whether the room was messy or not had simply never been a question requiring his minding or not minding.

She stepped aside from the doorway.

"Come in."

Lu Shiyan bent to step through the low door frame—he really was too tall; this door was like dressing a child in adult clothes, awkward no matter how you looked at it.

He stood in the entryway, his gaze sweeping across the entire room.

The thirty-square-meter space took it all in at a glance. The bed sat against the far wall, the blanket folded with perfect neatness. The desk by the window was piled high with design books, their spines frayed from constant flipping. In the corner stood a drawing board and an easel; pencil shavings and eraser crumbs littered the floor. On the walls were pinned some of her old practice sketches, several already yellowed with age.

His gaze came at last to rest at the very center of the room—where a makeshift worktable had been set up, on it forty-two drafts arranged in perfect order, from concept sketches to rendered images, from floor plans to detail nodes, every one of them complete.

Su Qingyuan followed behind him, watching as he walked toward the drafts.

He walked slowly, as though giving the room a moment to breathe. The black leather shoes pressed against the cement floor, making a faint sound. The hem of his coat brushed past the jacket she'd tossed carelessly on the floor—no pause, no frown, as though those things did not exist.

Lu Shiyan stopped before the worktable.

He looked down at the first draft—the overall rendering of "Listening to the Sea." A pure white building rose along the coastline, its curves as gentle as a stone caressed over and over by the sea wind. The glass curtain wall wasn't straight but tilted ever so slightly, so that sunlight would refract through it at a special angle, casting rippling patches of light across the floor, as if the sea had surged indoors.

He said nothing.

He went through them one by one, like reading a book. He lingered long over each image—composition to line, light and shadow to texture, missing not a single detail.

Su Qingyuan stood behind him, watching his back, her heart beating inexplicably fast.

She had confidence in her drafts, of course—but that was by her own standard. She didn't know whether, in the eyes of a man like Lu Shiyan, these things were good enough.

He looked for a long time.

Long enough that Su Qingyuan began to feel uneasy.

At last he finished the final detail-node drawing and turned around.

Su Qingyuan met his eyes and found in those jet-black pupils a kind of light she had never seen before. Not polite admiration, not a perfunctory "not bad," but something almost scrutinizing, earnest, carrying a certain solemn approval.

"Su Qingyuan," he said, "do you know what you've painted?"

His tone left her a little tense. "My work."

"No," Lu Shiyan said. "You've painted an era."

There was no exaggerated rhetoric in the words. He said it very calmly, as though stating a fact.

Su Qingyuan froze where she stood.

Instinctively she wanted to say "You flatter me," but the words caught in her throat. Because she saw his expression—he wasn't comforting her, nor was he flattering her. This man had no need to flatter anyone.

He truly believed it.

"The Yunlan Bay project—the original budget was twelve million, eight million for design and four million for construction." Lu Shiyan said. "Now I'm going to change the budget."

Su Qingyuan's heart sank.

Yes, she thought. Eight million was too much. She was an unknown newcomer; what right did she have to a design fee of eight million?

"Thirty million," Lu Shiyan said. "Twenty million for design, ten million for construction."

Su Qingyuan thought she'd misheard.

"What?"

"If your design were built on the original budget, it would be a desecration of it." Lu Shiyan's tone was still that maddening calm. "The structural curved surfaces require higher-grade concrete, the tilt angle of the glass curtain wall requires custom molds, and if the interior floor is to mimic the play of light on water, it must use a special imported Italian stone—all of which costs money."

Su Qingyuan opened her mouth. "How did you know I wanted to use that stone?"

Lu Shiyan glanced at her.

"The fourth of your detail-node drawings—the stone-jointing method you drew—I've only seen its match in a private collection room in the Carrara quarry district of Italy."

Su Qingyuan was utterly speechless now.

She knew that someone had collected that stone—she had stumbled across it while researching material for her thesis during graduate school. But that paper was written in Italian, published in a journal almost no one in the country subscribed to, let alone something read by a man in real estate investment.

Just how much had this man seen?

"The Yunlan Bay Art Center is not one of my real estate projects," Lu Shiyan continued. "It was my mother's last wish before she died. She was an architect."

Su Qingyuan's heart gave a violent jolt.

There was no ripple of emotion on Lu Shiyan's face, but she couldn't say why—she simply felt that his voice was different from a moment ago, as though something were flowing beneath a thin sheet of ice.

"Before she passed, she drew thirty-seven versions of the design, and she wasn't satisfied with any of them. She said this place was too special; it had to be designed by someone who truly understood the sea." Lu Shiyan's gaze fell on the drafts, his voice dropping low. "She never lived to meet that person."

The room fell silent for a few seconds.

The faucet was still dripping, drip after drip, like some ancient timekeeper.

"Your design is the answer she was searching for," Lu Shiyan said.

Su Qingyuan lowered her eyes, her lashes trembling faintly.

Not because she was moved—though she truly was. But because she suddenly understood why this man had appeared at the awards gala of the design competition, why he had stood up for her, why he had come through the rain to her rented room at one in the morning.

Not because of "devotion"—at least not entirely.

It was because he truly understood her design.

A tycoon who held half the world in his grasp, a man the business world called "the King of Hell," a man rumored to be cold, untouchable, a lone wolf who never went near women—and yet he understood her design.

That stirred her heart more than any words of love could.

"Where's the contract?" Su Qingyuan lifted her head.

Lu Shiyan drew a document from the inner pocket of his coat and handed it to her.

Su Qingyuan took it, didn't look at the second page, flipped straight to the last, picked up a pen, and signed her name.

Lu Shiyan watched the fluid grace of her movements, and rarely revealed an expression—one eyebrow lifting just slightly.

"You don't read the terms?"

"Whatever you've offered is certain to be the best terms." Su Qingyuan handed the signed contract back. "Besides, even if you weren't paying, I'd still paint it."

"Why?"

"Because that place is worth it."

Lu Shiyan took the contract and looked down at the elegant signature on the last page. Su Qingyuan. The three characters were written cleanly and crisply—no flourishes, no connecting strokes—just like the person herself: clean, clear.

"There's one more thing," he said. "The International Young Designers Competition, three days from now—I need you to enter."

Su Qingyuan was taken aback. "Hasn't registration for that competition already closed?"

"Lu Group Global is the title sponsor of the competition." Lu Shiyan's tone was as flat as if he'd said, "The rain's a bit heavy today." "A supplementary slot can be added anytime."

Su Qingyuan: "…"

Fine, very nice, very rich.

"Why do you need me to enter?"

"Because the global grand champion of that competition earns a solo exhibition at Milan Design Week." Lu Shiyan looked at her. "Your 'Listening to the Sea' deserves to be seen by the whole world."

Su Qingyuan's heart skipped a beat.

Milan Design Week. The ultimate dream of designers across the globe. A twenty-three-year-old newcomer designer from China holding a solo show at Milan Design Week—such a thing had never happened in all of history.

"I'll enter," she said.

The system's notification chime sounded in her mind right on cue.

【Ding—Main quest triggered: The Path to Global Apotheosis.

Quest description: Win the global grand championship of the International Young Designers Competition and secure the qualification for a solo exhibition at Milan Design Week.

Quest reward: Appearance +5, Intelligence +5, unlock Advanced Design Talent, unlock new skill: Advanced Language Talent (including native-level mastery of Italian, French, and English), unlock new skill: Advanced Piano Performance.

Stage quest rewards: reaching the global finals, winning the continental championship, and winning the global grand championship each carry additional rewards.】

Su Qingyuan drew a deep breath.

She knew that from this moment on, her path would no longer be one arranged for her by others.

Lu Shiyan put the contract away and glanced toward the door.

"It's late. You should rest."

Su Qingyuan nodded. She really was exhausted—from yesterday until now, she'd slept only three hours.

Lu Shiyan turned and walked toward the door.

Su Qingyuan followed behind to see him out.

When he reached the doorway, he suddenly stopped and turned around. The turn was so abrupt that Su Qingyuan couldn't check her step and nearly collided with his chest.

The distance between them had narrowed to barely a dozen centimeters.

She could smell that cold, crisp scent on him—not cologne, more like some expensive fabric-care product, clean, aloof, untouchable, just like the man himself.

Lu Shiyan lowered his head and looked at her.

From this angle she could clearly see the sharp arc of his jawline, see the shadow his lashes cast across his cheekbone.

"Su Qingyuan," he said, "you don't need to live here anymore."

Su Qingyuan was startled.

"Qin Zhou will arrange new lodgings for you. It's not charity—it's a condition of our partnership. The designer of the Yunlan Bay project cannot live in a condemned building. That's my bottom line."

His tone brooked no argument, like a business clause so reasonable it couldn't be refused.

Su Qingyuan opened her mouth, wanting to say "There's no need," but meeting his gaze, the words lodged in her throat.

Not because she was afraid.

It was because she saw something in his eyes—not sympathy, not pity, but a kind of very earnest, very solemn… care.

He wasn't helping her because he thought she was pitiable.

He thought she deserved to be treated well.

"…All right," she said.

The corner of Lu Shiyan's mouth moved ever so slightly, the curve a fraction larger than the one outside the hotel the night before.

"Good night."

He turned and left.

Su Qingyuan stood in the doorway, watching his back disappear around the bend of the corridor. His footsteps descended, one after another, the voice-activated lights flaring on floor by floor—then, as his steps receded into the distance, dimming again floor by floor.

Only when all the lights had gone out did she close the door.

Leaning back against that brand-new door fitted with a smart fingerprint lock, she slowly slid down to the floor and buried her face in her knees.

Her heart was beating too fast.

So fast it almost frightened her.

At eight o'clock the next morning, Qin Zhou appeared at the door right on time.

When Su Qingyuan opened the door, Qin Zhou's gaze swept quickly around the room—the forty-two drafts were already sealed in protective sleeves, stacked neatly in a single drawing tube. The suitcase was already packed, just one, an old one, its zipper mended with needle and thread.

"Good morning, Miss Su," Qin Zhou said with a polite nod. "The car is waiting downstairs. Here are the keys to your new residence; your fingerprint has already been registered, so you can use it directly. Also, Mr. Lu asked me to relay that the registration for the International Young Designers Competition has been taken care of—you don't need to do anything, just prepare your work."

Su Qingyuan took the keys and nodded.

She glanced once at the rented room she'd lived in for two years. The paintings on the walls hadn't yet been taken down, a nearly withered pothos sat on the windowsill, the kitchen faucet still dripping.

Nothing here worth missing.

"Let's go," she said.

On the way down, Qin Zhou took the initiative to carry her suitcase, walking ahead. Su Qingyuan followed behind, noticing that all the corridor sensor lights had been replaced—the broken ones repaired, the dim bulbs swapped for bright LEDs, every floor aglow.

A black business sedan was parked at the building entrance—not the Maybach from the night before.

Qin Zhou opened the car door. "Mr. Lu has an early meeting today and can't come in person; he asks for Miss Su's understanding."

Su Qingyuan wanted to say she hadn't expected him to come in person at all, but the words felt strange on the tip of her tongue, so she only gave a soft "Mm."

The car drove out of the old neighborhood in the north of the city, crossed downtown, and turned into a high-end apartment district on the east side of the Capital.

Su Qingyuan watched the increasingly unfamiliar streetscape outside the window and felt, faintly, that something was off.

The car finally stopped beneath an apartment tower in the core of the CBD. She recognized this building, of course—Yunxi, the most expensive residence in the Capital. The top-floor full-floor penthouse was said to sell for over two hundred million; those who lived inside were nothing if not rich and powerful.

Qin Zhou swiped the access card and took her up by elevator straight to the top floor.

When the elevator doors opened, Su Qingyuan froze.

The entire top floor was a single open-plan unit, easily over three hundred square meters by her estimate. The living room was a floor-to-ceiling glass curtain wall, overlooking the whole skyline of the Capital. The décor was minimalist modern, in shades of gray and white, nothing superfluous, every detail exuding a quality that whispered, "I'm very expensive, but I won't say so."

"This is a vacant property under Mr. Lu's name," Qin Zhou said, his tone as flat as if introducing the day's weather. "Mr. Lu says that with you living here, he can come discuss the project plans anytime."

He delivered "come discuss the project plans anytime" with utter naturalness.

Su Qingyuan stood in the middle of the living room, looking out at the panoramic view of the city, only one thought in her mind.

This man's way of doing things was just like his looks—it left a person utterly defenseless.

Her phone buzzed.

She glanced down—a message from Lu Shiyan.

"Are you satisfied with the place?"

Su Qingyuan thought for a moment, then typed a few words: "It's too big. A waste for me to live here alone."

The reply came instantly: "Not a waste. I have a three-thousand-square-meter one. That's far more of a waste."

Su Qingyuan: "…"

She stared at that message for five seconds, the corners of her mouth curving up beyond her control.

This business-world King of Hell, rumored to be cold and untouchable, ascetic and aloof—and he actually made jokes.

Phone in hand, she walked into the bedroom prepared for her—the sheets and bedding all new, in the gray-blue she liked. On the nightstand sat a bouquet of white chamomile, small and very understated, with a card that read: Welcome home.

Not "Welcome to your new home"—but "Welcome home."

Su Qingyuan turned the card over. On the back was a line in Lu Shiyan's handwriting.

The strokes were bold and forceful, just like the man himself.

"You deserve all the best things in this world. —Lu."

Su Qingyuan looked at that line of words, and her eyes suddenly reddened.

In all her life, no one had ever said this to her.

No one.
