Chapter 6 — The Light of Milan
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626208.html

The Light of Milan
On the day they set off for Milan, Su Qingyuan ran into someone she never expected to see at the airport.
Wen Ruan.
Her best friend, wearing a goose-yellow coat and pushing two enormous suitcases, stood at the check-in counter waving at her like a madwoman, an "you finally made it" expression plastered across her face.
Su Qingyuan stopped in her tracks and turned to Lu Shiyan beside her.
"Was this your doing?"
Lu Shiyan's expression didn't change. "She said she wanted to watch you accept your award. And do some shopping while she was at it."
"I haven't accepted any award yet."
"She said it's a head start on the celebration."
Su Qingyuan looked at those two oversized suitcases and went silent for a couple of seconds. This woman wasn't going to Milan to watch a competition—she was clearly going to Milan to run a personal-shopper racket.
Wen Ruan came trotting over and threw her arms around Su Qingyuan, her voice trembling with excitement. "Qingyuan! I'm sitting with you! I'm going to watch you become a legend in Milan!"
"The seats on the plane are assigned."
"I don't care, I'm sitting with you!" Wen Ruan turned to Lu Shiyan, her eyes carrying a distinct "if you say no I'll expose you" sort of threat.
Lu Shiyan glanced at Qin Zhou.
Qin Zhou immediately pulled out his phone, and three seconds later looked up. "Miss Wen's seat has been changed to the one next to Miss Su."
Wen Ruan nodded in satisfaction, leaned in close to Su Qingyuan's ear, and lowered her voice. "This man of yours—efficient, I'll give him that."
Su Qingyuan's ears went faintly red.
"He's not 'my man' yet," she corrected quietly.
Wen Ruan's eyes went wide. "You still haven't made it official? He's done all this for you—bought you a building, cleared your path, helped you start a company, flown to Milan with you—and you two still aren't together? Su Qingyuan, is something wrong with you?"
Su Qingyuan took a deep breath and decided she was not going to discuss the progress of her love life in the middle of an airport terminal.
After they boarded, Wen Ruan did indeed sit next to Su Qingyuan, while Lu Shiyan sat in the row ahead. Qin Zhou sat beside Lu Shiyan, spine ramrod-straight the whole time, glancing back at the situation in the rear row every now and then like a dutiful sentry.
Once the plane took off, Wen Ruan grabbed Su Qingyuan's arm and dropped her voice. "Seriously, what exactly is going on between you two? What do you actually feel for him?"
Su Qingyuan looked out at the cloud banks receding into the distance and was quiet for a while.
"I don't know how to describe it," she said. "It's just… before, I thought the world was a cold place. So cold I had to wrap myself up tight just to survive. But after he showed up, it didn't seem so cold anymore."
Wen Ruan's eyes reddened.
"Qingyuan, you've finally met the right person."
Su Qingyuan didn't deny it.
Above the clouds beyond the window, the sunlight was almost absurdly brilliant.
At two in the afternoon, Milan time, the plane touched down at Malpensa Airport.
Milan in November was crisp and damp. The sky was a pale grayish blue, and the silhouettes of the ancient buildings drifted in and out of the thin mist, like an oil painting steeped in the passage of years.
Lu Shiyan had arranged cars in advance—two of them: one for him and Su Qingyuan, one for Wen Ruan and Qin Zhou.
Wen Ruan protested. "Why do I have to ride with Qin Zhou? I want to ride with Qingyuan!"
Qin Zhou's face was expressionless. "Miss Wen, the back seat of that car only has two places. Are you sure you want to squeeze in with Mr. Lu?"
Wen Ruan took one look at Lu Shiyan's keep-your-distance aura and promptly gave up.
"Fine. Qin Zhou, you can fill me in on Mr. Lu's gossip on the way."
Qin Zhou's expression didn't budge an inch. "I don't have any gossip."
"Liar."
"I don't."
"Then why are your ears red?"
Qin Zhou silently started the car.
Watching the back-and-forth between Wen Ruan and Qin Zhou in the car behind through her window, Su Qingyuan couldn't help laughing.
"Qin Zhou seems pretty scared of Wen Ruan," she said.
Lu Shiyan glanced at the rearview mirror, his tone flat. "He's scared of anyone who talks a lot."
"And you? What are you scared of?"
Lu Shiyan turned his head and looked at her.
"I'm scared of you crying."
Su Qingyuan's heart suddenly raced.
She looked away, turning toward the window and pretending to take in the scenery. But her fingers curled slightly against her knee, the knuckles going white.
This man was always saying things like this without any warning, leaving her utterly defenseless.
The car wound through the streets of Milan and stopped before a nineteenth-century building. It was a private design club, open only to the world's top designers, its membership including the Zaha Hadid estate foundation, Rem Koolhaas, and Philippe Delort himself.
The doorman wore a tailcoat, and when he pulled the door open he gave a slight bow, his bearing as graceful as a dancer mid-step in some ancient court dance.
Wen Ruan climbed out of the car behind them, and when she saw the building she sucked in a sharp breath. "This place… I feel like I'd get charged just for breathing."
Qin Zhou stood beside her and said, deadpan, "Breathing's free. But staining the carpet means paying for it."
Wen Ruan shot him a glare.
Su Qingyuan drew a deep breath and stepped through the door.
The corridor was long, and the walls on both sides were hung with design drafts—a sketch of Mies van der Rohe's Barcelona Pavilion, the façade of Le Corbusier's Notre-Dame du Haut chapel, the original works of a few contemporary masters she couldn't place. Every single one was an original. Every single one was priceless.
Su Qingyuan's steps slowed.
Not out of nervousness, but because the kind of vitality these drawings gave off—a vitality that reached across time—filled her with awe.
Lu Shiyan walked at her side, without hurrying her.
He understood this feeling.
At the end of the corridor was a heavy wooden door, with no nameplate, only a brass handle polished to a shine by countless hands.
Lu Shiyan pushed it open.
Behind the door was a spacious reception room. A fire burned in the hearth, the logs crackling. Several large architectural photography pieces hung on the walls, and the light beyond the window spilled in through white gauze curtains, bathing the whole room in a soft glow.
By the window, an old man with a head of white hair was bent over something, studying it.
At the sound of the door, he raised his head.
Philippe Delort. Seventy-three years old, a titan in the global fields of architecture and design, chairman of the jury for the International Young Designers Competition. His hair had gone completely white, but his eyes were astonishingly bright, like two dark gems buffed to a gleam.
His gaze slid past Lu Shiyan and came to rest on Su Qingyuan.
He looked at her for a long time.
So long that Su Qingyuan felt her heart was about to stop.
Then Philippe stood up.
He was not tall, his back slightly stooped, and he wore a dark gray wool sweater, a pair of khaki casual trousers, and a worn pair of brown leather shoes. He looked less like an emperor of the design world and more like a kindly old grandfather from next door.
He walked over to Su Qingyuan and held out his hand.
"Su," he said. Not Miss Su, not Su Qingyuan—just "Su." A single syllable, clean and crisp, as if they had known each other a very long time.
Su Qingyuan took his hand.
The old man's hand was thin, the joints pronounced, but warm and strong.
"Mr. Delort, it's an honor."
Philippe didn't let go; instead he watched her with those astonishingly bright eyes.
"Do you know why I wanted to meet you?" he said in English, heavily accented with French.
Su Qingyuan thought about it. "Because of my work?"
"No." Philippe released her hand, turned, and picked up a stack of drawings from the table—her very own "Fracture and Rebirth" series.
He flipped to the first one, the overall rendering she had drawn. A building growing up out of the ruins, old brick walls interwoven with new steel framework, like a giant rising again from its own wounds.
"Because this work," Philippe said, "reminded me of why I chose this profession."
Su Qingyuan froze.
Philippe set the drawings down on the table, turned, and faced the flames leaping in the hearth. His voice grew slow and far-off, as though recounting a story from long ago.
"When I was eighteen, my hometown was struck by a great earthquake. The whole city was reduced to rubble. Everyone was in despair, certain that it was all over. But three months later, I saw an old man on the ruins. Beside a collapsed house, he was using bricks from the wreckage to rebuild the wall, one brick at a time."
Philippe turned his head and looked at Su Qingyuan.
"I asked him, why bother building? It's all destroyed anyway. He said, it's precisely because it's destroyed that we must build. The ruins are not the end. They are the beginning."
The old man's voice trembled slightly.
"In that moment I understood: architecture is not about putting up buildings. It is about planting hope on the ruins. I chose this profession not because I loved design, but because I wanted to become the man laying bricks on the ruins."
He walked back over to Su Qingyuan and picked up her drawings.
"Su, your work let me see that old man. Not because of technique, not because of talent, but because there's something in your work—you are laying bricks on the ruins."
Su Qingyuan's eyes reddened.
Philippe set the drawings down and patted her shoulder.
"Technique can be learned, talent can be trained, but a heart that lays bricks on the ruins cannot be learned or trained. It is given by a person's own life. Su, you must have been through a great many terrible things in your past."
Su Qingyuan's tears finally fell.
This French old man she had never met before had seen straight through her in three minutes. Seen through twenty-three years of grievance, seen through every one of her scars, seen through all the words she had hidden behind those lines and never dared to speak aloud.
"Those terrible things did not break you," Philippe said softly. "They became the bricks you build with. Su, that is your gift. Not the gift of drawing—the gift of being alive."
Wen Ruan stood in the doorway, already dissolved into a sobbing mess.
Qin Zhou handed her a pack of tissues, expressionless. "Miss Wen, your makeup is running."
Wen Ruan blew her nose and said, "Shut up."
Lu Shiyan stood off to one side, watching Su Qingyuan cry, his fingers tightening slightly and then loosening.
He badly wanted to walk over and wipe her tears away.
But he knew that, in this moment, she didn't need him. What she needed was an old man's recognition of someone younger, a master's blessing upon someone just starting out.
So he stood there, watching quietly.
Su Qingyuan drew a deep breath, swiped clumsily at her tears with her sleeve, and looked at Philippe, her voice a little hoarse. "Mr. Delort, thank you."
Philippe smiled, a smile as guileless as a child's. "Don't thank me. You should thank yourself. Because you didn't lie down in the ruins. You stood up."
He took another folder from the table and handed it to Su Qingyuan.
"Open it and see."
Su Qingyuan opened the folder. Inside was a formal letter of invitation.
"Milan Design Week—a solo exhibition. Run dates: March of next year. Venue: the main pavilion of Milan Design Week, the premier booth."
Su Qingyuan's breath caught for a beat.
Milan Design Week, the ultimate stage for designers the world over. The premier booth in the main pavilion was never given to newcomers. In all of history, no designer from China had ever claimed that booth before the age of thirty.
And now, that letter of invitation was in her hands.
"Mr. Delort, this…"
"It wasn't my decision," Philippe said, waving a hand. "It was the decision of the Milan Design Week organizing committee. After your work was passed around the jury, everyone agreed unanimously. Su, you no longer need anyone to give you opportunities. Your work is the best calling card there is."
Su Qingyuan held that invitation, her fingers trembling faintly.
Behind them, Wen Ruan asked Qin Zhou under her breath, "Is that booth a big deal?"
In a voice only the two of them could hear, Qin Zhou said, "Last year that booth went to a Pritzker Prize laureate. The year before, to OMA. The year before that, to Zaha Hadid's firm."
Wen Ruan sucked in a sharp breath.
"So doesn't that mean Qingyuan just… vaulted straight to the top?"
Qin Zhou glanced at her. "Miss Su didn't vault to the top. She was always up there—she just got seen."
Wen Ruan paused, then said quietly, "Qin Zhou, you don't say much most of the time, but when you do, it's actually pretty profound."
Qin Zhou turned his head away, expressionless, but the tips of his ears went red.
Philippe kept Su Qingyuan and Lu Shiyan in the reception room talking for a long while.
He asked Su Qingyuan in detail about her design philosophy, her creative process, her plans for the future. He was not the sort of master who looked down from on high; he was more like an old student with a voracious thirst for knowledge, every question probing deep, very deep—so deep that Su Qingyuan had to think it over carefully before she could answer.
And each of her answers made his eyes light up.
At last, Philippe leaned back against the sofa and let out a long breath.
"Lu," he said, looking at Lu Shiyan, "this girl—you'd best take good care of her. She will be the greatest designer of this century. Whoever loses her, all of humanity will hate him for it."
Lu Shiyan looked at Su Qingyuan, the corner of his mouth curving up slightly.
"I know."
By the time they left the club, night had fallen over Milan.
The old streets gave off an amber glow under the streetlamps. In the distance, the spires of the Milan Duomo stood out clearly against the night sky, like so many arrows pointing toward the heavens.
Wen Ruan and Qin Zhou walked ahead, talking about who-knew-what; Wen Ruan was laughing happily, and Qin Zhou, still expressionless, walked with a noticeably lighter step.
Su Qingyuan and Lu Shiyan walked behind, half a pace apart.
The night wind was a little chilly, and Su Qingyuan hunched her shoulders.
The next second, a coat was draped over them.
The coat still carried Lu Shiyan's warmth, and that scent of his—clean to the point of crispness.
"Aren't you cold?" Su Qingyuan asked.
"No."
Su Qingyuan glanced at his upper body, clad in nothing but a thin sweater, and said nothing.
He was definitely cold—but he would never admit it.
She pulled the coat tighter around herself and walked on with her head down. The streetlamps stretched their two shadows long across the ancient cobblestones, like two trees whose roots had grown intertwined.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"When did you start thinking my work was good?"
Lu Shiyan thought about it.
"From the first glance."
"The first glance? At the awards banquet?"
"At the hotel entrance." Lu Shiyan's voice was low and steady. "When you walked out of the banquet hall, you weren't holding anything in your hands, but I saw light in your eyes. That light—it wasn't anger, it wasn't grievance. It was defiance. A person who refuses to lose can't possibly fail to create something good."
Su Qingyuan stopped and turned to look at him.
The lamplight fell across his face, softening his sharp features by a few degrees. His eyes were deep, and in them were reflected her own image and a whole sky full of stars.
"You refuse to lose," he said, "so I refuse to lose too. I'm going to make the whole world see you."
Su Qingyuan's heart gave a sudden lurch.
The night wind passed between the two of them, carrying the cool of Milan's late autumn and the toll of a distant church bell.
Su Qingyuan reached out and lightly touched the back of his hand.
Just a touch—and then she meant to pull it back.
But Lu Shiyan's hand was faster, turning to clasp hers.
His palm was large, dry and warm, wrapping her whole hand within it.
Su Qingyuan lowered her head, looked at their joined hands, and felt the corners of her mouth lift.
She didn't pull away.
And Lu Shiyan didn't let go.
The two of them walked hand in hand like that through the ancient streets of Milan. At some point Wen Ruan up ahead glanced back, then suddenly yanked at Qin Zhou's sleeve, shriek-whispering, "They're holding hands they're holding hands they're holding hands!!! Aaaaahhh!!!"
The yank made Qin Zhou stumble, and he steadied himself, expressionless. "Miss Wen, please mind your volume."
"I don't care! I've waited so long for some sugar, and now that I've finally got it, how am I supposed to not care?!" Wen Ruan whipped out her phone to take a picture, only for Qin Zhou to press her hand down.
"Mr. Lu won't allow it."
"Then I won't post it—I'll just keep it for myself!"
Qin Zhou hesitated, then let go of her hand.
Wen Ruan snapped a photo—in the distance, Lu Shiyan and Su Qingyuan walking hand in hand beneath the streetlamps, neither of them looking at the camera, yet the image was more moving than any posed shot could ever be.
Looking at the photo, Wen Ruan's eyes reddened again.
"Qin Zhou."
"Mm."
"Do you think they'll always stay like this?"
Qin Zhou glanced at those two figures walking side by side in the distance, and for once let an expression cross his face that wasn't blank.
"They will."
The next day, when Su Qingyuan woke in her hotel room, dozens of new messages had appeared on her phone.
Most of them were congratulations—somehow, someone had leaked the news of the Milan Design Week invitation, and the domestic media had already begun reporting on it.
But one message was different.
It came from an unknown number, and contained a single line: "Su Qingyuan, you think going to Milan means you've won? Dream on."
Su Qingyuan looked at the message and let out a cold laugh.
She didn't reply. Instead she screenshotted the number and sent it straight to Qin Zhou.
"Find out whose number this is."
Qin Zhou replied instantly. "Got it. Miss Su, Mr. Lu asked me to pass along that at tonight's banquet, you may run into a few people."
"Who?"
"Su Guoliang and Su Yurou."
Su Qingyuan's fingers paused.
"They came to Milan?"
"Yes. Su Yurou pulled some strings to get a ticket to tonight's banquet. The banquet is a warm-up event for Milan Design Week, hosted by the Italian Designers Association. Su Yurou applied as an 'independent designer.'"
Su Qingyuan set down her phone and walked to the window.
A Milan morning—sunlight spilling through the ancient buildings onto the streets, a sea of gold.
Su Yurou had chased her all the way to Milan.
She thought she could still do what she'd always done—snatch away the things that belonged to Su Qingyuan.
Looking at her own reflection in the glass, Su Qingyuan let the corners of her mouth lift slightly.
Things were different now.
This time, she would never let anyone snatch anything away from her again.
She turned and walked toward the dressing room, beginning to pick out a dress for tonight's banquet.
Since Su Yurou wanted to come, then she would let her stepsister get a good, long look at what a real designer was.
Outside the window, the sunlight grew brighter and brighter; a new day in Milan had begun.
Su Qingyuan looked at herself in the mirror, and in her eyes was a light she had never had before.
It wasn't anger, and it wasn't a thirst for revenge.
It was a kind of certainty—she knew her own ability, knew her own worth, knew that she would never again be trampled underfoot by anyone.
Lu Shiyan sent a message: "Are you ready?"
Su Qingyuan replied with a single word: "Yes."
"I'm waiting downstairs."
Su Qingyuan picked up her clutch and walked out of the room.
The elevator descended all the way down, and when it reached the ground floor, the doors opened.
Lu Shiyan stood in the lobby, wearing a black bespoke suit, no tie, the collar of his shirt slightly open, looking for all the world as though he'd just stepped off the runway at Milan Fashion Week.
When he saw Su Qingyuan, his gaze held for an instant.
Su Qingyuan wore a hazy-blue velvet gown, the hem flaring softly at her ankles like a flower blooming upside down. Her hair was pinned up, baring a slender, fair stretch of neck. She rarely wore makeup, and even today she had only lightly traced her brows and applied a thin layer of lipstick.
But it was precisely that understatement that made her look like a beauty who had stepped out of a classical oil painting.
Lu Shiyan's gaze rested on her for three seconds, then moved away.
"Let's go," he said.
Su Qingyuan walked to his side, and the two of them headed for the door shoulder to shoulder.
Qin Zhou was already waiting in the car.
The car drove toward the venue of the banquet—one of Milan's oldest palaces, built in the fifteenth century and now one of the core venues of Milan Design Week.
Watching the streetscape rush backward past the window, Su Qingyuan suddenly spoke. "Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Su Yurou is here."
"I know."
"You're not going to ask what I plan to do?"
Lu Shiyan turned his head and looked at her.
"Do whatever you want to do," he said. "If the sky falls, I'll hold it up."
Su Qingyuan's heart skipped a beat.
She lowered her head and looked at her hands resting on her knees. Lu Shiyan's hand reached over, settled on the back of hers, and gave it a light squeeze.
"Don't be afraid," he said.
"I'm not afraid." Su Qingyuan lifted her head, a fire burning in her eyes. "I'm just thinking about how to teach her a lesson."
The corner of Lu Shiyan's mouth curved up.
"Then teach her a lesson."
The car pulled up at the palace gates.
A red carpet ran from the entrance all the way out to the street, flanked on both sides by media reporters with cameras raised. When Su Qingyuan stepped out of the car, the flashbulbs went off in a blaze.
She stood on the red carpet and took a deep breath.
Then she saw Su Yurou.
Her stepsister, in a crimson-red gown, stood at the other end of the red carpet, staring fixedly at her. Su Yurou's face was thick with makeup, but it couldn't hide the dark circles under her eyes; she looked haggard and strung tight.
Su Qingyuan looked at Su Yurou and let the corners of her mouth lift slightly.
Then she shifted her gaze away and slipped her arm through Lu Shiyan's.
The two of them walked up the red carpet together, and the flashbulbs grew even more frenzied.
Su Yurou stood where she was, her fingers curling into fists.
Her nails dug deep into her palms, hurting so much her whole body shook.
But she didn't leave.
She wouldn't leave.
She was going to watch Su Qingyuan—and then make Su Qingyuan lose.
The banquet lights were as bright as daylight.
The instant Su Qingyuan walked into the hall, a great many eyes turned to her. Some recognized her as the creator of "Fracture and Rebirth," some recognized her as Lu Shiyan's companion, and still others murmured about the grudges between her and Su Yurou.
Su Qingyuan was unmoved.
Holding a glass of champagne, she stood in a corner of the hall and quietly took in the whole room.
"Nervous?" Lu Shiyan stood beside her and asked under his breath.
"Not nervous." Su Qingyuan took a sip of champagne. "I'm just wondering when Su Yurou is going to make her move."
The words had barely left her mouth when Su Yurou appeared.
She emerged from the crowd and walked straight toward Su Qingyuan. Her high heels clicked sharply against the marble floor, every step carrying a near-obsessive resolve.
Su Yurou stopped in front of Su Qingyuan.
"Sister," she said, her voice soft and sweet as if dipped in honey, but the hatred at the bottom of her eyes too thick to dissolve.
Su Qingyuan looked at her and said nothing.
"Sister, I came today to apologize to you." Su Yurou raised her voice, loud enough for the people around them to hear. "What happened before was my fault, it was Mom's fault, it was me wanting so badly to beat you… I know I was wrong. Can you forgive me?"
Her eyes reddened, tears welling and swirling, looking pitiful and helpless.
People around them began to whisper.
"This younger sister is so pitiable…"
"Yeah, the older one looks so cold…"
Su Qingyuan watched Su Yurou's performance, and the corner of her mouth curved slightly.
She waited until Su Yurou had finished, then spoke, unhurried. "Su Yurou, you say you were wrong. So tell me—what exactly were you wrong about?"
Su Yurou faltered.
"I… I shouldn't have stolen your work…"
"And?"
"I shouldn't have… shouldn't have reported you for plagiarism…"
"And?"
Su Yurou's expression began to stiffen.
"I shouldn't have… shouldn't have let Mom throw you out of the house…"
Su Qingyuan nodded.
"Good. You've admitted to all of that. So how do you intend to make it right?"
Su Yurou opened her mouth, but not a single word would come out.
She had thought that all she had to do was apologize and Su Qingyuan would forgive her. She had thought that under the gaze of the entire room, Su Qingyuan wouldn't dare withhold face from her.
But she was wrong.
Su Qingyuan lifted her champagne glass, gave it a gentle swirl, her gaze as calm as if she were looking at a stranger.
"Su Yurou, listen carefully. I don't accept your apology. Not because I'm not magnanimous enough, but because your apology isn't sincere. You only want to use your tears to force me into forgiving you, so that you can keep using me, keep stepping on me to climb higher."
Su Qingyuan's voice was not loud, but every word came out crisp and clear.
"In the past I yielded to you because I thought we were family. But you and your mother told me through your actions—you never once treated me as family. And if we aren't family, then on what grounds should I yield to you?"
The whole room fell silent.
Su Yurou's face flushed a deep red, and the tears finally fell for real—but this time not from grievance. From hatred.
"Su Qingyuan! Who do you think you are? You think winning a championship makes you something special? You're nothing but a woman riding on a man's coattails!"
Su Qingyuan laughed.
"I'm riding on a man's coattails? Su Yurou, who drew your work for you? Who bought your competition entry for you? Who wrote your report letter for you? You're the one who relies on others more than anyone in the world—what right do you have to say that about me?"
Su Yurou's face went utterly white.
The people around them began to murmur to one another, and the looks they cast at Su Yurou turned from sympathy to contempt.
"So she was the one who wrote the report letter…"
"How could a person be like this…"
"Putting on that pitiful act just now—disgusting."
Su Yurou stood frozen in place, trembling from head to toe.
She wanted to say something, but found that every excuse was pale and powerless in the face of the facts.
At last she stamped her foot, turned, and fled.
Her high heels struck the marble floor in a frantic, panicked rhythm, like a routed soldier.
Su Qingyuan watched her figure vanish out the door, lifted her champagne glass, and took a light sip.
No smugness, no rush of triumph.
Only a faint, dust-settled calm.
"Well done." Lu Shiyan's voice came from beside her.
Su Qingyuan turned her head and looked into his eyes.
"You don't think I went too far?"
"No."
"Why not?"
"Because she deserved it." Lu Shiyan lowered his head, his gaze settling on her eyes. "And besides, you were already very gentle with her. If it had been me, she'd have come out of it a hundred times worse."
Su Qingyuan couldn't help laughing.
"So you're saying I was too gentle?"
"I'm not complaining," Lu Shiyan said. "I'm relieved. Relieved that you didn't turn into someone like her."
Su Qingyuan went still for a moment, then lowered her head and looked at the amber champagne in her glass.
She hadn't turned into someone like Su Yurou.
Not because of any inborn kindness, but because—she had seen the finest person in this world, and so she knew that becoming a better person mattered more than winning.
Halfway through the banquet, Philippe Delort took the stage to give a few words.
He stood at the podium, his gaze sweeping across the room before finally coming to rest on Su Qingyuan.
"Tonight, I would like to introduce all of you to a young Chinese designer," he said. "Her name is Su Qingyuan. Her work, 'Fracture and Rebirth,' is one of the most powerful pieces I have ever seen. This coming March, she will hold a solo exhibition at Milan Design Week. I hope every one of you here will go and see it. Because what you will be seeing is not merely one designer's work—it is the beginning of an era."
The whole room erupted in thunderous applause.
Su Qingyuan stood among the crowd, feeling the gazes converging on her from all directions. Admiration, envy, curiosity—and jealousy, too.
But there was only one gaze she cared about.
She turned to look at Lu Shiyan.
He was looking at her, the faintest, lightest of smiles at the corner of his mouth.
Su Qingyuan smiled too.
The two of their gazes met across the crowd, like two rivers finally converging, never to part again.

========================================

Chapter 7 — The Night of the Champion
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626209.html

After the gala ended, Su Qingyuan returned to her hotel and found more than a dozen unread messages on her phone.

The one at the very top was a video from Wen Ruan. She tapped it open—it was Wen Ruan in her hotel room, dancing wildly in front of the camera: "Qingyuan! That bit where you tore Su Yurou apart at the gala—I've already watched it seventeen times! It feels incredible every single time! I'm going to set it as my ringtone!"

Su Qingyuan smiled helplessly and scrolled down.

There were congratulations from university classmates, collaboration offers from peers in the design world, and job offers from a few headhunters. There was also one from a number she didn't recognize, containing a single line: "Ms. Su, I'm a reporter from Vogue magazine. I'd love to interview you. Please reply if it's convenient."

Su Qingyuan was in no hurry to reply to anyone.

She set down her phone and walked to the window.

Milan at night was beautiful, the ancient city giving off a gentle glow under the moonlight. From far away, the tolling of church bells drifted over, like some kind of ancient blessing.

She thought of what Philippe had said at the gala—"What you are seeing is not merely the work of a designer, but the beginning of an era."

The beginning of an era.

She had never once imagined that she would become the beginning of any "era." She was only a discarded daughter cast out of the Su family, a victim whose work had been stolen by her stepsister, an ordinary person who had endured countless nights in a cheap rented flat.

But now, she stood in the Milan night, holding the invitation to Milan Design Week in her hand, the global grand champion's trophy tucked in her pocket.

Everything was different now.

Her phone buzzed.

A message from Lu Shiyan: "Still up?"

Su Qingyuan replied with two words: "Can't sleep."

"Me neither."

"Why?"

"Thinking about things."

"Thinking about what?"

The reply paused for a few seconds. Then came a voice message.

Su Qingyuan tapped it open, and Lu Shiyan's low voice came out of the phone, carrying a hoarseness peculiar to the dead of night: "Thinking about you."

Su Qingyuan's fingers suddenly tightened.

She stared at those two words—"about you"—for a long time, long enough that the screen dimmed and lit up, lit up and dimmed again.

She wanted to reply with something, but she typed a few words then deleted them, deleted them then typed again, over and over, until in the end she only sent an emoji: a single period.

Lu Shiyan replied with a question mark.

Su Qingyuan didn't explain.

She didn't know how to explain. It wasn't that she didn't want to respond—it was that she wanted to respond too much, thought about it too much, and so didn't know what to say.

Her phone buzzed again.

"Su Qingyuan, open the door."

Her heartbeat suddenly sped up.

She went to the door and looked out through the peephole—the corridor was empty.

"Where are you?" she typed.

"At your door."

Su Qingyuan paused, looked through the peephole again, and still there was no one.

"You're lying to me."

"I'm not lying. I'm at your door."

Su Qingyuan took a deep breath and opened the door.

There was no one outside.

She looked down. On the floor sat a paper bag. Inside was a strawberry cheesecake, and a card.

The card read: "To celebrate your win. Not winning the competition—winning against yourself. —Lu."

Su Qingyuan crouched down, picked up the card, and smiled.

And as she smiled, the tears fell.

This man, staying up in the dead of night, all just to bring her a cake. He didn't knock, didn't ring the bell, only set the cake at her door and then left.

Because he knew she was very tired today and needed to rest.

Because he didn't want to disturb her.

Because he wanted her to know—he had always been there.

Su Qingyuan carried the cake into the room and set it on the table. She didn't eat it; instead she opened her phone and sent Lu Shiyan a message.

"Got the cake. Thank you."

"Did you eat it?"

"No. Can't bear to."

"Why?"

"Because it's the first cake anyone ever bought just for me."

After the message was sent, the other end was silent for a long while.

Long enough that Su Qingyuan thought he had fallen asleep.

Then the phone lit up.

"From now on I'll buy you one every day."

Su Qingyuan stared at those words, her heart as though brushed lightly by a feather—ticklish, soft, aching.

She held the phone, tossing and turning, reading it many times over, then pressed it against her chest and closed her eyes.

That night, she had a very long dream.

In the dream there was no Su family, no Zhao Xiulan, no Su Yurou, none of those memories that had pained her. There was only a boundless, endless sea, and a person standing at its shore.

She couldn't make out that person's face, but she knew who it was.

The next morning, Su Qingyuan was woken by a burst of knocking.

Groggy, she opened the door, and Wen Ruan rushed in like a gust of wind, holding up her phone, so excited her face was flushed red: "Qingyuan! Quick, look! You're in the Italian news!"

Su Qingyuan took the phone. On the screen was an article in Italian, the headline reading: "China's Genius Designer Su Qingyuan: A Flower Grown from the Ruins."

The article devoted a large portion to introducing her work, "Fracture and Rebirth," calling it "one of the most moving architectural designs of this century." At the end the article quoted a line from Philippe Delort: "Su Qingyuan is not China's future—she is the world's future."

Su Qingyuan looked at that line, her fingers trembling slightly.

The world's future.

That praise was too lofty—so lofty that she felt unworthy of it.

[Ding—self-doubt detected in the host. This System rules: the host's self-perception is skewed. Based on current data, the rating index of the host's work in the global design world already exceeds 97% of active designers. The host's future is not a question of "worthy or not," but a question of "how far she can go."]

Su Qingyuan said silently in her heart: "System, you're actually quite pleasant to listen to today."

[This System has always been pleasant to listen to. The host simply usually refuses to listen.]

Su Qingyuan couldn't help but laugh.

Wen Ruan watched her suddenly start laughing, utterly baffled: "What are you laughing at?"

"Nothing. Just thought of something happy."

"What thing?"

Su Qingyuan thought for a moment: "From now on, someone's going to buy me strawberry cake every day."

Wen Ruan froze, then suddenly clapped a hand over her mouth: "Oh my god oh my god oh my god!!! Did Lu Shiyan say that? He said he'd buy you cake every day from now on? Are you two together?!"

"No."

"Then why would he say something like that?"

Su Qingyuan didn't answer, but the corners of her mouth curved up and wouldn't come back down.

Wen Ruan looked at that expression, took a deep breath, and said in the tone of someone who'd been there: "Su Qingyuan, you're done for."

"What do you mean, done for?"

"You've fallen in love with him."

Su Qingyuan's smile froze for an instant.

Then she lowered her head, looked at her own fingers, and said softly: "...I know."

Wen Ruan stood there, stunned.

She had known Su Qingyuan for seven years and had never seen her like this—soft, fragile, no longer wrapping herself up tight and impenetrable.

"Qingyuan," Wen Ruan walked over and hugged her, "you're finally willing to let someone in."

Su Qingyuan buried her face in the crook of Wen Ruan's shoulder and said nothing.

But she nodded.

That afternoon, Su Qingyuan and Lu Shiyan went together to the main exhibition hall of Milan Design Week.

The hall was enormous, covering over twenty thousand square meters, one of the oldest exhibition spaces in Milan. Next March, her solo showcase would be held here, in the prime exhibition slot.

The slot was still empty for now—only one enormous white wall and an expanse of bare floor.

Su Qingyuan stood before that white wall and closed her eyes.

In her mind, images began to surface—not specific works, but an atmosphere, a feeling. Like the riot of color light cast on the ground as it passes through stained glass, like the ripples that rise when wind brushes across water, like the traces time leaves on ancient buildings.

She opened her eyes.

"I need four months," she said.

Lu Shiyan stood behind her, hands in his pockets, his gaze resting on her: "Is that enough?"

"It has to be enough whether it is or not." Su Qingyuan looked at the white wall. "This is the biggest chance of my life. I won't let it slip away."

"It's not a chance," Lu Shiyan said.

Su Qingyuan turned to look at him.

"It's the stage you deserve."

Su Qingyuan's heart gave a sudden leap.

She turned around to face the white wall and took a deep breath.

"Lu Shiyan."

"Mm."

"If I hold my exhibition here next March, will you come?"

"I will."

"Will you be in the front row?"

"I will."

"Will you..."

She stopped, not going on.

Lu Shiyan walked to her side and stood shoulder to shoulder with her, facing the white wall.

"Will I what?"

Su Qingyuan lowered her head and looked at the toes of her shoes.

"Will you... give me an answer after the exhibition is over?"

Lu Shiyan was silent for a few seconds.

"What answer?"

Su Qingyuan took a deep breath, raised her head, and looked into his eyes.

"Why are you so good to me?"

It was very quiet in the hall, only the breathing of the two of them and the faint sounds of distant construction.

Lu Shiyan looked at her, his gaze deep—so deep she couldn't see the bottom of it.

"You really don't know?" he asked.

Su Qingyuan's heart was beating so fast it felt like it would leap out of her chest.

"I want to hear you say it."

Lu Shiyan slowly raised his hand, the pad of his finger lightly brushing across her cheek, tucking a stray strand of hair at her temple behind her ear. His movement was very slow, very gentle, as though touching something precious and fragile, a piece of porcelain.

"Because you're Su Qingyuan."

Those same five words again.

But this time, Su Qingyuan heard more meaning in them.

Not "because you're Su Qingyuan, your work is good," not "because you're Su Qingyuan, you're worth investing in."

But rather—because you are you, so I like you.

Without any conditions attached.

Su Qingyuan's eyes reddened.

"Lu Shiyan."

"Mm."

"Do you like me?"

The hall was so quiet you could hear a heartbeat.

Lu Shiyan looked at her, the corner of his mouth curving slightly.

"I thought I'd already made it pretty obvious."

Su Qingyuan's tears finally fell, but she smiled, and her smile was beautiful.

"Then why didn't you say it sooner?"

"Because I didn't want to put pressure on you." Lu Shiyan's voice was low and gentle. "You'd just won the championship, just gotten your Milan solo show, just broken free of the Su family. Your life is just beginning—I didn't want to tie you down with feelings."

Su Qingyuan shook her head.

"You're not tying me down. You're holding me up."

Lu Shiyan's expression trembled faintly.

Su Qingyuan reached out and grabbed the hem of his clothes—that same little gesture again, tugging it, and then not letting go.

"Lu Shiyan, I want to be with you."

The hall was quiet for a very long time.

Long enough that Su Qingyuan thought he hadn't heard.

Then Lu Shiyan reached out and pulled her into his arms.

His embrace was tight, so tight that Su Qingyuan could feel his heartbeat—very fast, just as fast as her own.

"Su Qingyuan." His voice was a little hoarse.

"Mm."

"I've waited a long time for you to say that."

Su Qingyuan buried her face against his chest and listened to his heartbeat, beat after beat, strong and real.

She closed her eyes, and the corners of her mouth curved up.

From today on, she was no longer alone.

On the flight back home, Wen Ruan kept staring at Su Qingyuan.

Su Qingyuan got goosebumps under her gaze: "What are you doing?"

"You two are together."

Su Qingyuan didn't deny it.

"I knew it!" Wen Ruan nearly jumped out of her seat. "You two were alone in the exhibition hall for a whole hour, and when you came out your eyes were red, his ears were red, and Qin Zhou said his boss has never smiled like that before!"

Su Qingyuan glanced at Lu Shiyan, seated in the row ahead. He was reading documents, the lines of his profile sharp, his expression focused and serious, no different from usual.

But the tips of his ears were indeed red.

Su Qingyuan couldn't help but smile.

"We're together," she said, her voice very soft but her tone very certain.

Wen Ruan threw her arms around her and burst into messy tears: "Qingyuan, you finally have someone to love you... you finally don't have to be alone anymore... boo-hoo-hoo..."

Su Qingyuan's eyes reddened too from Wen Ruan's tears, and she patted her on the back: "Stop crying, your makeup's going to run."

"I don't care! My best friend is in love! I'm happy!"

Hearing the commotion behind him, Qin Zhou in the front row sneaked a glance back. Wen Ruan had cried her makeup off, and Su Qingyuan was smiling as she handed her tissues.

Lu Shiyan, without even lifting his head, turned a page of his document and said flatly: "Qin Zhou, turn around."

Qin Zhou turned back around at once.

But the corner of his mouth curved into a very small arc.

The plane passed through the clouds, and sunlight spilled in through the cabin window, falling onto Su Qingyuan's face.

She leaned back against her seat, gazing out at the boundless sea of clouds, calmer in her heart than she had ever been.

When the plane landed, Su Qingyuan turned on her phone and found that social media had already exploded.

The official Milan Design Week account had posted an announcement: "We warmly welcome Chinese designer Su Qingyuan, who will hold a solo showcase in the prime slot of the main exhibition hall next March. This is the first time this slot has been used by a designer under thirty, and the first time it has been used by a Chinese designer."

The comments section had already gone wild—

"Su Qingyuan! Pride of China!!!"

"Ahhhhh I hereby declare that from today on Su Qingyuan is my one and only goddess!!!"

"Whoever said before that she rose on a man's back—face slapped now, huh? Milan Design Week isn't run by Lu Shiyan, is it?"

"Boo-hoo-hoo I'm crying, Chinese design has finally stood up."

Su Qingyuan looked at these comments, the corners of her mouth curving up.

She didn't reply to a single one; instead she posted a new update.

Just one line.

"I'll be in Milan, waiting for you all to come."

The attached image was a photo of the Duomo, which she'd taken the night before.

After she posted it, Lu Shiyan reshared it in an instant, his caption just one word: "Waiting."

Wen Ruan reshared Lu Shiyan's reshare, with a long string of exclamation marks: "Ahhhhhhh can you two please stop being so sweet!!!"

Qin Zhou reshared Wen Ruan's reshare, captioned: "Shipping couples in the work group chat is prohibited."

Wen Ruan replied underneath: "Then leave the group."

Qin Zhou did not leave the group.

But he saved a screenshot of the exchange, with the note: First time getting roasted by Wen Ruan, a keepsake.

Su Qingyuan looked at all these interactions and laughed out loud.

Her life, from the day she met Lu Shiyan, had turned into a grand, sweeping revelry that everyone took part in.

And she, at last, was no longer the person who hid alone in a corner, drawing.

========================================

Chapter 8 — The Journey Home
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626210.html

On the flight home, Su Qingyuan made a decision.
She was going to truly build "Yanyi Culture" into something real.
When she'd agreed to join Lu Shiyan's company earlier, it had been more out of instinct than anything else—she trusted him, trusted that he would never do her harm. But as for what exactly she should do, and how, she hadn't really thought it through. Over these past few days in Milan, she'd met with Philippe, wandered through the design exhibitions, taken in countless brilliant works of design. It was as if someone had thrown open a window in her mind.
She didn't want to be merely a passive "investee."
She wanted to be a true founder.
By the time the plane touched down at the Capital's international airport, it was already two in the morning, Beijing time. Beyond the cabin window everything was pitch black, only the runway lights flickering in the night.
Su Qingyuan unbuckled her seatbelt and stretched. More than ten hours of flying had left her back and waist stiff, but her mind was unusually clear.
Lu Shiyan turned around from the row in front and glanced at her.
"Qin Zhou has arranged a car. It'll take you back to Yunxi first."
"And you?"
"There's something at the company. I need to swing by first."
Su Qingyuan frowned. "Going to the office at two in the morning?"
Lu Shiyan's expression didn't change at all, but his gaze flickered ever so slightly, as if he were weighing whether to tell her the truth.
"There's a problem with an acquisition. The other side suddenly backed out at the last minute. I need to handle it in person." He said it in a tone as flat as if he were remarking that the weather was nice today.
Su Qingyuan looked into his eyes. There was a faint layer of dark shadow beneath them—he hadn't really slept on the flight either, had been poring over documents the whole time.
"How long has it been since you slept?" she asked.
Lu Shiyan paused. "Not long."
Su Qingyuan didn't press further. She knew that asking would get her nowhere. This man would never admit to her that he was tired, never let his guard down in front of her, never let her worry. But the more he was like this, the more she felt some part of her heart being gripped tight—aching, sore, tender.
Once the plane had come to a full stop, the group disembarked. Wen Ruan walked ahead, yawning, Qin Zhou trailing behind with the luggage, while Lu Shiyan and Su Qingyuan brought up the rear.
The pre-dawn airport was utterly deserted, only the sound of their footsteps echoing through the cavernous arrivals hall.
As they reached the exit, Su Qingyuan suddenly stopped.
"Lu Shiyan."
Lu Shiyan turned around.
Su Qingyuan stepped closer, reached out, and gently straightened the collar of his coat. She'd done this once before—in Milan, with a loose thread on his shirt collar that hadn't really been there. But this time, her hand lingered a little longer, her fingertips trailing lightly along the edge of his collar, as if reluctant to leave.
Lu Shiyan's breath caught.
"Get some rest," Su Qingyuan said, her voice very soft. "Don't make me worry."
Lu Shiyan looked down at her.
The pre-dawn airport lights fell across his face, casting his features like an oil painting. His eyes were very deep, and in them was her reflection, along with some emotion she couldn't quite read.
"All right," he said.
Just two words. But Su Qingyuan heard everything hidden inside them—there was a promise, there was tenderness, there was restraint, there was all the earnestness a twenty-eight-year-old man held for a twenty-three-year-old woman.
Su Qingyuan let go and turned toward the car Qin Zhou had arranged.
Lu Shiyan stood where he was, watching her receding figure. She didn't walk fast, but every step was steady. Her back was held perfectly straight, her hair lifting faintly in the night wind.
She didn't look back.
But just before getting into the car, she paused, turned her face slightly, and gave him a glimpse of her profile.
The light struck her from the side, her silhouette as sharp and clear as a paper-cut.
Then she bent down and got into the car.
The sound of the car door closing echoed once through the empty airport hall, then faded into silence.
Qin Zhou came over and said cautiously, "Mr. Lu, the car's ready."
Lu Shiyan didn't move, still watching the spot where the car had vanished toward the exit.
"Mr. Lu?"
"...Let's go."
Qin Zhou followed behind Lu Shiyan, silently making a note to himself: today the boss had watched Miss Su leave for seven seconds longer than last time.
Back at Yunxi, Su Qingyuan didn't go straight to sleep.
She took a shower, changed into something comfortable, then sat down at her desk and opened her laptop.
The piece she would exhibit at her solo show in Milan wouldn't be a single work, but a whole series. She'd already settled on the theme—"The Rebirth Trilogy."
Part One: Fracture. About pain, about breaking, about the marks left behind by the grinding passage of time.
Part Two: Growth. About healing, about struggle, about the new shoots that push up out of the cracks.
Part Three: Bloom. About hope, about the future, about a brand-new self.
The theme was too vast—so vast that no single work could contain it. So she needed three, or even more—a complete series, each piece answering the others, building layer upon layer, like the three movements of a symphony.
In the document she typed the first line: "A fracture is not an ending. It is a beginning."
Then she stared at that line for a long time.
Her phone buzzed. A message from Lu Shiyan: "Home yet?"
"Yes. And you? At the office?"
"Mm."
"Have you eaten?"
"Yes."
Su Qingyuan looked at that "Yes" and knew full well he was most likely lying to her. Three in the morning—where would he get food? But she didn't call him out on it. She knew this man had his own rhythm and his own limits; she didn't need to keep an eye on him every second.
"Get back to it, then. I'll draw for a while and then sleep."
"Don't stay up too late."
"You too."
The conversation ended there. Brief, plain, without a single sweet word. But to Su Qingyuan, this very plainness was its own kind of sweetness. As if some unspoken understanding already existed between them—neither of them needed to say much to know what the other was thinking.
She switched off her phone and turned back to the computer screen.
Her fingers tapped at the keyboard, ideas welling up like spring water.
She wrote for two full hours, from three in the morning until five, laying out the complete framework of "The Rebirth Trilogy." The core concept, the form of expression, the choice of materials, the spatial layout of every single piece—all of it now had a clear outline.
When she typed the last word, she leaned back in her chair and let out a long breath.
【Ding—Main quest updated: The Rebirth Trilogy.
Stage One: Complete the overall framework design. Progress: 100%.
Quest reward: Intelligence +2, new skill unlocked: Advanced Project Management.
Stage Two: Complete the first draft of the first work, "Fracture." Time limit: 30 days. Quest reward: Appearance +3, new skill unlocked: Advanced Materials Science.】
Su Qingyuan looked at the quest panel, the corner of her mouth curving up slightly.
Thirty days to finish the first work.
The timeline was tight, but she loved this feeling of being pushed forward by deadlines. For as long as she could remember, her best work had always been done under pressure. Not because she enjoyed pressure, but because pressure left her no time to hesitate, no time to doubt herself, no time to revise over and over. She could only trust her first instinct—and that instinct was usually the best.
She shut down the computer, went back to her bedroom, and lay down on the bed.
Before closing her eyes, she glanced at her phone. Lu Shiyan hadn't sent any new messages, but she noticed his WeChat status had changed to "On a business trip."
A business trip. Three in the morning—not the office, but a business trip.
Su Qingyuan's finger hovered above the screen for a moment, then she typed out a line: "Stay safe. Let me know when you get there."
After sending it, she set the phone down beside her pillow and closed her eyes.
Just before drifting off, she heard the system give a soft little chime.
【Host's heartbeat value: 85→89. Note: Only 6 points away from the "Deep Love" threshold. This system recommends that the Host—】
In her mind, Su Qingyuan said silently, "Recommend that I go to sleep."
【...Understood. Good night, Host.】
The next morning, Su Qingyuan was woken by a call from Qin Zhou.
"Miss Su, Mr. Lu asked me to pass along that he's gone to Shanghai to handle the acquisition. It'll take about three days. I'll be in charge of everything here at Yunxi—if you need anything at all, just reach out to me anytime."
Su Qingyuan rubbed her eyes, her voice still a little hoarse. "Has he arrived?"
"He got in at five this morning. He's already resting at the hotel."
Su Qingyuan glanced at the time—ten in the morning. He'd slept less than five hours.
"Has he had breakfast?"
Qin Zhou was silent for a second.
"Mr. Lu says he isn't hungry."
Su Qingyuan drew in a deep breath.
"Qin Zhou, do something for me."
"Go ahead."
"Find a reliable restaurant near his hotel and order a light breakfast—congee, some small side dishes, eggs. Nothing greasy, nothing spicy. Have them deliver it to his room before eleven. Don't tell him I ordered it."
Qin Zhou was silent for another second, then his voice carried a barely perceptible trace of a smile. "Of course, Miss Su."
After hanging up, Su Qingyuan got up, washed, changed her clothes, and went to the study.
She was about to start drawing "Fracture."
It was the first piece of "The Rebirth Trilogy," and also the hardest. Because what it depicted wasn't something beautiful or polished—it was pain itself. She needed to take all the grievance, rage, loneliness, and despair of those twenty-three years and transform every bit of it into line and color, lay every bit of it bare on the page.
This wasn't merely a matter of technique—it was a matter of the psyche.
She had to tear those wounds open all over again.
Su Qingyuan picked up her pencil and closed her eyes.
Into her mind rose the cluttered attic of the Su household. At eight years old, her favorite thing had been to hide up there and draw. The attic's skylight was tiny, and sunlight poured in through that little opening, casting a square patch of light on the floor. Dust danced in the column of light, as if it were alive.
At twelve, Zhao Xiulan told her that drawing was "a waste of money" and threw all her pencils into the trash. She crouched beside the bin and picked them back out one by one. Some were already broken; she wrapped them in tape and kept using them.
At fifteen, Su Yurou took a work she'd spent a month on, submitted it to the school art exhibition, and won first place. When she went to explain the situation to the teacher, the teacher said, "Your sister draws quite well too. Just let her have this one."
At eighteen, her university acceptance letter "got lost," and Su Yurou went to Beijing and attended the school she'd wanted to go to.
At twenty-two, Lin Haoyu cheated on her and got together with her stepsister.
At twenty-three, Su Yurou stole her work and won the gold medal.
Scene after scene, as if someone were playing a film inside her memory.
Su Qingyuan opened her eyes, and her pencil fell to the paper.
Scratch, scratch, scratch—
The lines flowed out from her fingertips, sharper and more violent than ever before. All the emotions she usually hid so well now took shape in the strokes beneath her hand. Not graceful, composed lines, but twisted, broken lines, lines that looked as if they were struggling.
She drew for an entire day.
From ten in the morning until nine at night, with only two glasses of water in between and a single bowl of congee Qin Zhou had sent over. Her eyes were fixed on the page, her hand moving at lightning speed, her whole body as if possessed by something.
At nine that night, she finally set down her pencil.
On the paper was an abstract architectural sketch—a building growing up out of a fracture. Not out of ruins, but out of a crack. And those cracks weren't external, they were internal. As if the building itself had come alive, had wounds, and those wounds were bleeding.
Su Qingyuan looked at the drawing, and suddenly felt a sharp pain in her chest.
Not a physical pain.
It was that old pain from long ago, the one she'd pressed down into the deepest part of her heart, the one she'd thought had healed—suddenly surging back up, drowning her like a rising tide.
Her tears slid down soundlessly.
One drop, two drops, three drops.
She wiped at them with the back of her hand, but couldn't wipe them all away. The tears were like a broken dam—she couldn't stop them no matter what.
Her phone buzzed.
She picked it up to look. It was a message from Lu Shiyan.
"Did you order the breakfast?"
Su Qingyuan sniffled and replied with a single word: "Mm."
The other side's reply paused for a few seconds.
Then came a video call request.
Su Qingyuan looked at the green answer button on the screen and hesitated. The state she was in right now—red eyes, red nose, the not-yet-dry tear tracks still on her face—she didn't want him to see her like this.
But she pressed answer anyway.
The screen lit up. Lu Shiyan's face appeared, the background a business suite at the hotel. He sat at a desk, his shirt collar slightly open, his sleeves rolled up to his forearms.
He glanced at her, and his expression changed at once.
"What's wrong?" His voice was low and urgent.
"Nothing," Su Qingyuan said with a small smile. "I got too absorbed in the drawing. Just a bit emotional."
Lu Shiyan stared into her eyes for several seconds.
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm?"
"You're crying."
Su Qingyuan's smile froze.
This man—he could always see right through her.
"While I was drawing 'Fracture,' I remembered some things from the past," she admitted honestly. "It's all right. Crying it out actually helps. I'd been holding it all in, and that was why I couldn't draw it."
Lu Shiyan was silent for a while.
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm."
"I'm not by your side. Take good care of yourself."
Su Qingyuan's nose stung again.
This man, in Shanghai, more than a thousand kilometers away, across a screen, hadn't said "don't cry," hadn't said "don't be sad," but "take good care of yourself." Because he knew there were past things he couldn't bear in her place, wounds she had to face on her own.
But he wanted her to know—he cared.
"I will," Su Qingyuan said. "You too. Don't push yourself too hard."
Lu Shiyan looked at the screen, the corner of his mouth curving slightly.
"All right."
The two of them looked at each other across the screen for a few seconds, neither of them speaking. That silence wasn't awkward—it was a very deep, very quiet kind of companionship.
"Go and rest," Lu Shiyan said first. "You've been drawing all day."
"How do you know?"
"Qin Zhou told me."
Su Qingyuan couldn't help laughing. "Is Qin Zhou your man or mine?"
Lu Shiyan thought about it. "Yours."
Su Qingyuan's heart skipped a beat.
That answer had come too fast. Faster than she'd been ready for.
"Good night," she said first.
"Good night."
The video call ended.
Su Qingyuan looked at the words "Call duration 4 min 32 sec" on the screen, pressed the phone against her chest, and closed her eyes.
Three days later, Lu Shiyan came back from Shanghai.
By the time he reached Yunxi, it was already eight in the evening. Su Qingyuan was in the study, working on the second version of the "Fracture" sketch. When the doorbell rang, she assumed it was Qin Zhou delivering dinner and ran over to open the door.
The door opened, and Lu Shiyan stood in the doorway.
He wore a black cashmere coat, a paper bag in his hand—strawberry cake again.
His hair was a little windblown and disheveled, the shadows under his eyes even darker than three days ago, but his eyes were bright, and the moment he saw her, those eyes seemed to ignite.
"You're back," Su Qingyuan said.
"Mm."
"Have you eaten?"
"No."
Su Qingyuan stepped aside to let him in. "I made congee. There's some left. Wait a moment, I'll heat it up."
As Lu Shiyan changed his shoes, his gaze swept across the whole room—the study lights were on, sketches scattered all over the floor, a half-eaten bowl of congee and a cup of gone-cold tea on the dining table. Compared to when he'd left three days ago, the place now had a certain air of being earnestly lived in.
Not tidy—alive.
In the kitchen, Su Qingyuan heated the congee, pots and pans clinking and clattering. Lu Shiyan leaned against the kitchen doorframe, watching her busy figure from behind.
She was wearing a white loungewear set, her hair carelessly tied at the back of her head, her apron knotted crookedly, like a schoolkid.
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm." She didn't even turn around.
"Three days, and you've gotten thinner."
Su Qingyuan's hand paused.
"So have you," she said, her voice a little smaller. "You've barely slept, haven't you?"
Lu Shiyan didn't answer.
The congee was heated. Su Qingyuan brought it to the dining table, then stir-fried a light dish of seasonal vegetables and fried a poached egg. Lu Shiyan sat at the table, watching her bring out the food dish by dish, as if he were watching a performance.
"Eat," she said, handing him the chopsticks.
Lu Shiyan took the chopsticks and lowered his head to eat.
He didn't eat fast, but every bite was deliberate, as if he were savoring something precious. Su Qingyuan sat across from him, chin propped in her hands, watching him eat, the corners of her mouth curved.
"You're not eating?" he asked.
"I already ate. This is what I saved for you."
Lu Shiyan lifted his head and glanced at her. In that glance was something very complicated—there was emotion, there was tenderness mixed with ache, there was some soft feeling he wasn't quite willing to admit to.
He lowered his head and kept eating.
After the meal, Lu Shiyan went to wash the dishes. Su Qingyuan leaned against the kitchen doorframe and watched him, just as she had three days ago before she left for Milan.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Did the acquisition get sorted out?"
"It did."
"Did it go smoothly?"
"No. But it's resolved."
Su Qingyuan didn't press further. She knew there was nothing she could do to help with his work, but there was one thing she could do—make sure that while he was here, he was relaxed, comfortable, free of all those troubling matters.
"When you're done washing up, come take a look at my new drawings," she said.
Lu Shiyan set the last bowl in the drying rack, dried his hands, and followed her into the study.
Twenty-odd sketches were scattered across the study floor, all of them studies for "Fracture." Lu Shiyan crouched down and looked at them one by one. He wasn't just glancing—he was truly looking, lingering over each one for a long time, as if reading every detail within the drawing.
Su Qingyuan stood behind him, so nervous her palms were sweating.
Even though they were already that kind of close, even though he knew what she was capable of, every time she showed him new work she still got nervous.
Lu Shiyan finished looking at the last one, stood up, turned around, and looked at her.
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm."
"In these three days, you've drawn what would take someone else three months."
Su Qingyuan was taken aback.
"And what's more," Lu Shiyan's gaze fell on the sketches, his voice low and earnest, "this isn't a question of technique anymore. It's a question of the heart. You've carved your own heart out and put it on the page."
Su Qingyuan's eyes reddened.
"Does it hurt?" Lu Shiyan asked.
Not "is it good," not "do you feel confident," but "does it hurt?"
Su Qingyuan's tears fell.
"It hurts," she said.
Lu Shiyan reached out and pulled her into his arms.
His embrace was warm, carrying the longing of three days apart, and a very deep, unspoken ache.
Su Qingyuan buried her face against his chest, listening to the beat of his heart, steady and strong, one beat after another.
"It'll be all right," Lu Shiyan's voice came from above her head, low and gentle. "These fractures will become your finest work."
Su Qingyuan closed her eyes, and her tears slid down soundlessly.
But the corners of her mouth were curved.
Because she knew he was right.
Three days later, Su Qingyuan received a call from Su Guoliang.
The number was an unfamiliar one she hadn't blocked. She picked up, and what she heard was Su Guoliang's weary, aged voice.
"Qingyuan, your mother's been hospitalized."
Su Qingyuan gripped the phone, saying nothing.
"Her high blood pressure flared up. The doctor says it's serious. Could you... could you come and see her?"
Su Qingyuan was silent for a long time.
"Su Guoliang."
"Mm?"
"Do you remember? The year I was eighteen, I ran a high fever, forty degrees, and you and your wife took Su Yurou off on a trip. I was home alone, burning up for three days, and in the end I crawled to the hospital by myself."
The line went silent.
"You didn't make a single phone call to me back then," Su Qingyuan said, her voice perfectly calm—so calm it held not a trace of warmth. "Now your wife is in the hospital, and you want me to go see her?"
Su Guoliang's voice trembled a little. "Qingyuan, she is your mother, after all..."
"She is not my mother," Su Qingyuan cut him off. "My mother died when I was three. That woman you married was never my mother."
A stifled sob came through the line.
Su Qingyuan didn't soften.
"Su Guoliang, I won't come to see her, and I won't come to see you either. From this day on, your affairs have nothing to do with me."
She hung up the phone and blocked that number too.
Then she sat at her desk, looking out at the Capital's gray, overcast sky, and lost herself in a daze for a while.
Her phone buzzed. A message from Lu Shiyan.
"What's wrong?"
Su Qingyuan was startled. How did he know? She glanced at the study doorway—no one there. Then she glanced out the window—the Maybach was parked down below, Lu Shiyan leaning against it, looking up at her window.
She hadn't told him, and he'd come again.
Su Qingyuan walked to the window and, across the dozens of meters between them, looked down at the man standing below, his face tilted up toward her.
She picked up her phone and typed a line: "Su Guoliang called. Said Zhao Xiulan was hospitalized and wanted me to go see her. I refused."
Lu Shiyan lowered his head to glance at his phone, then lifted it, his gaze crossing the dozens of meters to land on her.
"Well done," he replied.
Su Qingyuan looked at those two words and smiled.
Not a bitter smile, not a helpless smile, but a smile of release.
Because she knew that in this world, there was at least one person who would always stand on her side.
