Chapter 9 — The First Crack Blooms
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626211.html

The First Crack Blooms
The first draft of "Cracks" was finished on a rainy night.
When Su Qingyuan set down her brush, the first rain since the start of winter was falling outside her window. The fine, dense threads of it tapped against the floor-to-ceiling glass with a soft rustling, like someone sighing gently in some faraway place.
She stepped back a few paces and looked at the painting before her.
On the paper, a building grew out of the darkness. It was not whole—its walls were riven by countless cracks, as if something had torn it apart from within. But within the cracks there was no emptiness; there was light. The light seeped out from the fissures, fine and faint, like sparks that refused to go out. The base of the building was old, weathered brick on the verge of collapse, but the higher it rose, the fewer the cracks and the more the light, until at its summit the entire structure looked as though it had been cast anew out of light—transparent, weightless, almost ready to take flight.
This was "Cracks."
Not a complaint, not a play for pity, not a wound torn open for others to gawk at.
It was telling you—no matter how deep the crack, light can still shine through.
【Ding—Main quest "Rebirth Trilogy," Stage Two complete. Work "Cracks" first-draft assessment: SSS-rank. Quest reward: Beauty +3, new skill unlocked: Advanced Materials Science. Current composite scores: Beauty 97, Intelligence 101, Talent 92, Business 23, Medicine 0, Combat 12. Composite rating: A-.】
Su Qingyuan didn't look at those numbers. She looked at her painting, and her eyes stung faintly.
This time it wasn't from grievance. It was from pride.
Pride in herself.
Her phone buzzed. A message from Lu Shiyan: "Done with the painting?"
Su Qingyuan glanced out the window—there was no Maybach downstairs. He wasn't here tonight.
"How did you know?" she replied.
"A feeling."
Su Qingyuan stared at those two words for several seconds, and the corners of her mouth curved up. This man—now he was even using words like "feeling." The old Lu Shiyan's dictionary had probably held only cold, clinical terms like "data," "analysis," "results."
"It's done," she typed. "The first draft. I start refining it tomorrow."
"I want to see it."
"I'll show you tomorrow. It's too late tonight—get some rest."
His reply paused for a few seconds.
"I'm downstairs at Yunxi."
Su Qingyuan froze, then hurried to the window and looked down—the street below was empty. No car, no one.
"You're lying to me," she typed.
"I'm not lying. I'm in the basement garage, level B1."
Su Qingyuan drew in a deep breath.
This man wasn't sleeping in the middle of the night—he'd driven over to the garage beneath her building, just to look at her painting?
She picked up her phone and walked out the door still in her slippers. The elevator descended all the way down, and when it reached B1 the doors opened onto the dim light of the garage, the air thick with the faint smell of gasoline.
Lu Shiyan was leaning against his car, wearing a thin charcoal-gray sweater, phone in hand, the blue glow of the screen reflected on his face. Hearing the elevator doors open, he raised his head.
Their eyes met.
"Come up," Su Qingyuan said.
Lu Shiyan put away his phone and walked over.
The two of them rode the elevator back up to the top floor together. Su Qingyuan opened the door, Lu Shiyan changed his shoes and went straight to the study. He stopped before the drafts, crouched down, and studied them one by one.
Su Qingyuan stood behind him, her heart racing. She'd shown him her work many times before, but every time, she still grew nervous. Because every piece was different, every one a sliver of her life from some particular stage.
Lu Shiyan looked for a long time.
So long that Su Qingyuan felt she was about to suffocate.
At last he stood, turned around, and looked at her.
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm."
"Do you know how much this painting would sell for at auction?"
Su Qingyuan was taken aback. She'd never once considered the question.
"No."
"Ten million. U.S. dollars."
Su Qingyuan's heart gave a violent jolt. Not because of the money—though ten million dollars truly was a great deal—but because of how calmly he said the figure, so calm it was as if he were saying, "It rained today."
"You're flattering me again," she said.
Lu Shiyan frowned slightly, his expression too serious to be joking. "I'm not flattering you. At Christie's last year, a contemporary artwork of the same caliber as this painting sold for twelve million dollars. Yours has more power than that one."
Su Qingyuan opened her mouth and didn't know what to say.
Lu Shiyan walked back to the drafts and lowered his head to look at the most fully realized rendering.
"But this painting can't be sold."
"Why not?"
"Because it belongs to the whole world." He turned his head to look at her. "You painted this not to hang in someone's living room. You painted it so that everyone who feels they have cracks of their own can see—cracks aren't something to fear. A crack is where the light gets in."
Su Qingyuan's tears fell again.
This man could always say, in the calmest tone, the very words most likely to make her cry.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Can you stop always saying things like that?"
"Things like what?"
"Things that make me want to cry."
Lu Shiyan looked at her red-rimmed eyes and her stubbornly pressed lips, and the corner of his mouth curved.
"All right. From now on I'll say things that make you laugh."
"What kind of thing could make me laugh?"
Lu Shiyan thought for a moment.
"Qin Zhou confessed to Wen Ruan today."
Su Qingyuan froze, tears still on her face, but the corners of her mouth had already started lifting beyond her control. "What?!"
"Wen Ruan was being harassed by an actor on set. Qin Zhou went over, picked the guy up, and threw him out." Lu Shiyan's tone was as flat as if he were reading a news bulletin. "Wen Ruan asked him, 'Do you like me?' He said, 'Yes.' Wen Ruan said, 'Then take me to dinner.' He said, 'Okay.' They should be out for a late-night meal right now."
Su Qingyuan couldn't help laughing, laughing until she doubled over.
She pictured Qin Zhou's eternally deadpan face and tried to imagine his expression when he said "Yes." She pictured Wen Ruan's startled look. She pictured the two of them sitting at a late-night food stall, Qin Zhou eating skewers without batting an eye while Wen Ruan chattered away beside him.
"When did they get together?" she asked, still laughing.
"About three hours ago."
"How do you know?"
"Qin Zhou sent me a message: 'President Lu, I'm taking the night off.' I asked why, and he said: 'Personal matter.'" Lu Shiyan paused. "He's been with me five years. It's the first time he's ever taken leave for a personal matter."
Su Qingyuan laughed even harder.
She wiped her eyes—this time tears from laughing—pulled out her phone, and sent Wen Ruan a message: "I hear someone confessed to you?"
Wen Ruan replied instantly: "AAAAAAAH how did you know!!!"
Su Qingyuan showed the phone to Lu Shiyan. He glanced at it, the corner of his mouth twitched, but he said nothing.
Wen Ruan's messages kept bombarding in: "Qin Zhou never says anything normally, and when he finally does it's just 'Yes'!!! He answered with one single word!!! But he's so handsome, what do I do, Qingyuan, I'm done for, I've fallen!!!"
Su Qingyuan replied, laughing: "Didn't you always want someone who says little but gets things done?"
Wen Ruan: "But he says WAY too little!!! We've been sitting here eating for half an hour and he's said exactly three things: 'What do you want to eat,' 'Okay,' and 'I'll take you home.'"
Su Qingyuan: "Isn't that great? Concise and to the point."
Wen Ruan: "But I want to hear him say other stuff!! Like 'You look so pretty'!!! He won't even look at me!!!"
Su Qingyuan turned to Lu Shiyan. "When Qin Zhou's chasing a girl, does he never look at her?"
Lu Shiyan considered. "He looked. Twenty-seven times. I counted."
Su Qingyuan: "……"
This man—he'd even count how many times his assistant glanced at someone.
She relayed Lu Shiyan's words to Wen Ruan. Wen Ruan sent a long string of exclamation marks, then said: "He looked at me and I didn't even notice!!!"
Su Qingyuan: "Because you were looking at him too."
Wen Ruan went silent for five seconds, then sent a "shut up" sticker.
Laughing, Su Qingyuan set down her phone and looked at Lu Shiyan. He was studying her drafts, the profile of his face especially gentle in the light of the desk lamp.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Thank you."
Lu Shiyan turned his head to look at her.
"For what?"
"For letting Qin Zhou go after Wen Ruan."
Lu Shiyan raised an eyebrow slightly. "I didn't make him go after her. He went on his own."
"Then how many hints did you give him?"
Lu Shiyan was silent for a second.
"……Three."
Su Qingyuan laughed.
This man—he even managed his assistant's love life. But his way of managing it was peculiar—not orders, not arrangements, but creating opportunities and then letting everything happen naturally.
Just like what he did with her.
"Come here," Su Qingyuan said.
Lu Shiyan walked over and stopped in front of her.
Su Qingyuan rose on her tiptoes, reached out, and lightly brushed his hair. His hair was very soft, not what she'd imagined. She'd thought a man as cold and hard as him would have hair just as hard, but it actually felt like the down of some small animal.
Lu Shiyan's body stiffened slightly.
"Your hair is so soft," Su Qingyuan said.
Lu Shiyan didn't answer, but the tips of his ears turned red.
Su Qingyuan drew her hand back, her eyes curving with her smile. "All right, you can head home now. It's very late."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, his gaze deep.
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm?"
"You just touched my head."
"Mm, what about it?"
"Do you know what it means to touch a man's head?"
Su Qingyuan's heart suddenly raced, but she didn't shrink back. Instead she tilted her face up, looked into his eyes, and said with a smile, "It means I wanted to touch it."
Lu Shiyan's throat bobbed.
He reached out and gently pinched her earlobe. The pad of his finger was cool, but the instant it touched her earlobe it was as if he'd been scalded, and he pulled it back.
"Now we're even," he said.
Su Qingyuan's ears turned red enough to bleed.
The two of them stood facing each other in the entryway, both with red ears, neither looking at the other.
"Goodnight," Lu Shiyan said first.
"Goodnight."
Lu Shiyan pulled the door open and walked out. The instant the door closed, Su Qingyuan leaned against it and slowly slid down to sit on the floor, burying her face in her knees.
Her ears were still burning.
She reached up and touched her own earlobe—it seemed to still hold the warmth of his fingertip.
【Ding—Host's heartbeat value: 89→92. Note: only 3 points from the "Deep Love" threshold. This system suggests—】
"Shut up."
【Understood. Sweet dreams to the host.】
Su Qingyuan sat on the floor for quite a while before she stood and walked back to the study.
She carefully put away the "Cracks" drafts and slid them into a drawing tube. Then she opened her laptop and began writing the first business plan for Yanyi Culture.
If she was going to start a company, it couldn't be just a name on paper. She would have her own team, her own projects, her own brand. She didn't want to live forever beneath Lu Shiyan's wing—warm as that was, what she wanted more was to stand shoulder to shoulder with him.
She wrote the plan until three in the morning.
She wrote out the company's vision, its scope of business, its organizational structure, its three-year development roadmap. She didn't go into too much detail, since many things could only be settled once the company was actually up and running. But she made one thing crystal clear—Yanyi Culture's core competitiveness wasn't "Lu Shiyan's investment," it was "Su Qingyuan's design."
She wanted everyone to know that this company would survive and grow not because someone powerful was backing it, but because her work was good enough.
After writing the last word, she saved the document and shut down the laptop.
Outside the window, the night over the Capital was deep. In the distance, a few scattered lights still glowed in the office towers, like the eyes of people who couldn't sleep.
Lying in bed, before she closed her eyes, Su Qingyuan sent Lu Shiyan a message: "I finished the business plan."
To her surprise he was still awake, and replied instantly: "What business plan?"
"Yanyi Culture's business plan."
His reply paused for a few seconds.
"Send it to me."
Su Qingyuan sent over the document.
A few more minutes passed, and Lu Shiyan sent a message: "Su Qingyuan, you don't need to write this."
Su Qingyuan's heart sank.
"Why not?"
"Because at Yanyi Culture, you have the final say in everything. You can do whatever you want, however you want, no business plan required."
Su Qingyuan stared at that line, a tangle of emotions welling up inside her. There was the warmth of being moved, of being trusted, but also a little stubbornness.
"But I want to prove to you that I don't have to rely on you."
Lu Shiyan's reply came quickly.
"You never need to prove anything to me. You only need to be yourself. When you're being yourself, you're already the very best there is."
Su Qingyuan pressed the phone to her chest and closed her eyes.
This man really did know how to make her heart go soft.
She rolled over, buried her face in the pillow, and muttered something only she could hear: "Lu Shiyan, you're really such a nuisance."
But she was smiling.
Smiling so hard her smile pressed a little hollow into the pillow.
The next morning, Su Qingyuan got a video call from Philippe Delort.
The old man sat in his study in Milan, a whole wall of design sketches behind him. Today he wore a red sweater, looking full of spirit, his eyes bright as two stars.
"Su, how far along is your 'Cracks'?" he came straight to the point.
Su Qingyuan aimed the camera at the drafts and showed them to him one by one.
Philippe watched intently, asking many questions with each one: "Why this material here?" "Why does the line run in this direction here?" "How did you handle this effect of light?"
Su Qingyuan answered each in turn.
After Philippe had heard her out, he leaned back in his chair and let out a long breath.
"Su."
"Mr. Delort."
"You don't need me anymore."
Su Qingyuan was taken aback.
"Your work has already gone beyond the scope of what I can teach." There was no regret in Philippe's voice, only pride. "What you need now isn't a teacher, it's a stage. And you already have one—Milan Design Week. Su, you've graduated."
Su Qingyuan's eyes reddened.
"Mr. Delort, you'll always be my teacher."
Philippe laughed, laughing like a child.
"All right. Then I'll wait for you to come to Milan. When you do, I'll sit in the front row to see your exhibition."
"You'll definitely be in the front row."
After the video call ended, Su Qingyuan sat at her desk, gazing out the window, lost in thought for a long while.
She suddenly realized something—from the moment she met Lu Shiyan until now, in less than two months, her life had been turned completely upside down.
Two months ago, she was still living in a thirty-square-meter rented room, eating milk five days past its expiration date and wilted cucumbers, with only three thousand yuan left in her bank account.
Two months later, she lived in the most expensive apartment in the Capital, with two million yuan in her bank account—the first advance payment on the "Listening to the Sea" project, which Lu Shiyan had insisted on paying early—and when she couldn't refuse, she'd accepted it.
Two million.
She'd never seen so much money in her life.
But she hadn't spent it recklessly. She saved most of it, taking out only a small portion to buy herself new design tools and a few decent pieces of clothing. She wasn't the kind of person to let money go to her head—her experiences with the Su family had taught her that money mattered, but money wasn't everything. What truly mattered was ability, was the work, was the things no one could ever take from her.
Her phone buzzed. A message from Qin Zhou.
"Miss Su, all of Yanyi Culture's registration procedures are now complete. The business license, the company seal, the bank account—everything is ready. The company is located in the CWTC Tower in the CBD, an entire floor. Mr. Lu says the décor style is yours to decide."
Su Qingyuan looked at the message and took a deep breath.
The company—it was really up and running.
Not a shell company under Lu Shiyan's name, but a company truly her own, one where she had the final say.
She sent Lu Shiyan a message: "Thank you."
Lu Shiyan replied: "It's not thanks. It's investment."
Su Qingyuan laughed. This man—he always had to dress up something emotional as something rational. But she knew that wasn't how he really felt inside.
"Then I'll do it well. I can't let you lose money," she replied.
"You won't let me lose money."
"You believe in me that much?"
"It's not belief. It's knowing."
Su Qingyuan stared at the word "knowing" for a long time.
Knowing. Not believing. Belief could be wrong; knowing was certain. When Lu Shiyan said "knowing," it meant that in his eyes, her success wasn't a matter of probability—it was a matter of inevitability.
This man believed in her more than she believed in herself.
That afternoon, Su Qingyuan went to the CWTC Tower.
Yanyi Culture's office was on the forty-seventh floor, the entire floor wrapped in floor-to-ceiling glass curtain walls, looking out over the whole CBD. Standing at the window, Su Qingyuan felt as if she were standing on the very heart of the Capital.
Qin Zhou had come with her, standing behind her, waiting quietly.
"Qin Zhou." Su Qingyuan didn't turn around.
"Yes."
"You and Wen Ruan… are you really together now?"
Qin Zhou was silent for a second.
"Yes."
"Are you happy?"
Qin Zhou was silent again for a second.
"……Yes."
Su Qingyuan turned her head and looked at Qin Zhou's eternally unchanging poker face. His expression was no different from usual, but she noticed his eyes were a little brighter than usual, and the curve of his mouth a fraction higher—something no one who didn't know him very well would ever catch.
"That's good then." Su Qingyuan smiled. "Wen Ruan is my best friend. If you ever mistreat her, I won't let you off."
Qin Zhou's expression finally shifted a touch—his brow moved slightly, as if he wanted to say something but held it back.
"Miss Su," he said, "I won't mistreat her. I'll treat her the way Mr. Lu treats you."
Su Qingyuan was taken aback, then smiled even wider.
"Qin Zhou, you don't talk much normally, but when you do, you make people want to cry."
Without any change in expression, Qin Zhou took a pack of tissues from his pocket and handed it to her.
Su Qingyuan took the tissues, laughing until she doubled over.
On her way out of the CWTC Tower, Su Qingyuan ran into someone.
Lin Haoyu.
Her ex-ex-boyfriend—no, "ex-boyfriend" no longer fit; he should be called her "cheating ex-boyfriend." The man who had left her when she was at her lowest and gotten together with Su Yurou.
He stood at the entrance of the CWTC Tower in a poorly fitting suit, a bouquet of flowers in his hand, "regret" written all over his face.
The instant Su Qingyuan saw him, her steps didn't pause, didn't even slow.
"Qingyuan!" Lin Haoyu chased after her and blocked her path.
Su Qingyuan stopped and looked at him.
Two months without seeing him, he'd lost a lot of weight, dark circles heavy under his eyes, stubble he hadn't shaved clean on his chin. He was no longer the spirited student council president from their university days; he looked more like a middle-aged man beaten down by life, ragged and wretched.
"What are you here for?" Su Qingyuan's tone was as calm as if she were asking a stranger.
Lin Haoyu held out the flowers. "Qingyuan, I came to apologize. I wronged you before. Getting together with Su Yurou was a mistake. She's not a good person at all—she just used me…"
"And so?" Su Qingyuan cut him off.
Lin Haoyu froze.
"And so, the moment you realized she was using you, you came running back to me?" Su Qingyuan looked into his eyes—no anger, no grievance, not even contempt. "Lin Haoyu, you didn't come to apologize. You came begging to be taken in. Su Yurou threw you away, your career is gone, your reputation stinks, you have nothing left now—so you remembered me."
Lin Haoyu's face went pale, then flushed, by turns.
"Qingyuan, I know I wronged you before, but I really do realize my mistake now…"
"You realize your mistake?" Su Qingyuan tilted her head slightly. "Then tell me—what exactly was your mistake?"
Lin Haoyu opened his mouth. "I shouldn't have cheated…"
"And what else?"
"I shouldn't have… shouldn't have gotten together with Su Yurou…"
"And what else?"
Lin Haoyu couldn't get another word out.
Su Qingyuan looked at him, the corner of her mouth curving slightly—the kind of polite smile that carried no feeling at all.
"Lin Haoyu, your mistakes are too many to count, so let me count them for you. First, you pursued me because I was a daughter of the Su family, and you thought I could help you. Second, the moment you learned Su Yurou had more say in the Su family, you dumped me without a second thought. Third, after you got together with Su Yurou, you talked behind my back, calling me a 'psycho' who 'wouldn't stop hounding you.' Fourth, you came to me today not out of regret, but because Su Yurou is finished and you want to climb your way back to me."
Lin Haoyu's face went completely white.
"Qingyuan, I didn't…"
"You did." Su Qingyuan's voice wasn't loud, but every word drove into his ears like a nail. "Lin Haoyu, why did I fall for you back then? Because you came to pick me up when I worked part-time late into the night, because you gave me a bouquet of flowers on my birthday. Back then I thought you were the best man in the whole world. It was only later that I realized none of it was real. You were just playing the role of a 'good boyfriend,' because you thought playing it well would get you what you wanted."
Su Qingyuan looked at him, her gaze as calm as a mirror, reflecting back every bit of his ugliness.
"Lin Haoyu, I don't hate you. Hating you would require me to care about you. But to me, you stopped being anything a long time ago."
With that, she stepped around him and kept walking.
Qin Zhou followed behind her, and as he passed Lin Haoyu, he paused.
"Mr. Lin," Qin Zhou's voice was very flat, "I'd advise you not to come looking for Miss Su again. Otherwise, even that last little bit of career you have left won't survive."
Lin Haoyu shuddered all over.
Qin Zhou didn't say another word, striding off to catch up with Su Qingyuan.
Su Qingyuan settled into the car, leaned back in her seat, and looked out the window.
Qin Zhou started the engine and glanced at her in the rearview mirror.
"Miss Su, are you all right?"
"I'm fine." Su Qingyuan smiled. "Better than I'd imagined. I thought seeing him would hurt, but it didn't hurt at all. If anything, I felt… relieved."
"Why?"
"Because I could never figure out before why I'd ever liked him. Seeing him today, I finally understood." Su Qingyuan watched the city scenery flying backward outside the window. "It wasn't because he was good. It was because back then I was so starved for love. Anyone who was a little kind to me felt like the whole world. But it's different now."
She didn't finish, but Qin Zhou understood.
It was different now. Because she'd met someone who was truly good to her. Because her eyes had been opened, and she knew now what real goodness looked like.
The car stopped at a red light. Qin Zhou looked at Su Qingyuan in the rearview mirror and, rarely, added one more line: "Miss Su, the way Mr. Lu treats you—it's real."
Su Qingyuan turned her head and looked at Qin Zhou.
"I know," she said, her voice soft but certain.
When she got back to Yunxi, Su Qingyuan found a cardboard box at her door.
She opened it to find a complete set of design tools—from markers to scale rulers, from drawing boards to professional-grade colored pencils, all the best brands on the market. On top of the box sat a card, the handwriting bold and forceful: "Yanyi Culture's first project—start by designing your own desk."
Su Qingyuan pressed the card to her chest and smiled.
She took out her phone and sent Lu Shiyan a message: "Got the tools. Lin Haoyu came to find me today."
He replied instantly: "I know. Qin Zhou told me."
"You're not going to ask how I handled it?"
"No need. I know you'll have handled it well."
Su Qingyuan looked at that line, her heart racing. This man never asked her "Are you okay?", never asked her "Are you all right?", never treated her as someone who needed protecting. He trusted that she could handle everything; he would only appear when she needed him.
"I told him he was nothing to me," Su Qingyuan typed.
"What did he say?"
"He couldn't say a word."
"Naturally. Because what you said was the truth."
Su Qingyuan laughed, and as she laughed her nose began to sting again.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Thank you for letting me know what it really means to like someone."
His reply paused for a long time. So long that Su Qingyuan thought he wouldn't answer at all.
Then the screen lit up.
"Su Qingyuan, the things you've let me know are even more."
"Like what?"
"Like the fact that being alive has meaning."
Su Qingyuan's tears fell.
She held her phone, sitting on the carpet of Yunxi's top floor, the ten thousand lights of the Capital beyond the window, and in her arms a man's heart that he restrained with all his strength and that still overflowed despite him.
She cried for a while, and then she smiled.
Crying and laughing at once, like a fool.
But she didn't care anymore.
Because in this world, at last there was one person who let her never have to pretend again.

Chapter 10 — His Private Domain Holds Traces of Her
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626212.html

His private domain holds traces of her.
The Nancheng financial district.
Here the city's skyline reached its highest point. The headquarters of the Lu Group rose like a drawn sword piercing straight into the clouds, its glass curtain wall reflecting the afternoon sun—dazzling and cold.
The taxi pulled up at the base of the building. Su Qingyuan looked up and drew a deep breath.
She had passed this building countless times before. Each time she would tilt her head back for a single glance, then lower it and hurry past. She had never imagined that one day she would walk inside—much less that she would be invited in.
"Miss, we're here," the driver said.
Su Qingyuan paid the fare and pushed the door open to get out.
She wore the beige skirt suit she'd worn to the salon that day, carrying a black tote bag stuffed with her portfolio materials. Standing before the building, her slender figure looked small against the colossal structure, yet her spine was held perfectly straight.
There was a security booth at the entrance. The guard in his crisply pressed uniform spotted her and was about to step forward to ask her business, when a woman in business attire strode briskly out from the direction of the front desk.
"Excuse me, are you Miss Su Qingyuan?" The woman's smile was perfectly poised.
"I am."
"President Lu gave instructions. This way, please." The woman turned to lead the way, her gestures respectful without being obsequious. "President Lu is on the top floor. I'll take you up."
Su Qingyuan followed her across the spacious, brightly lit ground-floor lobby. Marble beneath her feet, a ten-meter-high crystal chandelier overhead—every detail breathed the grandeur of a top-tier enterprise.
A few young women at the front desk stole glances her way, their eyes brimming with gossip.
"Is that the person President Lu's been waiting for?"
"Oh my god, she's gorgeous, what an aura."
"No wonder President Lu pushed back all his meetings this afternoon…"
The whispers drifted into her ears, but Su Qingyuan's expression never changed, her pace neither hurried nor slow.
The elevator was a private one—it required a keycard before a floor could be selected. The woman pressed the button for the top floor, then stepped back to one side and stood quietly, saying nothing more.
The elevator rose all the way up, the numbers ticking past at a dizzying speed.
Thirty-eight… forty-two… fifty-seven… seventy-one…
Su Qingyuan noticed that this elevator made no stops at all between the ground floor and the top.
A private channel.
The elevator doors opened on the eighty-eighth floor.
Before her stretched a short corridor, at the end of which stood a pair of dark wooden double doors.
"President Lu is just inside, Miss Su." The woman bowed slightly, then turned and retreated into the elevator.
Su Qingyuan walked the corridor alone, the wooden floor giving off a faint sound beneath her steps.
She raised her hand and knocked.
"Come in."
The low, familiar voice came from within.
Su Qingyuan pushed the door open, and her steps faltered for an instant.
This was not the cold, sterile corporate office she had imagined.
The entire floor was one open space, wrapped in floor-to-ceiling glass on all three hundred and sixty degrees. Nancheng's mountains and rivers, its buildings and streets, all lay spread before the eye like an enormous scroll of the city unfurled beneath her feet.
Sunlight poured in from every direction, bathing the whole space in a clear, warm glow.
The work area sat at the very center—a vast desk of dark solid wood, on which documents and a laptop were neatly arranged, with a minimalist metal desk lamp beside them.
But what truly stopped Su Qingyuan in her tracks was the arrangement next to the work area.
A small round table, two armchairs, a white porcelain tea set on the table along with a slim-necked vase holding a few stems of white chamomile.
The sofa area was by the floor-to-ceiling windows—a dark gray fabric couch draped with a light beige throw, and a bookshelf beside it holding several design magazines and art albums.
This corner looked nothing like the office of the man who steered a trillion-yuan commercial empire. It looked more like a… home.
"What are you spacing out about?"
Lu Shiyan came around from behind his desk, two cups of coffee in his hands.
He had shed his suit jacket, wearing only a dark gray shirt, the cuffs rolled up to his forearms, baring well-defined wrists and an understated, restrained watch.
This look had a touch more ease than a formal suit—and a touch more… good looks.
Su Qingyuan drew her gaze back and took the coffee. "I thought your office would be very severe."
"It was, originally." Lu Shiyan lifted his chin, gesturing for her to look at the soft furnishings in the sofa area. "Then I had it changed."
"Why?"
He didn't answer directly. Instead he walked toward the floor-to-ceiling windows with his coffee, his voice mild. "Because some places are too cold to stay in—you can't settle. A little change makes it more comfortable."
Su Qingyuan looked at the white chamomile and the light beige throw, and couldn't shake the feeling that this color palette seemed somehow familiar.
It almost seemed… connected to that offhand remark she'd once made about liking "clean, warm colors"?
She didn't ask, afraid she was reading too much into it.
【Devotion System notice: The male lead's office renovation style references the female lead's aesthetic preferences.】
【No change in affection level, but the female lead's inner thought: How does he know what I like?】
Su Qingyuan: …
System, stop overinterpreting things.
"Sit down and talk." Lu Shiyan settled into the sofa area and pointed to the seat across from him.
Su Qingyuan sat down. The sofa was soft but well-supported—she sank in without feeling like she was collapsing into it. She set the document folder in her hands on the coffee table and took out the collaboration framework Zhou Wanyin had given her.
"The deal she's offering is a fifty-fifty split. I'd be attached as an independent designer, and she'd provide the resources, the channels, and the brand endorsement." Su Qingyuan pushed the documents across. "What do you think?"
Lu Shiyan took them and flipped through quickly, but lingered a few seconds on every page—clearly reading the key clauses.
Su Qingyuan noticed that his expression while reading the contract was utterly different from the one he'd worn at the salon. At the salon he was an onlooker, gentle and self-restrained; reading the contract he was the one in command, his gaze sharp, letting no detail slip past.
"A fifty-fifty split isn't low by industry standards." Lu Shiyan turned to the last page and closed the file. "But given your potential, you could actually negotiate for more."
"More?"
"You have no reputation right now, so a fifty-fifty split feels like a win to you. But what Zhou Wanyin has her eye on isn't the you of today—it's your value three to five years from now." Lu Shiyan lifted his eyes to her. "If your judgment about yourself isn't wrong, then you could push her for forty-sixty, even thirty-seventy."
Su Qingyuan was taken aback. "It never occurred to me that there was room to negotiate."
"There are a lot of things that never occurred to you before." Lu Shiyan's tone was calm—not belittling her, simply stating a fact. "But now you can start thinking about them."
He set the file back on the coffee table and leaned back slightly against the sofa, his posture relaxed yet commanding all the same.
"My advice is this: you can accept the fifty-fifty split, but add a clause—after two years, the profit-sharing ratio is renegotiated based on your market valuation. That way you give Zhou Wanyin enough profit margin to keep her motivated to promote you, while ensuring your own future upside doesn't get locked in."
Su Qingyuan listened intently, silently committing it to memory.
No one had ever taught her any of this before. Lin Haoyu would only say, "Just do your job, don't overthink it." The Su family only ever thought it was "lucky enough she even had a job."
No one had ever told her that her value was something she could negotiate, that her future was something she could plan.
"And another thing," Lu Shiyan went on. "The contract doesn't clearly define ownership of the intellectual property. The most common problem with attachment-style partnerships is squabbling over copyright of the work. You need to nail this down before signing—your original works, the copyright stays yours forever, and any licensed use requires your written consent."
Su Qingyuan nodded, carving every word into her mind.
"Also—" Lu Shiyan suddenly paused, looking at her.
Su Qingyuan waited a few seconds. He didn't go on, and she couldn't help asking, "Also what?"
"Also," he leaned forward slightly, his voice dropping a register, "I'm glad you came to me to analyze the contract."
Su Qingyuan's heart skipped a beat.
"Not because of the fact that you came to me itself." Lu Shiyan's gaze settled on her face, calm and earnest. "It's because you know who to come to when you need advice."
The words were restrained, deeply restrained, but Su Qingyuan understood them.
He was saying: you've started to trust me.
She lowered her eyes, picked up the coffee and took a sip, using the rim of the cup to hide the slight upward curve at the corner of her mouth.
"Don't flatter yourself," she said softly. "I just happened to be passing."
"Mm. Just passing." Lu Shiyan agreed obligingly enough, but the arc at the corner of his lips gave him away.
【Devotion System notice: The male lead is delighted by the female lead's "saying one thing and meaning another."】
【Affection +1! Current affection level: 71!】
Su Qingyuan: System, you really ought to shut up.
---
After finishing her coffee, Su Qingyuan stayed in the office a while longer.
Lu Shiyan went to deal with an email, and she stood at the floor-to-ceiling windows, taking in the view.
The view from the eighty-eighth floor was simply too vast. The whole city unfurled beneath her feet, and in the distance the surface of the river glittered with broken gold under the sun. She was suddenly struck by a very strange feeling—standing here, it was as though even life itself had become wider, more open.
"What are you looking at?" Lu Shiyan had come to her side without her noticing.
"The view." Su Qingyuan paused, then said honestly, "I've never looked at this city from this angle before."
"You can come often from now on."
Su Qingyuan turned her head to look at him. He was gazing out the window, the line of his profile cold and severe, but in the depths of his eyes there was a very, very faint tenderness.
She was about to say something when the phone in her pocket buzzed.
It was Su Yurou's number.
Su Qingyuan's brow furrowed slightly as she answered.
The voice on the other end wasn't Su Yurou's—it was an unfamiliar man's, thick with drunkenness and urgency:
"Hello? Are you a friend of the person who owns this phone? She's blackout drunk all by herself in our bar, crying the whole time, and refuses to leave. We're about to close—could you come pick her up?"
Su Qingyuan was silent for two seconds.
"Her affairs have nothing to do with me. Call someone else in her contacts."
"But there are only three contacts in her phone—one's switched off, one isn't picking up, and you're the last one—"
Su Qingyuan hung up.
Lu Shiyan turned his head to look at her, but didn't ask who it was.
Su Qingyuan put the phone back in her pocket, her expression placid. "Su Yurou got drunk at a bar and wants me to come get her."
"Are you going?"
"No."
Her answer was crisp and clean, without a trace of hesitation.
Lu Shiyan looked at her, and something hard to define surfaced in his eyes—not surprise, but a kind of "just as I expected" appreciation.
"The old you would definitely have gone," he said.
"The old me is the old me." Su Qingyuan raised her eyes to him. "Before, I owed the Su family. That debt is paid. Now, she owes me."
She paused, her voice low:
"That I'm not kicking her while she's down—that's already the greatest kindness I have in me."
Lu Shiyan said nothing, only let out a soft "Mm."
But Su Qingyuan noticed that the look in his eyes as he regarded her had grown a shade deeper than before.

【Current affection level: 74!】

At dusk, Su Qingyuan left the Lu Group building.
Lu Shiyan saw her to the door without saying much, only handing her a document before she got into the car.
"What's this?"
"Suggested supplementary clauses for that partnership with Zhou Wanyin. I had legal draft them for you. Use them if you want, no problem if you don't."
Su Qingyuan took it—a thick stack, clearly not something tossed off carelessly.
She looked up at him, wanting to say thank you, then felt those two words were far too light.
"Lu Shiyan." For the first time, she didn't call him Mr. Lu.
His brow flickered.
"You've helped me with so much," Su Qingyuan said, looking at him earnestly. "I'll repay it."
Lu Shiyan looked down at her. The light of dusk fell across his shoulders, and his whole figure seemed gilded with a soft golden edge.
"There's no need to repay it," he said, his voice very low. "If you make a good life for yourself, that's the best repayment there is."
Su Qingyuan gripped the document folder tightly, something in her chest squeezed hard.
She turned and got into the car without looking back.
Because she was afraid that if she did, she wouldn't be able to hide the emotion in her eyes.
The taxi pulled out of the financial district and merged into the evening rush-hour traffic.
Su Qingyuan leaned back against the seat, watching the neon lights gradually brighten outside the window, his words replaying over and over in her mind—
"If you make a good life for yourself, that's the best repayment there is."
She closed her eyes, the corners of her mouth curving.
This man—he kept talking about "investment," but the things he did, which one of them was an investment?
It was plainly—
Never mind. Stop thinking about it.

Meanwhile, at a certain bar in the southern part of the city.
Su Yurou slumped over the bar counter, a row of emptied glasses before her.
The bar had already closed, and the staff were doing their final cleanup. Seeing that she showed no sign of leaving, they wore expressions of helplessness.
"Ma'am, we really do have to close now…"
Su Yurou lifted her head, her eyes red and swollen, her makeup a complete ruin.
She looked at the empty bar and suddenly laughed.
The laughter was shrill and desolate, echoing through the empty space, the kind of sound that made one's skin crawl.
"Su Qingyuan, your heart is so cruel." She muttered to herself, her voice hoarse. "You really just won't help me anymore?"
"You weren't like this before… before, all I had to do was cry a little and you'd soften…"
She braced herself against the bar and stood, staggering, steadying herself only by grabbing the back of a chair.
Her phone screen lit up.
It was a message from her agent: 【Yurou, the brand has officially terminated the contract. About the penalty fee—come to the company tomorrow to discuss it.】
Su Yurou stared at the message, and the last tear in her eyes fell.
Then she laughed.
A laugh uglier than weeping.
"Fine… fine then…" She gripped the phone tight. "Su Qingyuan, you think you've stomped me down so now you can rest easy?"
"It won't happen."
"If I'm not getting my peace, don't you dream of getting yours either."
She staggered out of the bar, the night wind pouring down her collar, cold enough to make her shudder.
The nights of Nancheng were never warm.
Least of all for the losers.

Chapter 11 — Her First Studio Was His Doing
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626213.html

Su Qingyuan returned to her apartment and set down on the table the supplementary-clause proposal Lu Shiyan had given her—a thick stack, every page covered in dense legal annotations.
She sat at the table and turned through it, page by page.
The terms were clearly worded, the rights and responsibilities sharply delineated; even the "dispute resolution" section had thoughtfully been drafted to favor "negotiation first" rather than going straight to litigation—clearly, whoever had drawn up this document assumed she didn't want to fall out openly with Zhou Wanyin.
She turned to the last page and spotted a line of small handwriting in the bottom right corner, the fountain-pen strokes clean and sharp—just like the man who had written them.
"Sign it or don't, either way. But before you sign, come find me."
Su Qingyuan stared at that line for a long while.
Then she closed the document and put it away in a drawer.
It wasn't that she wouldn't sign. She just didn't want to go find him so soon.
She was afraid of forming a dependence.
Some things, once you got hooked, you could never quit.
[Devotion System notice: The female lead has "saved" the male lead's handwritten note rather than "discarding" it.]
[Hypocrisy index rising; affection level unchanged, but… never mind, as long as you two are happy.]
Su Qingyuan: …System, whose side are you even on?

The next morning, Su Qingyuan went to see Zhou Wanyin.
It was again that studio beneath the ginkgo tree. Autumn sunlight streamed in through the windows, and the worktables were spread with new design sketches.
Zhou Wanyin was as brisk and capable as ever, with no wasted pleasantries. She asked outright, "Made up your mind?"
"I have." Su Qingyuan sat down and handed over a revised cooperation framework. "I accept a fifty-fifty split, but I'd like to add one clause—two years from now, the split ratio gets renegotiated based on my market valuation."
Zhou Wanyin raised an eyebrow and glanced at the document.
Then she smiled.
"Did you come up with this yourself?"
"Someone gave me advice."
Zhou Wanyin let out a meaningful "Oh," but didn't press further. She picked up a pen, made a few changes to the document, and pushed it back. "Two years is too short. Make it three. If your personal brand is valued at over fifty million three years from now, the split can be adjusted to sixty-forty—sixty for you, forty for me."
Su Qingyuan was taken aback.
She had only dared to imagine sixty-forty in Zhou Wanyin's favor—forty for herself.
She hadn't expected Zhou Wanyin to simply hand her the sixty.
"Teacher Zhou, you…"
"I have faith in you." Zhou Wanyin cut her off, her tone flat but her gaze earnest. "If you can't reach a fifty-million valuation in three years, then it means my judgment was off. And there's nothing I trust more than my own judgment."
Su Qingyuan looked at the woman before her, and a complicated rush of emotion suddenly welled up in her chest.
All her life, she had met far too many people who wanted to milk her for gain, who wanted to climb over her to get ahead, who wanted to use her as a stepping stone.
But Zhou Wanyin wasn't one of them.
Neither was Lu Shiyan.
"All right." Su Qingyuan picked up the pen and signed her name on the contract. "Teacher Zhou, I won't let you misjudge me."
"Just call me Sister Wanyin." Zhou Wanyin tucked away the contract, stood up, and extended her hand. "Here's to a happy partnership."
"To a happy partnership."
Their two hands clasped together.
A brand-new beginning.

How did he know everything?

The walls were painted a warm white, the floor a light-gray self-leveling finish, clean and crisp. The display area had an entire wall of glass display cases with built-in light strips—perfect for showcasing jewelry pieces.
The work area held a huge solid-wood worktable, already fitted with professional lighting equipment, a magnifier lamp, and various tool-storage racks.

Exactly the way she liked it.

Sunlight poured in through the windows, lighting everything bright and warm.

At last she had a place of her own.
A place where she needn't read anyone's expression, needn't live under another's roof, needn't grovel just to survive.
And the key to this place had been handed to her by Lu Shiyan.

Chapter 12 — Su Yurou's Last Gamble: Digging Her Own Grave
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626214.html

During the three-day burst of inspiration, Su Qingyuan practically lived in her studio.
She left at the crack of dawn every morning and didn't come home until deep in the night, surviving the hours in between on takeout and coffee. Her worktable was buried under design sketches, one after another, pencil lines evolving from rough to refined, from blurry to crisp.
Over those three days, the prototype of the "First Light" series went from nothing to something, from zero to complete.
Seven pieces in all.
A necklace, a bracelet, drop earrings, a ring, a brooch, a hair ornament, and cufflinks.
At the heart of every piece was a single shaft of light—light breaking through the clouds, light piercing the deep sea, light shining into the abyss, the first ray before dawn.
Each of the seven pieces stood on its own, yet together they told one complete story: struggling out of the darkness, meeting that first ray of light, being wrapped in light, and finally becoming the light herself.
Su Qingyuan looked at the seven finished drafts spread across her worktable, her eyes faintly stinging.
Not from exhaustion, but from that particular kind of sting—the relief of finally pulling out something she'd kept bottled up in her heart for so long.
These seven drafts weren't drawings of jewelry.
They were her.
From being exploited, betrayed, and trampled into the dirt, to encountering that rainy night, that car, that man, to standing here now, brush in hand, becoming her own light.
Her phone buzzed.
Lu Shiyan: [Three days, no word. Still alive?]
Su Qingyuan looked at the message, smiled, and snapped a photo of her worktable to send over.
In the photo, the seven design drafts were lined up neatly, surrounded by scattered pencil shavings, an eraser, and a half-cup of coffee gone cold.
Lu Shiyan's reply came fast:
[This is the fruit of three sleepless nights?]
Su Qingyuan: [I slept. Four hours a day.]
Lu Shiyan: [……]
Lu Shiyan: [I'm coming over now.]
Su Qingyuan blinked, and just as she was about to reply "no need," another message came through:
[Not to see you. To collect rent. First quarter's.]
Su Qingyuan looked at those two words—"collect rent"—and simply couldn't press the corners of her mouth back down.
When this man made up an excuse, could he at least put a little more heart into it?

Forty minutes later, Lu Shiyan appeared at the studio door.

A bag of fruit in his left hand, a bag of snacks in his right, and an assistant carrying an insulated bag trailing behind him.

Three days apart, and she'd gotten visibly thinner. Faint shadows under her eyes, slightly chapped lips, hair carelessly tied back with a few stray wisps falling against her cheek, and pencil dust smudged on her work clothes.
But her eyes were bright.
That weary yet exhilarated brightness of someone who'd stayed up all night to finish an important piece.

Not takeout.
Cooked at home, packed in an insulated bag, and driven over forty minutes to be delivered here.

Lu Shiyan undid his shirt cuffs and rolled his sleeves up to his forearms, calmly setting out the utensils as he spoke. "My housekeeper made it. I can't cook."

Lu Shiyan sat down across from her, leaning back in his chair, posture relaxed, voice casual: "Eat first. We'll talk about the rent after."

But she didn't call him out, just lowered her head and ate in earnest.
Because she really was hungry.
Three days of running on coffee and sandwiches, and her stomach had long since started protesting.
The way she ate wasn't exactly graceful, but it was earnest. She chewed every bite carefully, as if completing some important task.
Lu Shiyan watched her eat, saying nothing, doing nothing. He just sat there, quiet and patient, waiting for her to finish.

Her mind was full of that one line of his: "If that light is me, then I'm honored."
Su Qingyuan put the pen down and buried her face in both hands.
It was over.
Completely over.

The person who'd called the police was Su Yurou.

The police station.
Su Qingyuan was led into an interrogation room where someone was already seated.
Su Yurou.
She wore a white dress and delicate, light makeup, her eyes red as if she'd been crying. Beside her sat a middle-aged man in a gray suit—presumably the lawyer she'd hired.
The moment she saw Su Qingyuan walk in, Su Yurou shot to her feet, pointed at her, and said in a trembling voice, "Officers, it's her! She stole my design!"
Su Qingyuan looked at her expressionlessly.

As she spoke, she pulled a sketchbook out of her bag, flipped it open, and handed it to the officers.
Su Qingyuan's gaze swept over it, her pupils contracting slightly.
The sketchbook did indeed contain rough drafts resembling the "First Light" concept. The theme of light and shadow, the motif of breaking free from a cocoon—a few of the compositions even looked very much like the ones she'd drawn.
But the strokes in those sketches were clumsy and the structure scattered, clearly the work of an amateur copying from some template.
To be precise, Su Yurou had peeked at her sketchbook when she wasn't paying attention, then drawn it from memory.
The one who'd stolen the design was biting back, accusing the victim of being the thief.
Su Qingyuan let out a cold laugh.

"Then do you know that the core technique of the 'First Light' series is a bidirectional cutting process for moonstone? I only developed that technique last month. Su Yurou's lawyer took the card, glanced at it, and his face instantly turned grim.
Jintiancheng. One of the top three law firms in Nancheng. This Lawyer Gu had never lost an intellectual property case.
Lu Shiyan picked up Su Yurou's sketchbook, flipped through two pages, and handed it to his own lawyer, his voice as light as if discussing some trivial little matter:

And backfired catastrophically.

The evidence was ironclad.

Chapter 13 — The Night Wind Was Gentle, and She Said, "I think I'm starting to like you"
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626215.html

Su Qingyuan said "my treat," but in the end it was Lu Shiyan who paid.
It wasn't that she didn't want to pay. When they finished eating and went to settle the bill, the cashier smiled and said, "This gentleman has already taken care of it."
Su Qingyuan turned to look at him. Lu Shiyan was standing by the door, head bowed over his phone, his profile traced into soft lines by the restaurant's warm amber light. Sensing her gaze, he lifted his head, his expression all innocence. "What is it?"
"We agreed it was my treat."
"Mm." He slipped his phone into his pocket. "You're treating. I'm paying. No conflict there."
Su Qingyuan looked at his perfectly self-righteous expression, opened her mouth, and found that she had absolutely nothing to say.
This man could even cheat with airtight logic.
They stepped out of the restaurant, and the night wind rushed to meet them, carrying the crisp chill peculiar to late autumn. Su Qingyuan instinctively drew his coat tighter around her shoulders—the one he'd draped over her outside the police station, which she'd kept forgetting to return.
Lu Shiyan glanced at the gesture but didn't remind her to give it back.
"Drive you home?" he asked.
"Let's just walk," Su Qingyuan said. "I ate too much. Need to walk it off."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, then nodded.
The two of them walked side by side through the nighttime streets of Nancheng.
This street was near the creative park, and at this hour there was hardly a soul around. The streetlamps stretched their two shadows long, long, overlapping then parting, parting then overlapping.
Neither of them spoke.
Yet that silence wasn't awkward—on the contrary, it carried a strange sense of ease. As if they'd been together for a long time, with no need to force a topic, no need to fill the quiet, just walking, and that alone was enough.
Passing a flower shop that hadn't yet closed, Su Qingyuan paused.
In the window sat a bouquet of white chamomile, the tiny blossoms huddled together, clean and warm.
Lu Shiyan followed her gaze.
"You like them?"
Su Qingyuan pulled her eyes away and shook her head. "Just looking."
He said nothing, and the two of them kept walking.
After about a dozen steps, Su Qingyuan heard the bell of the flower shop door ring behind her. Assuming they were closing up, she didn't turn around.
Until Lu Shiyan said, "Hold out your hand."
She turned, and a bouquet of white chamomile was held out in front of her.
She froze.
"Didn't you say you were just looking?"
"You said you were just looking," Lu Shiyan's voice sounded especially low in the night wind, "but the way you looked at them—it wasn't just looking."
Su Qingyuan looked at the bouquet, then back at him.
His expression was very calm, with none of that deliberate romance, none of that grand show. As if he'd done something perfectly ordinary, not worth making a fuss over.
But the string in her heart had just been plucked, hard.
"Thank you." She took the flowers, lowered her head, and breathed in their scent, her voice a little muffled.
"You're welcome."
The two of them kept walking.
Su Qingyuan held the chamomile in her arms, and as she walked the little blossoms trembled and trembled, brushing against her chin—ticklish, and sweet.
By the time they reached the foot of her apartment building, the light above the entrance was still on, its dim yellow glow spilling onto the ground like a small, warm lake.
"We're here." Su Qingyuan stopped.
Lu Shiyan stopped too.
The two of them stood facing each other, a bouquet's distance between them.
"About today," Su Qingyuan lifted her head to look at him, "thank you. Not just for the flowers—for the police station too. If it weren't for you, I wouldn't have gotten out of there so fast."
Lu Shiyan lowered his eyes to look at her, his voice very soft. "I told you, you don't need to thank me."
"I know you said that. But I still want to say it."
Su Qingyuan looked into his deep eyes. The night wind tousled her hair, a few loose strands falling against her cheek. She suddenly felt that there were some things which, if she didn't say them tonight, she might never have the courage to say later.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"I think I…" She paused, her fingers tightening slightly around the bouquet, her voice soft as though afraid of startling something, "…am starting to like you."
The night wind suddenly went still.
Lu Shiyan looked at her, his eyes deep, so very deep, like undercurrents hidden beneath the surface of a midnight sea.
He didn't speak right away. He was silent for a few seconds, then bent slightly toward her, narrowing the distance between them.
"Think?" His voice was very low, low enough that it seemed meant for her ears alone.
Su Qingyuan's heart was pounding hard, but she fought to keep her face composed. "It's just 'think.' I'm not sure yet."
"Then tell me once you're sure."
His tone was very calm, but Su Qingyuan noticed that the hand hanging at his side curled slightly at the fingertips.
That tiny movement made the last bit of uncertainty in her heart melt away all at once, like a block of ice meeting hot water.
So he was nervous too.
So she wasn't the only one whose heart was racing.
"Goodnight." Su Qingyuan took a step back.
"Goodnight."
She turned and walked through the entrance, the bouquet of white chamomile in her arms, climbing the stairs one step at a time.
Three floors up, she couldn't resist glancing down through the stairwell window.
Lu Shiyan was still standing there.
Beneath the streetlamp, he stood alone, his suit jacket on her shoulders, leaving him in nothing but his shirt, the night wind lifting its hem ever so slightly.
He was gazing up at the building, though she couldn't tell which window he was looking at.
Su Qingyuan ducked back, her heart pounding like a drum.
She hurried up the stairs, opened her door, stepped inside, set the flowers carefully on the table, then walked to the window and looked down.
He was already gone.
The space beneath the streetlamp was empty, leaving only a patch of dim yellow light spilled across the ground.
Su Qingyuan stood at the window, then slowly crouched down and buried her face against her knees.
It was over.
Completely over.
[Devotion System notice: The female lead has made the first confession—"I think I'm starting to like you." With "think" and "starting to" both hedging.]
[Male lead's response: "Tell me once you're sure"—outwardly restrained, inwardly in ruins.]
[Male lead's inner monologue unlocked: She said "I think I'm starting to like you." Think. Starting to. Both words holding something back. Su Qingyuan: ……

The tiny blossoms, their clean and pure color, their faint fragrance.
She remembered what he'd said: "The way you looked at them—it wasn't just looking."
This man—how did he manage to be domineering and tender all at once?
Su Qingyuan found a glass jar, arranged the flowers in it, and set it on the windowsill. Moonlight spilled in through the window, falling on the little white blossoms, quiet and lovely.
She looked at the bouquet and suddenly let out a small laugh.
Think.
Starting to.
Those two words really were holding something back.
But she knew that her real feelings ran far more than "think," weighed far more than "starting to."
She just… wasn't ready yet to say "I like you so much, so very much."
A little longer.
Wait for him to come a little closer, wait for her to be a little more sure.
And then, she'd look him in the eyes and say it, sincerely and in earnest:
Lu Shiyan, I like you. Not "I think," not "starting to."
It's "so much." So very much.
---
Early the next morning, Su Qingyuan had barely arrived at the studio when her phone blew up.
Countless messages came flooding in—WeChat, Weibo, industry forums—all buzzing about the same thing.
The design drafts for the "First Light" series had been posted online.
She hadn't posted them.
Su Qingyuan opened the Weibo post, and her pupils shrank.
Nine images, capturing all seven finished drafts of the "First Light" series, down to the pencil shavings scattered across the worktable and a half-finished cup of coffee. The shots were taken from directly above the table, in high resolution—clearly someone had slipped into the studio while she was away to photograph them.
The Weibo caption was dripping with snide insinuation:
"A certain up-and-coming 'genius designer's' 'First Light' series—the inspiration and compositional elements bear a striking resemblance to a foreign designer's portfolio from three years ago. Original work, or 'borrowing'? See for yourselves."
Below it were several comparison images.
Su Qingyuan zoomed in on the comparisons and nearly laughed in fury.
The other side had dug up the portfolio of an obscure foreign designer. There were indeed a few light-and-shadow-themed elements in it, but whether in structure, material, craftsmanship, or core concept, it was completely different from the "First Light" series.
The so-called "striking resemblance" was entirely manufactured—through cropped angles, selective close-ups, and forced associations.
But the average netizen wouldn't look that closely.
They'd only see the word "plagiarism," only see those "similarities" deliberately framed in the comparison images, and then storm into the comment section to fling abuse with gusto.
The comments had already climbed toward ten thousand.
"Another plagiarism freak?"
"Crashed and burned the second she got popular. Hilarious."
"Zhou Wanyin actually signed her? Looks like Sister Wanyin misjudged this one."
"People like this deserve to get blacklisted."
Su Qingyuan's fingers went cold, but her mind was racing.
Who had posted this Weibo?
Su Yurou was in the detention center—it couldn't be her.
Someone from the Su family? Possible. But more likely—Su Yurou had left a contingency plan in place before going in. She'd been scheming this for a while; she just hadn't expected to get arrested first. That Weibo post had been scheduled in advance.
Su Qingyuan drew a deep breath, set down her phone, and walked to the window.
The osmanthus tree was still there, its fragrance still there.
But her state of mind was completely different from yesterday.
She closed her eyes, her thoughts spinning at top speed.
She couldn't panic.
She couldn't lose her composure.
This was her first collection, drawn line by line with her own hand. Every line, every structure, every detail of craftsmanship—she could explain the creative logic behind all of it.
The other side couldn't produce any evidence that she'd plagiarized.
But she could produce evidence of her own originality.
From the conceptual sketches to the finished drafts, she had every step on record in her system.
Su Qingyuan opened her eyes and dialed Zhou Wanyin.
"Sister Wanyin, have you seen what's going on online?"
"I've seen it." Zhou Wanyin's voice was steady and composed, without a trace of panic. "I've got the legal team handling it right now. Qingyuan, let me ask you one question, and I want you to answer me honestly—are these designs your original work or not?"
"They are."
"Good." Zhou Wanyin's tone turned firm. "Then I'll handle this matter. Don't post anything, don't respond to anything. Wait for word from me."
The call ended.
Su Qingyuan held her phone, most of the worry settled out of her heart.
But she knew this wouldn't blow over so easily.
The fact that the other side had chosen this particular moment to strike was clearly carefully planned—the "First Light" series hadn't been officially released yet, she hadn't had the chance to establish any public recognition, and slinging mud at a time like this was the easiest way to make it stick.
She had to do something.
She couldn't just wait.
Su Qingyuan walked to the worktable, opened her computer, and logged into her own Weibo account.
She'd registered for Weibo a long time ago but had never posted anything. Her avatar was still the default gray, and she had only a few dozen followers, most of them bots.
She thought for a moment, then pulled up a photo of the very first draft of the "First Light" series from her phone—the first version she'd drawn three days ago, with rough lines and a loose structure, worlds apart from the final draft.
Then she uploaded that photo with a single line of text:
["First Light," day one. In three days, it became what you've seen. I have a record of every step of the process. Just wait.]
After posting, she set the phone face-down on the table and began assembling all the records of her creative process.
From the first rough sketch, to the second version, the third, the fourth… all the way to the seventh and final draft.
From notes on material selection, craft research, and technical breakthroughs.
From the experimental process of the bidirectional moonstone cutting technique, to photographs of all the failed versions.
She organized every bit of it, arranged it along a timeline, and compiled it into a complete creative archive.
If the other side wanted a fight, then a fight they'd get.
A fight to the finish.
---
Two hours later, Zhou Wanyin called.
"Qingyuan, I tracked down the account that posted that Weibo. It's a marketing account, and behind it is a small PR firm. I had someone ask around, and they said they were commissioned to post it by a man named Su Guoqiang."
Su Guoqiang.
Su Qingyuan's adoptive father.
Su Yurou's biological father.
Su Qingyuan closed her eyes, her fingers tightening around the phone.
She wasn't surprised.
Not in the slightest.
Su Yurou had been arrested, and Su Guoqiang had panicked. His daughter's reputation was already ruined, and now she'd lost her personal freedom too—he had to do something to turn the situation around. Or rather, to take revenge.
"Sister Wanyin, I'll handle this one myself."
"Are you sure?"
"I'm sure." Su Qingyuan opened her eyes, her voice frighteningly calm. "There are some accounts that it's time to settle all at once."
She hung up, scrolled through her contacts, and found a number.
It belonged to the lawyer who'd helped her with her lease before—not the top-tier attorney Lu Shiyan had brought, but a middle-aged female lawyer who specialized in family disputes, surnamed Liu, sharp and efficient in her work and upright in character.
"Lawyer Liu, I'd like to consult about something. Concerning the support obligations between adoptive parents and an adopted daughter, and… the matter of prosecuting adoptive parents on suspicion of defamation and copyright infringement."
Lawyer Liu clearly hadn't expected her to ask about this. She was silent for two seconds, then said, "Ms. Su, for something like this, I'd advise you to talk it over with your adoptive parents first. Once you take the legal route, whatever the outcome, the family bond is severed for good."
"It's already severed." Su Qingyuan's tone didn't waver in the slightest. "And besides, they're the ones who drew the knife first."
There was silence on the other end for a few more seconds, then Lawyer Liu said, "All right. I understand. Come to the firm, and we'll talk it through in person."
Su Qingyuan hung up and picked up her bag to head out.
At the door she paused, glancing back at the seven design drafts on the worktable.
Outside the window, the osmanthus tree swayed gently in the wind, its shadow falling across the drafts.
She suddenly remembered what Lu Shiyan had said standing right here yesterday: "This story—I'm in it too."
Su Qingyuan pulled her gaze away and pushed open the door.
This time, she didn't want anyone to take the hit for her.
She would sweep her own battlefield clean—by herself.
---
On the way to the law firm, her phone buzzed.
Lu Shiyan: [I saw what's happening online. What do you need me to do?]
Su Qingyuan looked at the message, warmth stirring in her chest, but her reply was perfectly composed:
[Nothing. I've got this one myself. He's my adoptive father—this is a fight I should fight on my own. You just stay on the sidelines and watch.]
There was a pause on the other end.
Lu Shiyan: [All right. I'll watch.]
Then, a few seconds later:
Lu Shiyan: [But if you get tired of fighting, tell me anytime. I'll finish the second half for you.]
Su Qingyuan looked at those words—"I'll finish the second half for you"—and her nose suddenly stung.
This man, who would always say "step in when you can't go on anymore," who always handed her the initiative, who never overstepped.
And the more he was like this, the more she wanted him to overstep.
[Devotion System notice: The female lead refuses the male lead's help, choosing to face her adoptive father alone—displaying an independent character.]
[The male lead expresses "I respect your choice, but I'm on standby anytime"—displaying high-level emotional intelligence.]
[No change in affection level, but the quality of their relationship has improved markedly.]
[System's verdict: A good relationship isn't one person shielding the other from every storm—it's "I know you'd take the hit for me, but I still want to try it myself." The two of you managed that.]
Su Qingyuan put her phone away and looked out the car window.
The taxi was just passing Nancheng's financial center, the tallest tower glittering in the sunlight.
The windows on the eighty-eighth floor reflected a dazzling glare. She couldn't see whether anyone was standing up there, but she knew—there was one person there.
Watching her.
Waiting for her.
Ready, the moment she grew tired of fighting, to step in and finish the second half for her.
Su Qingyuan pulled her gaze back, the corners of her mouth curving up.
Su Guoqiang.
Bring it on.
Old debts and new—today we settle them all.

Chapter 14 — Facing Down Her Adoptive Father: The Truth, Live for the Whole Internet
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626216.html

By the time Su Qingyuan arrived at Lawyer Liu's firm, it was already two in the afternoon.
Lawyer Liu was in her early forties, with short hair, no makeup, and sharp eyes. She went through every piece of material Su Qingyuan had brought—from the evidence of her adoptive parents docking her wages and restricting her freedom in the early years, to the court verdict on Su Yurou stealing her design drafts and framing her with false charges, all the way to the chat logs and transfer receipts of Su Guoqiang bribing a marketing account to spread slander this time around.
Page after page, Lawyer Liu's expression went from calm to grave, from grave to silent.
When she finished the last page, she took off her glasses and pinched the bridge of her nose.
"Ms. Su, with this evidence, you could put them away for the rest of their lives."
Su Qingyuan sat across from her, her expression composed. "I don't need them behind bars. I need a public apology, and an admission that the 'First Light' series is my original work. And on top of that, to sever the adoptive relationship—so we're square, once and for all."
Lawyer Liu glanced at her. "You're sure you don't want to go the criminal route? Defamation, copyright infringement—the evidence is more than enough."
"I'm sure." There wasn't a trace of hesitation in Su Qingyuan's voice. "What I want isn't to throw them in prison; it's to cut every last tie between them and me, completely. A criminal case drags on too long, and my career can't afford to wait. A civil case is fast."
Lawyer Liu nodded, then pulled out her phone to glance at the trending topics on Weibo.
"Things are still heating up on Su Guoqiang's end. The internet's split into two camps now. Plenty of people cursing you out—but more and more are starting to speak up for you, too. Especially after Zhou Wanyin put out her statement."
Su Qingyuan paused for a beat, then opened Weibo.
Zhou Wanyin's account had posted a long article, titled "Regarding the 'First Light' Series, I Stake My Career On It."
There wasn't a single wasted word in the whole piece—she laid out three things right up front: the original-work declaration Su Qingyuan had submitted when she joined the studio, the contract's guarantee clause stating that "all works are original," and—Zhou Wanyin's own professional appraisal report on the seven pieces of the "First Light" series.
The last line of the report read: "Upon appraisal by myself and the studio's professional team, all seven pieces of the 'First Light' series are Su Qingyuan's original creations, free of plagiarism, derivation, or any form of infringement. Should this prove false, I will retire from the design world permanently."
That final sentence landed with the weight of an oath.
The tide in the comments turned in an instant.
"Zhou Wanyin's staking her whole career on it? That's a heavy bet."
"I trust Sister Wanyin's eye. She wouldn't misjudge someone."
"Hold on—so it's this guy named Su Guoqiang slinging the mud?"
"Who's Su Guoqiang? Seems like he's that Su Yurou's dad?"
"God, this whole family is disgusting—they stole someone's work and then have the nerve to play victim?"
Looking at Zhou Wanyin's statement, Su Qingyuan felt her nose sting.
She sent Zhou Wanyin a message: Sister Wanyin, thank you.
Zhou Wanyin replied in a heartbeat: Thank me for what? Your work is genuine; I just told the truth. What about you—what are you planning to do next? Su Guoqiang won't take this lying down.
Su Qingyuan: I've arranged to meet him tomorrow afternoon, at the old Su family house. Lawyer Liu is coming with me. I plan to livestream the entire meeting.
Zhou Wanyin: You sure? If you livestream and something goes sideways, the whole internet's watching.
Su Qingyuan: I'm sure. If they want to make a scene, then let's make it the biggest one yet. Who's lying, who's doing wrong—let everyone see it with their own eyes.

Su Qingyuan: Yes, please. Thank you, Sister Wanyin.
Zhou Wanyin: No more thanks—go get ready. Tomorrow, I'll be waiting for your good news.
[Devotion System notice: The female lead chooses to confront her adoptive father via livestream—burning her boats, facing him head-on.]

By the time Su Qingyuan got back to the studio, it was nearly dark.
Someone was standing at the door.
Lu Shiyan.
He was leaning against the osmanthus tree, a document envelope in hand. Seeing her approach, he straightened up, said nothing, and simply held the envelope out to her.
"What's this?"
"The evidence you wanted."
Su Qingyuan took it and opened it. Inside was a thick stack of documents—Su Guoqiang's complete transfer records with that PR company, the chat logs, and the PR company's internal emails, spelling it out in black and white: "Task: manufacture public opinion that Su Qingyuan plagiarized. Budget: fifty thousand. Goal: sink her first collection."
"These… how did you get them?"
"The PR company's boss is a supplier to one of our group's subsidiaries." Lu Shiyan's tone was flat, as if remarking that the weather was nice today. "I had someone make a phone call, and he handed over everything."
Su Qingyuan looked up at him. The evening light fell across his shoulders. His expression was placid, as if he'd done some trivial little thing not worth mentioning.
"Didn't you say you'd let me fight this on my own?"
"Letting you fight it yourself doesn't mean I won't hand you a weapon." Lu Shiyan lowered his eyes to her. "The evidence is yours to begin with. I just helped you gather it."
Su Qingyuan gripped the envelope and lowered her head, her voice a little muffled. "Lu Shiyan, can't you just not do this every single time?"
"Do what?"
"This… doing everything so perfectly. Making me feel like I'm capable, while also making me feel… like without you, I might not be able to pull it off."
A few seconds of quiet.
Lu Shiyan's voice came down from above her, very low, very soft: "Su Qingyuan, you could do it without me too. It would just be a little slower, a little more exhausting, a little more painful. I don't want you to hurt anymore."
The fragrance of the osmanthus grew especially rich in the dusk.
Su Qingyuan didn't look up. She was afraid that the moment she did, the thing welling up in her eyes would spill over.
"Two o'clock tomorrow afternoon, the old Su family house. I'll be livestreaming." She said it, her voice steady now. "Do you… want to come?"
"Do you want me there?"
"I do."
"Then I'll come." Lu Shiyan paused. "But I won't be on camera. I'll be off to the side, watching you."
Su Qingyuan finally raised her head and looked at him.
His eyes seemed especially deep in the twilight—holding lamplight, the evening glow, the shadow of the osmanthus tree, and her, too.
"Okay." She smiled.
He smiled too.
Faint, but lovely.
