Two o'clock the next afternoon. The old Su family house.
Su Qingyuan stood before that familiar iron gate, not a ripple in her heart.
She had lived in this house for over a decade. Here she'd weathered the scoldings, the beatings, the countless cold stares. Here she'd been told to "let your sister have her way," to "be sensible," to "stop causing trouble for the family."
And it was here, too, that she'd been told: "You're not our flesh and blood. You should be grateful we raised you at all—don't go thinking you deserve better."
Su Qingyuan drew a deep breath and pushed the gate open.
A crowd stood in the courtyard.
Su Guoqiang, Liu Xiulan, a few of Su Yurou's uncles and aunts, and several neighbors from the street. The setup was elaborate, as if they were waiting to put someone on trial.
The moment they saw Su Qingyuan walk in, Su Guoqiang's face hardened, his voice climbing an octave above normal. "You still have the nerve to come back? Look at what you've done to your sister!"
Liu Xiulan dabbed at her tears beside him. "Yurou's been frail since she was little—how could you have the heart to send her to a place like that? She's still just a child…"
Expressionless, Su Qingyuan opened her phone, launched the livestream app, set up the angle, and spoke into the camera: "Hello, everyone. I'm Su Qingyuan. Today I've come to the old Su family house to settle some personal matters. Every conversation will be streamed live, start to finish—no editing, no pausing."
The viewer count in the livestream room shot up rapidly from a few dozen.
Zhou Wanyin had shared the link, and Lu Shiyan's PR team was quietly boosting the traffic behind the scenes. In less than five minutes, the number of live viewers broke a hundred thousand.
Su Guoqiang still had no idea what was happening, and kept on roaring: "What are you livestreaming for?! Haven't you shamed this family enough?!"
Su Qingyuan fixed the phone onto the flower rack in the courtyard, the lens capturing a full view of the entire yard.
"Mr. Su"—it was the first time she hadn't called him "Dad"—"you say I've ruined Su Yurou. Then let's get one thing straight first: how did Su Yurou end up locked away?"
"She filed a false police report, falsely accusing me of plagiarism. After investigating, the police found that she was the one who stole my design drafts, copied a key to my apartment, and fabricated evidence. Her detention is entirely of her own making. It has nothing to do with me."
Su Guoqiang's face went livid. "You—"
"Don't be in such a hurry, I'm not finished." Su Qingyuan took out the documents Lu Shiyan had given her and held them up to the camera. "This is evidence that Su Guoqiang—my adoptive father, that is—bribed marketing accounts to defame me. Transfer records, chat logs, the PR company's internal emails—all of it, right here."
The danmaku in the livestream room went wild.
"Holy crap, a father buying trolls to smear his own daughter?"
"Not his real father—his adoptive father, and the kind who plays favorites at that."
"This family is seriously disgusting, huh?"
"This girl's got guts! Calling them out on a live stream!"
When Su Guoqiang saw those documents, his face shifted from livid to ashen.
"You… where did you get those?!"
"Where I got them doesn't matter. What matters is that every bit of it is fact." Su Qingyuan put the documents away and looked at Su Guoqiang, her gaze as calm as a pool of still water. "Mr. Su, I didn't come here today to argue. I came to lay out my terms."
"First, you issue a public apology, admitting that the 'First Light' series is my original work, and admitting that you hired trolls to spread rumors."
"Second, you and Liu Xiulan sign an agreement dissolving the adoptive relationship. From now on, I have nothing to do with the two of you."
"Third, the apology Su Yurou owes me can wait until she's out. But what you two owe me gets paid back today."
Liu Xiulan suddenly shrieked: "Dissolve the relationship?! In your dreams! We raised you for over a decade, and now that your wings are strong you want to fly off? Let me tell you, don't think you'll be shorting us a single cent of support money!"
Su Qingyuan shot her a glance and spoke in an unhurried tone: "Ms. Liu, regarding the duty of support, I've consulted a lawyer. According to the law, if adoptive parents abuse or abandon their adopted child, or otherwise seriously harm the adopted child's interests, the adopted child may petition to dissolve the adoptive relationship—and is not obligated to provide support."
She pulled a stack of old photographs from her bag and held them up to the camera one by one.
"This is a photo of me at thirteen. The bruises on my body are from Liu Xiulan beating me with a coat hanger. This is my report card at fifteen—third in the entire grade—but they wouldn't let me go to high school, because 'there's no point in a girl studying that much.'"
"These are my pay stubs from eighteen to twenty-one—I worked as a designer at the shop the Su family ran, and my monthly wage was eight hundred yuan, while everyone else in the same position made four thousand."

Liu Xiulan stared at the photographs, her face as white as paper, her lips trembling, unable to get a word out.
Su Guoqiang glared at Su Qingyuan, his eyes brimming with hatred. He suddenly let out a cold sneer: "You think that just because you've got money and power now, you can stamp us into the ground? Su Qingyuan, let me tell you—you've got the blood of some random wild man running through your veins. What makes you think you're anything decent?"
The air went suddenly still.
Su Qingyuan wasn't angry, wasn't agitated. She simply looked at him, calm.
"Are you finished?"
Su Guoqiang was only further enraged by her composure: "And what if I am? You think you can have me arrested?"
"No, I can't." Su Qingyuan turned, lifted the phone from the flower rack, and faced the camera. "Everyone, that's the end of today's livestream. The legal proceedings to follow, I'll announce publicly through my lawyer."
She ended the stream and turned to Lawyer Liu.
Lawyer Liu nodded and drew a set of three identical legal documents from her briefcase.
"Mr. Su Guoqiang, Ms. Liu Xiulan, this is the agreement to dissolve the adoptive relationship. You may choose to sign it voluntarily, or you may choose not to. If you don't sign, we will file suit with the court, attaching all the evidence of abuse, defamation, and copyright infringement. Criminal case and civil case, pursued together."
Su Guoqiang stared at the agreement, his hands shaking.
He couldn't read, but he knew what was written on it.
Sign it, and once his daughter Yurou got out, there'd be nothing left. No Su Qingyuan to use as a stepping stone, no source of income, nothing to lean on.
Don't sign it, and he might end up locked away. Abuse, defamation, copyright infringement—altogether enough to put him behind bars for several years.
He glanced at Liu Xiulan.
Liu Xiulan had stopped crying. Her eyes were hollow, like a husk drained of its soul.
"I…" Su Guoqiang's voice was hoarse. "I'll sign."
He picked up the pen and wrote out his name on the agreement, stroke by stroke.
Liu Xiulan signed after him.
Once she'd finished, Liu Xiulan suddenly lifted her head and looked at Su Qingyuan, tears in her eyes, along with some emotion too tangled to name: "Qingyuan… Mom is sorry."
Su Qingyuan looked at her and said nothing.
I'm sorry.
Those words came far too late.
Over a decade too late.
"Lawyer Liu," Su Qingyuan picked up the agreement, her voice very soft, "I'll leave the rest to you."
She turned and walked out through the iron gate of the old Su family house.
Outside, Lu Shiyan was leaning against the car, watching her.
He didn't ask "how did it go," nor did he say "you did well." He simply pulled open the car door and said one thing to her:
"Get in. I'm taking you to dinner."
Su Qingyuan looked at him and suddenly smiled.
And as she smiled, the tears fell.
Not tears of sorrow, but the kind that come from finally heaving off the mountain that had crushed you for more than a decade—tears of release.
Lu Shiyan didn't say "don't cry," nor did he hand her a tissue. He simply stood before her, quiet and patient, waiting for her to finish crying.
Only after she'd wiped her own tears dry did he say, "Let's go."
"Mm." Su Qingyuan sniffled and got into the car.
The car started up and pulled away from the old street she'd lived on for over a decade.
She didn't look back.
From today onward, she was no one's adopted daughter, no one's stepping stone, no one's punching bag to bully at will.
She was simply Su Qingyuan.
A jewelry designer.
Someone destined to shine, blindingly bright.
[Main quest updated: Completely sever the ties to your family of origin—Complete!]
[Current achievement progress: 50%!]
[System reward: Industry reputation +500, talent value +300, popularity value +10,000!]
[Devotion System notice: The female lead has completed the most crucial step of her self-redemption. No change in affection level, but the male lead's inner monologue is unlocked—]
[Male lead's inner monologue: When she cried, I wanted to hold her. But I didn't. Because those were her own tears. She needed to cry them all out herself. The most I could do was stand beside her, so she wouldn't be alone.]
Su Qingyuan watched the streetscape rushing backward outside the window, then suddenly spoke: "Lu Shiyan."
"Mm?"
"Last time I said I think I kind of like you."
Lu Shiyan's fingers tightened ever so slightly on the steering wheel.
"Now," Su Qingyuan's voice was soft, but perfectly clear, "I'm certain."
The car went quiet for a moment.
Then Lu Shiyan pulled over to the side of the road.
He turned his head, his deep eyes fixed steadily on her.
"You're certain?"
"I'm certain."
"No taking it back?"
"No taking it back."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, the light in his eyes like something he'd finally been waiting for.
Then he leaned in, one hand gently cradling the back of her head, and pressed his forehead to hers.
Their breaths intertwined, close enough that their lashes nearly touched.
"Su Qingyuan." His voice was low and husky, like emotion held back far too long had finally found its way out.
"I've waited a long time for those words."
Su Qingyuan closed her eyes, the corners of her mouth curving up.
"I know."
"You were waiting for me to be certain."
"Now, I'm certain."
The scent of osmanthus drifted in through the half-open window, mingling with the cool, clean fragrance inside the car—sweet, but never cloying.
And so they stayed, forehead to forehead, neither of them saying another word.
Outside the window the sky gradually darkened, and the streetlights came on one by one, linking into a warm river of light.
[Devotion System notice: Affection level +4! Current affection level: 99%!]
[System assessment: Ninety-nine percent. Just one to go. That last one percent isn't a matter of not liking each other enough—it's that a certain something hasn't happened yet. That something, you both know what it is.]
Su Qingyuan: I don't.
System: You do.
Lu Shiyan: I don't either.
System: …You two really are a perfect match.
What Su Qingyuan didn't know was that when Lu Shiyan started the car, no matter how he tried, he couldn't press the curve of his lips back down.
He even hummed softly, like a laugh, or maybe a sigh.
He'd gotten his wish.
She was finally certain.
And he—from the night of that rainstorm onward—had never once been uncertain.

Chapter 15 — Going Public? No—Being Made Public
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626217.html

Lu Shiyan parked the car downstairs from Su Qingyuan's apartment building but didn't cut the engine right away.
The car was so quiet they could hear each other breathing. The warmth from where their foreheads had touched a moment ago still lingered on her skin, like a tiny brand.
Su Qingyuan unbuckled her seatbelt, but she didn't push the door open to get out.
She turned her head and glanced at him. His hand was still resting on the steering wheel, fingertips tapping lightly without his noticing, the rhythm a little faster than usual—he was nervous.
The discovery inexplicably made her want to laugh.
"I'll head up, then," she said.
"Mm."
"You should get home early too."
"Mm."
After two "mm"s, neither of them moved.
Su Qingyuan finally couldn't hold back her laughter. "Lu Shiyan, are you going to say something to me or not?"
Lu Shiyan turned to look at her. The glow of the streetlamp beyond the window fell into his eyes, like shattered stars.
"Say what?" he asked, knowing full well.
"Such as…" Su Qingyuan drew the words out. "What exactly are we now?"
Lu Shiyan looked into her eyes, the corners of his mouth slowly curving up. The smile was impossible to suppress, so he simply stopped trying.
"You tell me."
"I'm asking you."
"I'd say," he leaned in, his voice dropping low, "it's the kind where, from this day on, I'm part of all of it—every triumph, every mess."
Su Qingyuan's heart skipped another beat.
This man. He wouldn't just say something ordinary like "boyfriend and girlfriend"—no, he had to use one long sentence to make her blush.
"Can't you just say things straight?"
"No." Lu Shiyan said it with complete conviction. "Saying 'you're my girlfriend' outright would be letting you off too easy."
Su Qingyuan: "…What kind of logic is that?"

Su Qingyuan fell silent.
Of course she knew. The system broadcast his affection level every single day. Even though he himself had no idea the system existed, she'd watched every flutter of his heart, every act of restraint, every quiet thing he'd done for her—all of it, perfectly clear.
"Not that long," she said, her voice gentle. "Barely over a week."
"To me, it felt like a year."

Lu Shiyan was already out of the car.
He came around the front, pulled open her door, and held out his hand.
Su Qingyuan looked at that hand, knuckles sharply defined, hesitated for a fraction of a second, then placed her own in it.
His palm was dry and warm, his grip neither too firm nor too loose—just enough to make her feel safe without feeling held captive.
The two of them walked hand in hand through the building's entrance and up the stairs.
Su Qingyuan fished her keys out of her bag, and as she slid the key into the lock, she glanced back at him.
The stairwell light was a dim yellow. He stood two steps below her, tilting his head up slightly to look at her. The angle softened the usually severe lines of his face, making him look like a boy waiting at the door, reluctant to say goodbye.
"I'm going in," Su Qingyuan said.
"Mm."
"Be careful on your way down."
"Mm."
Two more "mm"s.
Su Qingyuan bit her lip, then suddenly rose onto her toes and pecked him quickly on the cheek.
A dragonfly skimming water—light as a flower petal landing on skin.
Then she swiftly opened the door, slipped inside, and slammed it shut with a bang.
One fluid motion, fast as if she'd rehearsed it.
Inside the door, Su Qingyuan leaned back against it, both hands pressed over her face, her ears red enough to bleed.
Outside the door, Lu Shiyan stood rooted in place. Slowly he lifted his fingers and touched the spot on his skin where she'd kissed him.
Then he smiled.
Not his usual restrained, reserved little smile—a real one, rising from the bottom of his heart, impossible to suppress no matter what.
He turned and headed downstairs, his footsteps echoing in the empty stairwell, every step light as if he were treading on clouds.
【Devotion System Alert: Female lead initiated a kiss on the male lead's cheek—first kiss (cheek edition).】
【Male lead's reaction: Stood in place and smiled for seventeen seconds.】
【Affection level: Has reached 99%. The remaining 1% requires a special event to trigger.】

Su Qingyuan instinctively touched the corner of her mouth.
It really was turned up.

The two of them locked eyes across five floors.
Su Qingyuan didn't duck away, and Lu Shiyan didn't wave.
They just looked, for a single moment.
Then he got into the car, the engine started, and he drove out of the complex.
Su Qingyuan watched the taillights disappear at the intersection, drew the curtain shut, leaned against the window, and reached up to touch her own lips.
That kiss just now—it had been too fast. So fast she hadn't even had time to feel it.
Next time… next time, maybe linger a little longer?
She shook her head hard, flinging the dangerous thought out of her mind.
Su Qingyuan! What are you thinking! You only just made it official!

The next day, when Su Qingyuan arrived at the studio, she found something new by the door.
A plant stand.
Wrought iron, white, set neatly beside the door, already holding a pot of pothos and a bunch of white chamomile.

"Passed a flower shop this morning, picked these up on the way. No need to thank me. —Lu"
Su Qingyuan looked at the words "on the way," and remembered how yesterday he'd said "your eyes don't look like they're just admiring it" and then bought the flowers—and now today it was "on the way" again.
This man—just how many "on the ways" did he have?

She sat down at her worktable, opened her sketchbook, and tried to draw a new design. But the moment her pen tip touched the paper, her mind was full of nothing but his face.
She bit the cap of her pen, struggling to focus, and drew a few strokes on the paper—then looked down to find she'd drawn the line of a man's profile.
Su Qingyuan: "…"
She flipped past that page and started over.
This time, she drew the next piece in the "First Light" series. The inspiration came fast, her pen gliding across the paper, the lines smooth and certain.
As she drew, she suddenly stopped, and in the corner of the draft she wrote a small line of text:
"For Lu."
Once she'd written it, she felt it was too sappy and wanted to scribble it out. Her pen hovered above the paper—but in the end, she didn't.
Forget it.
He wouldn't see it anyway.
【System: But the system can see it, and will record it as future "sugar."】

Him leading her by the hand through the entrance. Her rising on her toes to kiss his cheek. Him smiling at her.
All of it captured.

"Another gold-digger climbing the ladder."

She and Lu Shiyan had made it official less than twenty-four hours ago, and already the entire internet had exposed them. This wasn't what they had planned—it wasn't even something they'd chosen to make public themselves.
Who took the photos? Why post them? What was the goal?

Lu Shiyan.
"You've seen it?" His voice was very calm—so calm it didn't quite seem like a normal reaction.

Su Qingyuan closed her eyes and drew a deep breath.
Lin Haoyu.
The man who'd knelt in the hotel lobby begging to get back together, whom she'd cursed back to where he came from.
The man who'd traded curses with Su Yurou over the phone, the two of them tearing each other apart.
Failing to win her back, he'd started his revenge.
Not revenge against Su Yurou—revenge against her.
Because he couldn't have her, he had to destroy her?

This man—while she was still panicking, still wondering "what do we do," had already finished cleaning up every last bit of the aftermath.

Just those two words.
Su Qingyuan gripped her phone, her palm breaking into a sweat.
Go public.
Not be secretly photographed, be exposed, be forced to admit it.
He was the one choosing to go public.
After everything blew up, he didn't choose to handle it quietly, didn't choose to deny it, didn't choose to "protect her" by hiding her away.
He chose—to stand beside her, and face it together.

Just one photo, and one line of text.
The photo was that moment last night when she'd kissed his cheek, the one that had been secretly captured. But he hadn't used the blurry image the marketing account had posted—he'd had someone pull the high-definition original from the surveillance footage.
The text was only a single sentence:
"I'm the one who asked for this. She isn't climbing the ladder."
A single short line, with no extra justification, none of the canned "please give us our space" lines.
Just one resounding declaration—"I'm the one who asked."
The comment section exploded instantly.
"Ahhhhh he's so bold!!!"

She reposted it, adding a line of her own:
"No ladder to climb. Just a person walking forward together with me."
The moment she sent it, her phone began buzzing wildly. Her follower count surged from a few thousand to several hundred thousand—private messages, comments, likes, the numbers leaping so fast they made her dizzy.
Zhou Wanyin was the first to comment: "Congratulations!!! Should the studio throw a celebration party?"

Even a few of the normally lofty industry heavyweights liked and reposted, one after another.

Su Qingyuan: 【A little.】
Lu Shiyan: 【Me too.】

Su Qingyuan: 【Then let's be nervous together.】
Lu Shiyan: 【Okay. Together.】
She set down her phone, walked to the window, and pushed it open.
The scent of osmanthus still lingered.
The late-autumn wind blew against her face, cool, but inside her chest it was warm.

Maybe that 1% wasn't a matter of not liking each other enough.
It was a certain moment—when they stood side by side before everyone, with nothing to hide and nothing to fear, neither groveling nor arrogant, and said "Yes, we're together"—
That moment was the 100%.

The system will keep you company, but it will no longer broadcast the affection level—because it's already full, and won't rise any higher. The rest is your own road to walk.】
Su Qingyuan read the system's closing words and suddenly felt a pang of reluctance.
This system, which from day one had nagged, snarked, thrown cold water, and secretly played wingman—was about to retreat behind the scenes.
In her heart, she quietly said: Thank you, System.

This man—nervous right up until they went public, and the moment it was official, he started dishing out sweet nothings.

Lu Shiyan: 【No. After meeting you, it just came to me, no teacher required.】
Su Qingyuan slapped her phone face-down on the desk and buried her face in both hands.
She was done for.
Completely done for.
In this life, she'd fallen straight into this man's hands.
【System: Told you long ago—you two are a perfect match.】
Su Qingyuan: Didn't you retreat behind the scenes?
【System: I pop out now and then to remind you I exist. All right, really retiring now. Be sweet, you two.】
Su Qingyuan shook her head with a laugh, picked up her phone again, and looked at that photo of the sunset and her chat window with Lu Shiyan. Her heart was full, as if something had packed it tight, fuller and fuller.
That something was called the certainty of being loved.
Not "maybe," not "a little."
Certainty.
The certainty she'd never once possessed in this life, now finally held firm in the palm of her hand.

Chapter 16 — Her Moment in the Spotlight, Witnessed by Him from Start to Finish
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626218.html

On the third day after Su Yurou got out, Su Qingyuan received an anonymous text.
"You think stepping on me means you've won? Sister Qingyuan, in all the years we've grown up together, when have you ever truly beaten me?"
There was no signature, but that form of address—in all the years they'd grown up together, only one person had ever called her that.
Su Qingyuan read it, deleted the message with a blank expression, and went back to the final stage of polishing "Daybreak."
She knew Su Yurou wouldn't let it go. But she knew something else even better: the woman she was now was no longer the girl who could be frightened by a single anonymous text.
"Who's messaging you?" Lu Shiyan sat on the sofa in the lounge area, a document in his hand, not even lifting his head.
"Spam," Su Qingyuan said lightly.
Lu Shiyan raised his eyes to her, his gaze lingering on her face for a second. He didn't press, just lowered his head back to the document.
But Su Qingyuan noticed that he turned the pages a little slower than before—he was thinking about something.
The polishing of "Daybreak" had entered its most critical phase. The three-layered halo of the moonstone had already taken shape, but that innermost touch of warm gold was never quite right—either too faint, faint to the point of being nearly invisible, or too thick, thick enough to smother the blue and white of the outer layers.
Su Qingyuan had already ruined five moonstones, each one worth a small fortune. It pained her to waste the material, and it pained her even more to waste the time.
"Where are you stuck?" Lu Shiyan had come to stand behind her at some point she hadn't noticed.
Su Qingyuan didn't turn around. She pointed at the moonstone under the magnifying glass. "The inner halo won't come out. The effect I want is 'the gradient of the sky at the very instant of daybreak, shifting from dark to light,' but right now it's either too dark or too bright."
Lu Shiyan watched for a few seconds, then suddenly said, "Have you tried changing the angle at which the blade enters? Instead of cutting from the front, cut in from the side, against the grain."
Su Qingyuan froze for a moment, then turned to look at him. "You know gem-cutting?"
"No." Lu Shiyan's expression was perfectly candid. "But I've read some material on it. The way you're cutting now follows the direction of the crystal structure, so the halo it produces is linear. If you go against the structure just a little, the light might refract out from within in different layers."
Su Qingyuan stared at him for three seconds, then turned, picked up a fresh moonstone, secured it, and adjusted the angle of the blade.
The first cut went in, and the change in the halo was visible to the naked eye.
It wasn't a linear gradient—it was a ring upon ring of light spreading outward from the core, like ripples.
That innermost touch of warm gold had finally come out.
Su Qingyuan's hands trembled faintly—not from nerves, but from exhilaration.
"Lu Shiyan, are you sure you don't know gem-cutting?"
"I'm sure."
"Then that suggestion you just made…"
"Logical reasoning." Lu Shiyan slid both hands into his pockets, his tone flat. "Cutting is essentially about controlling the path light refracts along inside the stone. Your problem was that the refraction path was singular—so you change the path. It's the same logic as making a business decision."
Su Qingyuan drew a deep breath, bent back down, and focused on driving the rest of the cut forward.
Lu Shiyan didn't say anything more. He went quietly back to the sofa and returned to his document.
The only sounds in the studio were the faint friction of tools against stone and the occasional birdsong drifting in from outside the window.
This state—each absorbed in their own work, undisturbed yet keeping each other company—was more reassuring than any sweet words could ever be.
Two hours later, Su Qingyuan straightened up, lifted "Daybreak" off the worktable, and cradled it in her palm.
Under the natural light, the moonstone revealed a perfect three-layered halo—the outer layer the deep blue of the hour before dawn, the middle layer the silver-white of daybreak itself, the inner layer the warm gold of the first ray of sunlight piercing through the clouds.
She turned it at an angle, and the three layers of halo seemed to come alive, slowly flowing, merging, separating—as though the entire passage of the sky from night to sunrise had been compressed into one small stone.
"It's done." There was a slight tremor in Su Qingyuan's voice.
Lu Shiyan walked over, lowered his head to look at the "Daybreak" in her palm, and was silent for a long time.
"Su Qingyuan." His voice was very low.
"Mm?"
"This piece is going to win an award."
Su Qingyuan looked up at him. The halo of the moonstone was reflected in his eyes, and those three layers of light seemed to settle into the depths of them too.
She suddenly felt that this moment was worth remembering more than any award.
The night "Daybreak" was finished, Su Qingyuan sent the photo to Zhou Wanyin.
Zhou Wanyin's reply was a voice message a full fifty-nine seconds long. Su Qingyuan opened it: the first fifteen seconds were silence, only the sound of rapid breathing, and then came Zhou Wanyin's voice, struggling to suppress her excitement:
"Qingyuan, I'm driving right now—when I saw your message I pulled over to the side of the road. This piece isn't 'going to win an award,' it's 'if it doesn't win, I'll flip the judging committee's table.' Send me the photo and the detailed materials. I'll submit the Biennale recommendation package tonight. Also, I want to arrange for a professional jewelry photographer to shoot the finished images of 'Daybreak.' When are you free?"
Su Qingyuan replied: [Anytime. Tomorrow works.]
Zhou Wanyin: [Then I'll have the photographer at your studio at ten tomorrow morning.]
At ten the next morning, the photographer arrived right on time.
He was a man in his early thirties, surname Lin, one of the most expensive jewelry photographers in the industry. For Zhou Wanyin to get him to come, she'd clearly spared no expense.
When Photographer Lin saw "Daybreak," the hand holding his camera paused.
"This halo…" He leaned in and studied it for a long while, then straightened up and said to Su Qingyuan, "Miss Su, I've been shooting jewelry for over a decade and I've never seen a cutting technique like this. Is it your own original work?"
"Yes."
"Does it have a name?"
Su Qingyuan thought for a moment. "Call it the 'Ripple Cut.'"
Because the halo spread outward from the core in ring after ring, just like ripples.
Photographer Lin nodded, asked nothing more, and began setting up the lighting to shoot.
The shoot went on for four hours. Photographer Lin cycled through seven different light sources and more than a dozen angles before he finally captured the most perfect rendering of "Daybreak's" halo.
He exported one raw frame on the spot for Su Qingyuan to see.
Su Qingyuan looked at the moonstone on the screen, glowing as if lit from within, was silent for a few seconds, then picked up her phone and sent the photo to Lu Shiyan.
The caption was just two words: [It's done.]
Lu Shiyan's reply was a screenshot—he'd set that very photo as his phone wallpaper.
Su Qingyuan stared at the screenshot, her ears turning red.
[System: Even though the affection level is already maxed out, the System still has to say this—this kind of quiet, sneaky sweetness is a hundred times more lethal than just saying "I love you."]
Su Qingyuan: …Didn't you say you were retiring to the background?
[System: For a scene this iconic, the System absolutely has to be here.]
---
At the same time Zhou Wanyin submitted the photo of "Daybreak" to the Biennale judging committee, she also posted it on her own social media.
The caption was extremely brief: "The latest work by my student Su Qingyuan, 'Daybreak.' Technique: original 'Ripple Cut.' I won't say much—see for yourselves."
Within an hour of that post going up, the shares broke ten thousand and the comments broke thirty thousand.
The industry blew up.
"Ripple Cut? Never heard of a cutting method like this."
"I zoomed in and looked for ten minutes. This kind of layered halo isn't something ordinary cutting can achieve."
"Zhou Wanyin's student? No wonder."
"It's not 'no wonder'—it's that Zhou Wanyin got lucky and stumbled onto a gem."
"Su Qingyuan—isn't that the one who went public with Lu Shiyan? I thought she got into the industry through connections, but turns out she's actually got real talent."
"Can connections get you an original cutting technique? Cut one and show me, then."
The tide in the comments section turned from doubt to recognition in less than half a day.
And those who had once followed the marketing accounts in calling Su Qingyuan a "plagiarist" quietly deleted their comments and pretended nothing had ever happened.
Su Qingyuan didn't bother scrolling through those comments. She sat in her studio, and before her, all seven pieces of the now-completed "First Light" series were lined up in a row across the worktable.
From "Breaking the Cocoon" to "Daybreak"—seven pieces, seven stories, strung together they traced her entire journey climbing from the abyss to the summit.
She took a group photo and posted to Weibo:
"The 'First Light' series, seven pieces, all complete. From conception to finished work, it took twenty-three days in total. Over these twenty-three days, I lost some things, and gained even more. Thank you to everyone who walked through it with me. The date for the series launch will be announced shortly."
The attached image was a family portrait of all seven pieces.
Within ten minutes of that Weibo post going up, the likes broke half a million.
The comments were a uniform chorus demanding the launch, demanding the presale, demanding more work.
Su Qingyuan read through them one by one, the curve of her lips growing wider and wider.
She set down her phone, walked to the window, and pushed it open.
The scent of osmanthus had already faded—at this time of year, the osmanthus was nearly done blooming.
But the sunlight was still there.
It fell on her face, warm.
Her phone buzzed.
Lu Shiyan: [For the launch venue, I had someone prepare a few options. Pick one.]
Su Qingyuan: [When did you secretly start preparing the launch too?]
Lu Shiyan: [From the day you started making "Daybreak." I knew you'd make it the best it could be, so I prepared a stage worthy of it in advance.]
Su Qingyuan looked at those words and drew a deep breath.
This man—he always had everything arranged before she'd even opened her mouth.
She chose one of the options—the Chengnan Arts Center, the place she'd passed by countless times, looked up at countless times, yet had never once stepped inside.
Su Qingyuan: [Decided. The Chengnan Arts Center.]
Lu Shiyan: [Good. Leave the rest to me.]
That phrase again.
"Leave the rest to me."
From that rainy night until now, she'd long since lost count of how many times he'd said it.
But every time she heard it, she felt that—however vast this world was, however many storms it held, she was never alone.
---
The launch was set for two weeks later.
Over those two weeks, Su Qingyuan was so busy her feet barely touched the ground. The launch run-of-show, the media invitations, the work-display layout, the on-site security, the guest list… every single thing required her review and confirmation.
Lu Shiyan reassigned an entire team from Lu Group's PR division to help, but Su Qingyuan insisted on personally overseeing every detail.
"This is my first series launch," she told Lu Shiyan. "I have to watch over it myself."
Lu Shiyan didn't object. He simply showed up at the studio door at ten o'clock sharp every night to take her home.
One day she worked until three in the morning, and when she came out of the studio, she found his car still there.
She walked over and knocked on the window. It rolled down. His eyes were threaded with red, but when he saw her, he still smiled.
"Why didn't you just go home first?" Su Qingyuan felt a pang of tenderness.
"I said I'd pick you up."
"You could've just texted to say it was too late and I'd take a cab home myself."
Lu Shiyan glanced at her, his voice very soft. "Su Qingyuan, every word I've ever said counts."
Su Qingyuan got into the passenger seat, buckled her seatbelt, didn't look at him, but her voice was a little muffled. "You're going to spoil me like this."
Lu Shiyan started the car, the corner of his mouth lifting slightly. "Spoiling you is exactly the point. If no one else can stand you, then you'll have no choice but to stay by my side."
Su Qingyuan turned to glare at him. He kept his eyes on the road ahead, his expression perfectly solemn.
But that little curve at the corner of his mouth gave him away.
[System: This man—saying "spoiling you is exactly the point" with his mouth, while in reality wishing the whole world would dote on her. Saying one thing and meaning another—he learned that from the female lead.]
Su Qingyuan: System, can you not over-analyze everything?
[System: The System's reading-comprehension ability is a perfect score. There's no need to "over-analyze."]
---
The day of the launch.
The Chengnan Arts Center, the main exhibition hall.
Su Qingyuan stood backstage, peering through a gap in the curtain at the audience below.
Not a seat was empty.
Those who'd come weren't just media and industry insiders—there were also plenty of ordinary visitors who'd bought tickets on their own just to see the exhibition. The launch tickets had sold out within ten minutes of going on sale; when Su Qingyuan heard the news, she'd thought she'd misheard.
In the front row below, Zhou Wanyin sat dead center, flanked by several heavyweights from the jewelry world—people Su Qingyuan had only ever seen in magazine photos.
In the second row sat reporters from more than a dozen mainstream and specialist jewelry outlets, their lenses long and short all trained on the stage.
And at the very back of the hall, in an inconspicuous corner, stood a man in a black suit.
Lu Shiyan.
He hadn't taken a seat in the front row. He hadn't claimed a prominent spot by the title of "Su Qingyuan's boyfriend." He hadn't even told anyone he'd be coming.
He simply stood there, like a silent mountain.
Through the gap in the curtain, Su Qingyuan saw him.
She drew a deep breath, turned, and said to the staff, "I'm ready."
The lights dimmed.
A single spotlight fell on the center of the stage.
Su Qingyuan walked out from behind the curtain, wearing a simple black dress, her hair pinned up to reveal the slender line of her neck. She wore no jewelry at all—because today the star wasn't her; it was her work.
She walked to the center of the stage, picked up the microphone, and the room fell silent.
"Thank you all for coming today to the launch of the 'First Light' series."
Her voice wasn't loud, but it was steady, carrying through the sound system to every corner of the hall.
"The name of this series comes from a very important turning point in my life. Before it, I was always in the dark. After it, I began to see light."
She paused, her gaze drifting unconsciously toward that corner at the back of the hall.
Lu Shiyan stood there, hands in his pockets, looking at her across an entire sea of people.
"This series has seven pieces in total, each corresponding to one of the seven stages of my journey from darkness into light. They weren't conjured out of thin air—they are my autobiography."
The hall was utterly silent.
Su Qingyuan pressed the remote in her hand, and the large screen behind her lit up. The high-definition photo of the first piece, "Breaking the Cocoon," appeared on the display.
"The first piece, 'Breaking the Cocoon.'" Her voice was calm and powerful. "The inspiration came from the moment I made up my mind to leave the place that had trapped me for more than a decade. The dark tones of the opal represent the abyss; the diamond wings around it represent the strength to break free."
She introduced them one by one—the source of inspiration, the creative process, the technical difficulties of each piece, all laid out clearly.
When she reached the last piece, she paused.
The photo of "Daybreak" appeared on the large screen.
The moonstone's three-layered halo shifted under the lens, like a true dawn.
"This piece is called 'Daybreak,'" Su Qingyuan's voice softened, "the final piece of the 'First Light' series, and the one I treasure most. Its core technique is an entirely new way of cutting moonstone, which I call the 'Ripple Cut.' This cutting technique was completed with the inspiration of… one particular person."
In the audience, Zhou Wanyin arched an eyebrow and smiled knowingly.
Su Qingyuan didn't look toward that corner, but her voice was a little softer than before, a little gentler too:
"The core logic of the 'Ripple Cut' is to change the refraction path of light. I used to always follow a single direction, walking straight into a dead end without ever knowing to turn. It was someone who reminded me—maybe if I changed direction, the light would shine in from a different angle."
She raised her head and finally looked toward the back of the hall.
Lu Shiyan stood there, perfectly still.
Across that great distance, Su Qingyuan couldn't make out his expression, but she could see the hand hanging at his side, the fingertips curling slightly.
"So, 'Daybreak' isn't only my daybreak," Su Qingyuan's voice grew a little hoarse, but she held it steady, "it's also the daybreak we lit together."
The audience was silent for an instant, and then thunderous applause erupted.
Su Qingyuan bowed deeply. When she straightened up, there were tears glistening at the corners of her eyes, but she didn't wipe them away.
The lights came back up.
Staff wheeled the seven pieces out from backstage and arranged them in glass display cases at the center of the hall.
The audience surged forward, crowding around the cases, camera flashes going off one after another, gasps of wonder, the buzz of discussion, the click of shutters all merging into one.
Su Qingyuan stood at the edge of the stage, watching it all, and was suddenly struck by an overwhelming sense of unreality.
Twenty-three days ago, she'd still been sitting on a hotel floor, staring blankly at an utterly empty bank account.
Twenty-three days later, she stood in Nancheng's most prestigious arts center, presenting her work to the whole world.
And the one person she most wanted to thank was, at this very moment, making his way toward her from the back of the hall, through the crowd.
The crowd parted to make a path of its own accord.
Not because they'd recognized him as Lu Shiyan—though some genuinely had—but because the aura around him was too powerful, so powerful that no one dared stand in his way.
He walked up to Su Qingyuan and stopped.
The two of them stood face to face, surrounded by the clamoring crowd, the flashing lights, the rise and fall of conversation.
But in his world there was only her.
"You spoke beautifully," he said, his voice low enough for only her to hear.
Su Qingyuan looked up at him, tears glistening in her eyes, and a smile too. "You were standing in the back the whole time? Why didn't you sit in the front row?"
"The front row is reserved for your career," Lu Shiyan said, lowering his head to look at her, undisguised affection in the depths of his eyes. "The back row is reserved for your person."
Su Qingyuan finally couldn't hold back, and the tears fell.
Lu Shiyan didn't say "don't cry," nor did he wipe her tears for her.
He simply took a step forward, came to stand at her side, his shoulder lightly brushing hers.
Then he turned his head, his voice low as if meant for her ears alone:
"Su Qingyuan, you're beautiful today. Not because of how well you're dressed, but because of the way you're standing here—you earned this yourself."
Su Qingyuan sniffled, wiped the tears away with the pad of her finger, and turned her head to glance at him.
"Lu Shiyan, could you not always say things like this at moments like this? My makeup's going to run."
Lu Shiyan glanced at her, the corner of his mouth lifting slightly. "You're not wearing any makeup."
Su Qingyuan: "…"
She really wasn't wearing makeup. Today had been too busy—there'd been no time at all.
Lu Shiyan let out a soft laugh and said nothing more.
He turned to face the crowd and stood at her side—not "standing in front of her to protect her," not "standing behind her to silently support her," but—shoulder to shoulder.
Like two trees growing side by side, roots entwined underground, branches and leaves touching in the wind, each independent, yet supporting the other.
[System: The affection level is already maxed out, so the System won't be broadcasting anymore. But the System wants to say one thing: this is the best ending. No—it's not an ending. It's a beginning.]
In her heart, Su Qingyuan silently said to the System: Thank you.
[System: You're welcome. The System will always be here. Even though it won't broadcast the affection level anymore, it'll always be watching over the two of you. All right, enough sentimentality. Today's launch was a great success. Congratulations, Designer Su.]
Su Qingyuan curved her lips into a smile.
The launch lasted three hours.
When it ended, Su Qingyuan received three things:
A formal shortlist notification from the Biennale organizing committee—"Daybreak" had passed the preliminary selection and advanced to the final round of evaluation.
A letter of intent for collaboration from a certain international jewelry brand, hoping she'd become the brand's first Chinese partner designer.
And one photo.
It was taken by Lu Shiyan, on his phone, of the launch in progress—she stood at the center of the stage, the spotlight falling on her, microphone in hand, her eyes full of light.
Below the photo was a single line:
"My designer."
Su Qingyuan stared at that line for a long time, then saved the photo and set it as her own phone wallpaper.
She sent a screenshot of the wallpaper to Lu Shiyan.
Lu Shiyan's reply came quickly:
[Stealing my photo?]
Su Qingyuan: [What do you mean, stealing? You shot me—the copyright belongs to me.]
Lu Shiyan: [Fair point. Then I'll buy the copyright. Name your price.]
Su Qingyuan: [You can't afford it.]
Lu Shiyan: [Want to bet?]
Su Qingyuan: [What I want isn't money.]
Lu Shiyan: [Then what do you want?]
Su Qingyuan looked at that question, thought for a long while, typed out a line, then deleted it character by character, and in the end only replied with two words:
[Guess.]
Lu Shiyan didn't volley "Guess" back at her to play along with the game.
He replied with three words:
[I know.]
Su Qingyuan stared at those words—"I know"—and her heartbeat suddenly quickened.
He said he knew.
Knew what?
She'd said "Guess," and he'd said "I know."
Which meant—he didn't need to guess. He'd known all along.
Su Qingyuan set her phone face-down on the table and buried her face in both hands.
She was done for.
This man—he could even hear the words she'd never spoken aloud.
Outside the window, the night in Nancheng had already grown deep.
But Su Qingyuan felt that the sky had already been bright for a very long time.

========================================

Chapter 17 — Undercurrents at the Biennale, and She Meets Them with Composure
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626219.html

Three days after the launch, the news became official: "Daybreak" had made the final shortlist of the Biennale.
Announced alongside it were the other eleven shortlisted pieces. Twelve works, from nine countries and regions — and Su Qingyuan was the youngest designer among them, and the only one to make the cut as an independent designer.
Beneath the official announcement, the comment section was as lively as a festival.
"Su Qingyuan is incredible!!! The Ripple Cut has finally been recognized internationally!"
"The only Asian among the twelve works — go for it!!"
"Wait — look at that piece on the shortlist, 'Undertow' — the designer is Su Yurou???"
That comment dropped like a depth charge and blew the whole thread wide open.
Su Qingyuan saw it while she was brewing tea in her studio. Her fingers froze, and she tapped open the shortlist to read it carefully.
"Undertow," designer: Su Yurou (China).
Her pupils contracted slightly.
Su Yurou. The one who'd been out of detention for less than a week. The one the entire industry had spat on, the one the brands had cut ties with, the one the whole internet had mocked.
She had made the Biennale final shortlist.
Su Qingyuan set down her phone, carried her teacup to the window, and took a slow sip.
Something was off.
She knew Su Yurou's design ability better than anyone — shaky fundamentals, mediocre creativity, and the only "talent" she had was stealing other people's work. Even if she'd studied like a madwoman after landing in detention, there was no way she could have produced a piece worthy of the Biennale shortlist in such a short span of time.
Unless that piece wasn't hers.
Su Qingyuan put down the teacup and dialed Zhou Wanyin.
"Wanyin-jie, have you seen the shortlist?"
"I have." Zhou Wanyin's voice was heavy. "I'm looking into it now. Su Yurou's piece, 'Undertow' — there's no prior public record of it anywhere. It just appeared out of nowhere and went straight into Biennale review. Something's wrong here."
"Can you find out who her sponsor was?"
"I'm digging." Zhou Wanyin paused. "Qingyuan, there's something I have to tell you — on the Biennale's judging committee, there's a juror who's a distant relative of Su Yurou's mother, Liu Xiulan. I'm not saying there's definitely something shady going on, but that connection is enough to put me on guard."
Su Qingyuan closed her eyes, her mind racing.
"Wanyin-jie, can you help me get hold of the materials for 'Undertow'? I don't need detailed specs — just the style, the craftsmanship, the theme."
"I'll try. But the review materials are confidential. I can only ask around through personal contacts, and I might not get anything."
"All right. Thank you for the trouble."
After hanging up, Su Qingyuan stood at the window, looking at the osmanthus tree outside. Most of the blossoms had already fallen, leaving only a few sparse clusters, but the fragrance lingered, faint and elusive.
Her phone buzzed.
Lu Shiyan: [Saw the shortlist. I've got people looking into the Su Yurou matter.]
Su Qingyuan: [How did you know I was thinking about it right now?]
Lu Shiyan: [Because whatever you're thinking, you write it into your silences.]
Su Qingyuan looked at the line of text and curved her lips. She put down the phone, sat back at her workbench, and picked up her carving knife.
No matter what tricks Su Yurou pulled, there was only one thing she could do — polish her own work to perfection.
Let the work speak for itself.
The rest, she'd leave to time, and to Lu Shiyan.
Three days later, Zhou Wanyin came with news.
"I got it. A friend of mine in the judging committee secretariat secretly photographed the brief for 'Undertow' and sent it to me." She handed her phone to Su Qingyuan, her expression complicated. "See for yourself."
Su Qingyuan took it, and after a single glance her fingers tightened.
The centerpiece of "Undertow" was a black opal, and the cutting method was… the Ripple Cut.
Not "similar." Not "inspired by." It was completely, identically, the Ripple Cut.
The halo radiated outward from the core in ring after ring, three graduated layers — deep blue on the outer ring, silver-white in the middle, warm gold at the core.
Exactly like "Daybreak."
But "Undertow" was darker, more oppressive in its overall design. The black opal's base tone swallowed most of the halo, leaving only that inner warm gold like the last breath escaping a throttled throat.
The piece's description read: "Undertow is the last light at the bottom of the abyss. Not everyone is worthy of seeing it."
Su Qingyuan stared at that line, her fingers trembling slightly.
Not out of fear. Out of fury.
Su Yurou had stolen her craft.
Not stolen a design — a design could be imitated. But the Ripple Cut's cutting parameters, the angle of the blade's entry, the sequence of polishing — those were core techniques she'd worked out by ruining more than thirty pieces of moonstone. She hadn't applied for a patent, because the technique was too novel and the patent process took too long, and she couldn't afford to wait.
Su Yurou must have gotten hold of her craft parameters some way or other.
"How did she do it?" Su Qingyuan's voice was cold.
Zhou Wanyin's face wasn't pleasant either. "I checked the timeline. The day you finished 'Daybreak,' photographer Lin came to shoot the finished piece. Was your studio door unlocked that day?"
Su Qingyuan thought back, and her expression changed abruptly.
That day photographer Lin had come to shoot, hauling equipment in and out, and she really hadn't locked the studio door. And photographer Lin's assistant — she remembered a young girl, wearing a mask, hardly speaking, always tidying gear in the corner.
"That assistant."
"I suspect her too." Zhou Wanyin nodded. "Photographer Lin told me afterward that the assistant was someone he'd hired on short notice. Her résumé said she was a photography student, but she only worked one day and then vanished. The phone number was a burner — no identity could be traced."
Su Qingyuan closed her eyes and took a deep breath.
A setup. It had started back then.
Su Yurou hadn't been idle in detention — she'd been planning. Before she got out, she'd already had someone lay the trap. That assistant had obtained the finished details of "Daybreak," and may even have secretly photographed Su Qingyuan's technical notes on the Ripple Cut sitting on her workbench.
Then, in the shortest possible time, Su Yurou had reproduced a piece and submitted it just before the Biennale registration deadline.
She knew Su Qingyuan's "Daybreak" was certain to make the shortlist. What she wanted wasn't to win — it was to compete on the same stage. To stand on the same platform as Su Qingyuan, in front of the whole world.
Lose, and she'd be "the newcomer who lost but is still very impressive." Win, and she'd turn everything around completely, climbing back up by stepping on Su Qingyuan.
No matter how you ran the numbers, she came out ahead.
"Wanyin-jie, do the Biennale's judging criteria have any rules about originality of craft?"
"They do. If two pieces use the same original technique, the committee will investigate who the technique originally belongs to. Whoever created it earlier is the originator." Zhou Wanyin paused. "Is your record of 'Daybreak's' creative process complete?"
"Complete. From the first sketch to every step of the process, I have timestamped records."
Zhou Wanyin let out a breath of relief. "Good. Get the materials ready and I'll help you submit them to the committee. Su Yurou likes playing dirty, doesn't she? Then let the international judges decide who the real originator is."
Su Qingyuan nodded, opened her laptop, and began compiling the creative archive of "Daybreak."
From the first crude concept sketch, to the first experimental log of the Ripple Cut, to the parameter log of the thirty-first successful experiment, to the final photographs and videos of the finished piece. Every entry had a timestamp precise to the second, and some even carried system-generated proof of time — although she couldn't reveal the System's existence, the timestamps it generated were blockchain-grade and impossible to tamper with.
She was halfway through compiling when Lu Shiyan arrived.
He didn't knock; he pushed the door open and walked straight in — Su Qingyuan had given him a key, and he was the only one who had one.
"Compiling evidence?" He glanced at her screen, unsurprised.
"You already know about Su Yurou?"
"I know. I tracked down that assistant's real identity." Lu Shiyan set a USB drive on the desk. "Her name is Chen Xiaoman. She's the younger sister of Su Yurou's college roommate. On the third day Su Yurou was in detention, Chen Xiaoman started submitting her résumé on job sites, specifically targeting temporary positions related to jewelry photography. She was aiming for photographer Lin's team, because Lin is acknowledged in the industry as the top jewelry photographer — Su Qingyuan was bound to hire him."
Su Qingyuan looked at the USB drive and was silent for a few seconds.
"You're saying that even while she was in detention, Su Yurou was already plotting all of this?"
"Phones aren't allowed in detention, but she could see her lawyer. Her lawyer visited twice a week." Lu Shiyan's voice was cold. "She passed information through her lawyer and had people on the outside carry it out."
Su Qingyuan leaned back in her chair, gazing at the ceiling, and suddenly laughed.
"Lu Shiyan, do you think that if she'd put all this scheming into honest work, she'd have become a master long ago?"
"No." Lu Shiyan sat down across from her. "People who bend their cleverness the wrong way can never become masters. Because a master needs more than intelligence — they need integrity. She has none."
Su Qingyuan looked at him, and the resentment in her chest suddenly dissolved.
That was true. She had no integrity. So even if she made a hundred pieces with the same technique, she would never be a master.
Because what she'd stolen would always be stolen.
"I'll finish compiling the materials tonight and submit them to the committee tomorrow." Su Qingyuan sat up straight again. "There's still a month until the Biennale final. In that month, I'll file for a provisional patent on the Ripple Cut's craft parameters. At least internationally, I'll establish originality first."
Lu Shiyan nodded. "I'll arrange the legal side for you."
"All right." Su Qingyuan didn't refuse this time. For this, she really did need his help.
The appearance of "Undertow" caused no small tremor within the industry.
It wasn't an official announcement — someone had seen the shortlist on the Biennale organizing committee's website, spotted Su Yurou's name, screenshotted it, and posted it online.
The hashtag #SuYurouShortlistedforBiennale shot up the trending list.
The comments were sharply divided.
"Didn't she just get out of detention? How can she still enter an international competition?"
"Detention and competing don't conflict — it wasn't a criminal conviction. Legally she only got administrative detention."
"The point is her work! Wasn't she caught dead to rights stealing Su Qingyuan's designs? This piece had better not be stolen again."
"Can you all stop trashing Yurou for everything? She's a victim too — wasn't the earlier thing reversed?"
"What reversal? The court verdict is out — malicious false accusation. Can't you read Chinese?"
"But if this piece really is her own work, that means she does have talent."
"Whether she has talent or not, we'll know once the final results are out."
Su Qingyuan didn't join the online debate. She turned off all her social media notifications, shut herself in the studio, and started on something new.
Not designing a new piece.
Writing a letter.
A letter to the Biennale judging committee.
There were no accusations in it, no denunciations, no emotional language. She simply stated a fact, objectively: the Ripple Cut was a cutting technique she had originated, and its creative process was fully documented with timestamps. Su Yurou's "Undertow" used the same technique, and was created later than her "Daybreak."
She attached an index of all the evidence and formally requested that, in the final round, the committee conduct an independent assessment of the originality of the craft in both pieces.
At the end of the letter, she wrote this:
"I am not accusing Su Yurou of plagiarism. I am only stating a fact: this technique is something I ground out, bit by bit, a month ago, in an eighty-square-meter studio. If it appears on another piece, I hope the committee can confirm whether the creator of that piece obtained my authorization. Thank you."
No drawn swords, no aggression.
Just the facts laid out, for professionals to make a professional judgment.
After reading the letter, Zhou Wanyin was silent for a long time, then said one thing: "This letter has more power than any accusation."
Su Qingyuan handed the letter to Zhou Wanyin, who, as the sponsor, would forward it to the committee.
Then she went back to work.
As if nothing had happened.
Of course Su Yurou wouldn't quietly wait for the verdict.
On the third day after the letter was submitted, Su Qingyuan received a long message from a new number — but the tone was one she knew far too well.
"Qingyuan-jie, did you write a letter to the committee? Do you think that just because you drew up the Ripple Cut first, the technique is yours? Did you know someone did a similar halo cut before you? You're not the originator — you just got lucky and found that angle first. I was only a little later than you. Make a big scene of this, and in the end you're the one who'll lose face."
Su Qingyuan read it and replied without expression:
"Su Yurou, do you have evidence that you independently developed the Ripple Cut? If not, I'll see you in court."
The other side fell silent.
Su Qingyuan put down her phone and went on polishing the moonstone in her hand.
She didn't tell Su Yurou that she'd already had Lu Shiyan's legal team prepare the litigation materials. If, after the Biennale's verdict came out, Su Yurou was found to have infringed, she would sue directly.
Not because she hated Su Yurou.
But because the Ripple Cut was something she'd ground out over thirty-some moonstones, through countless sleepless nights, with Lu Shiyan's inspiration. It deserved to be protected.
Just as her life deserved to be respected.
A month passed quickly amid all the busyness.
The day before the Biennale final, Su Qingyuan flew to the host city of the exhibition — Paris.
Lu Shiyan went with her. He cleared all his work and flew more than ten hours just to accompany her.
On the plane, Su Qingyuan leaned on his shoulder, gazing out the window at the sea of clouds, and suddenly said, "Lu Shiyan, have you ever thought about what we'd do if I don't win anything at this Biennale?"
"No." Lu Shiyan's voice came from above her head, low and steady.
"Why not?"
"Because you will win." He paused. "Not because I blindly believe in you. Because 'Daybreak' deserves it. No matter how the committee judges, its value won't change. Your value won't change."
Su Qingyuan closed her eyes and curved her lips.
"Lu Shiyan, you're starting to sound more and more like an inspirational influencer."
"You become like the company you keep."
"And who's the good company?"
"You."
Su Qingyuan laughed and gave him a light punch, but didn't lift her head from his shoulder.
The plane passed through the clouds, and sunlight came flooding in, falling over the two of them.
Through more than ten hours of flying, she didn't feel tired.
Because he was there.
On the day of the final, the Grand Palais in Paris.
Su Qingyuan stood in the exhibition hall, looking at the twelve shortlisted pieces lined up in a row, each carefully displayed in its own glass case — the lighting, the angles, the backdrops all meticulously designed to present the work's beauty to the fullest.
"Daybreak" was in the very center of the hall.
Under the professional lighting, its three layers of halo flowed and shimmered, as if dawn itself had truly been sealed inside a stone.
"Undertow" was at the other end of the hall. Under the lights, the black opal looked deep and oppressive, the Ripple Cut's halo mostly swallowed by the black base, leaving only that inner thread of warm gold, like a cornered beast's struggle.
Su Qingyuan stood for a while before the case holding "Undertow."
She had to admit Su Yurou's design concept had its bright spots — using darkness to devour light, leaving only a sliver of life. That theme formed a stark contrast with the "breaking out of darkness" of her own "Daybreak."
One was "light coming out of dark."
The other was "dark devouring light, leaving only the last trace."
If the Ripple Cut had been Su Yurou's own, Su Qingyuan might even have admired this piece.
A pity it wasn't.
"Ms. Su."
An unfamiliar voice came from behind her.
Su Qingyuan turned and saw a blonde woman in her fifties, wearing a sharply tailored gray suit, with the Biennale judging committee's badge pinned to her chest.
"I'm the chair of the judging committee, Isabelle Morillet." The woman spoke in English, her gaze settling on Su Qingyuan with scrutiny, and with appreciation. "I read the letter you wrote. The committee conducted an independent assessment of the Ripple Cut's originality, and the result is in."
Su Qingyuan's heartbeat quickened, but her face stayed calm. "And what is the result?"
Isabelle looked at her and suddenly smiled.
"The result is — the Ripple Cut is yours. All the evidence points to you. The timestamps, the creative logs, the evolution of the craft parameters — irrefutable." She paused. "And Ms. Su Yurou could provide no evidence whatsoever that she independently developed this technique."
Su Qingyuan said nothing, waiting for the "but."
Sure enough, Isabelle's tone shifted. "But the committee has decided to retain 'Undertow's' shortlist qualification and not revoke its right to compete. There are two reasons. First, Ms. Su Yurou's lawyer submitted a statement claiming she 'drew reference' from your technique without knowing, and that it was not malicious plagiarism. Second, the committee feels that although the two pieces use the same technique, their design concepts are entirely different and can be evaluated separately."
Su Qingyuan was silent for a few seconds, then nodded. "I understand. Thank you for telling me this."
Isabelle looked at her, a flicker of surprise in her eyes. "You're not angry?"
"Anger doesn't solve problems." Su Qingyuan said calmly. "The committee has its rules, and I respect them. But I reserve the right to pursue my claim afterward."
Isabelle gave her a long, deep look, nodded, and turned to leave.
Su Qingyuan stayed where she was, watching the crowd flow back and forth through the hall, and took a deep breath.
She wasn't angry.
She just felt that — the fact that Su Yurou's lawyer could submit that statement meant there was a master strategist behind her. That person had told her not to go head-to-head, to "admit fault but not guilt," to blur the lines with "drawing reference," making it hard for the committee to come down hard.
It was a clever move. Very clever.
"What are you thinking about?" Lu Shiyan walked up beside her.
Su Qingyuan turned her head to look at him. "Thinking about who's helping Su Yurou behind the scenes."
Lu Shiyan's gaze flickered slightly. "I'm looking into it too. No clear result yet, but there's one lead — Su Yurou changed lawyers. The new lawyer's surname is Fang. He's a partner at a mid-sized law firm in Nancheng, specializing in intellectual property. Behind that firm is the shadow of an investment company, and that investment company…"
He paused.
"Is connected to you?" Su Qingyuan asked.
"It has nothing to do with me." Lu Shiyan's voice dropped. "But it has something to do with a competitor of the Lu Group."
Su Qingyuan's heart sank.
This was no longer just Su Yurou's personal revenge.
Someone was using Su Yurou as a blade to stab at Lu Shiyan.
Because she was Lu Shiyan's girlfriend. To strike at her was to strike at Lu Shiyan.
"Lu Shiyan, this matter—"
"Leave it to me." Lu Shiyan cut her off, his voice soft but firm. "You go and claim your award. I'll handle the rest."
Su Qingyuan looked at him and wanted to say "we'll handle it together," but seeing the look in his eyes, she didn't say it.
That look told her: there were some storms he was determined to shield her from.
Even when she herself wanted to charge into them.
The award ceremony began at eight in the evening.
The main exhibition hall of the Grand Palais had been transformed into a ceremony venue — the lighting, the sound, the stage, every detail breathing French elegance and grandeur.
Su Qingyuan wore a champagne-colored gown, her hair swept up, revealing her delicate collarbones and that pair of "First Snow" earrings — her own design.
Lu Shiyan sat in the second row of the audience, off to the side. He didn't take a seat in the front row, because that row was reserved for the award winners and the committee. He didn't want to occupy a seat that might belong to an industry professional simply as "family."
Su Qingyuan waited backstage, her phone in her hand, the screen showing a message Lu Shiyan had sent five minutes earlier:
[Don't be nervous. You're already a winner. No matter the result.]
She replied with a single word: [Mm.]
The host took the stage, delivering remarks alternately in French and English. The ceremony officially began.
The awards started with the bronze.
The bronze medalist was an Italian designer, whose work was an ocean-themed sapphire brooch. Applause filled the hall.
The silver medalist was a veteran Japanese designer, whose work was a necklace set themed on the four seasons. The applause grew warmer still.
The gold.
The whole hall fell quiet.
The host opened the envelope, glanced at it, and a meaningful smile spread across his face.
"The gold medalist is—"
"Su Qingyuan, from China! For her work, 'Daybreak'!"
A "buzz" went off in Su Qingyuan's head.
She heard the applause, heard her own name, heard the congratulations of the people around her. But she didn't move.
It wasn't until a staff member gave her a gentle nudge that she came back to herself, took a deep breath, and walked up onto the stage.
The spotlight chased her, every step landing in light.
She took the trophy from the host's hands — a transparent crystal sculpture carved with the Biennale's emblem, heavy, pressing down into her palm, as if pressing down all her effort and persistence.
"Please share your acceptance speech," the host said with a smile.
Su Qingyuan stood at the microphone, looking out at the dense crowd below.
She saw Zhou Wanyin in the front row, her eyes red, clapping with all her might.
She saw the industry people who had once doubted her, mocked her, said she'd "risen on connections" — all of them now standing to applaud.
She saw, in a corner at the very back of the hall, Lu Shiyan standing there.
He hadn't taken his seat in the second row. He'd stood up and gone to the very back. Because from that angle — farthest from the stage, yet closest to her — he could see the whole of her, unblocked by anyone's back.
Across the entire length of the auditorium, their eyes met.
Su Qingyuan curved her lips and said into the microphone:
"Thank you to the committee, thank you to the Biennale. Thank you to everyone who has helped me. Thank you to my teacher, Zhou Wanyin — without her trust, I wouldn't be standing here."
She paused, her voice softening:
"And finally, thank you to one person. He never drew a single line of my designs, never polished a single stone for me, but he shielded me from every storm, so that I could sit quietly in that eighty-square-meter studio and carve the light in my heart, bit by bit, into stone."
"This piece is called 'Daybreak.' He is my daybreak."
The applause below thundered.
Su Qingyuan bowed deeply, and as she straightened, the tears finally fell.
She didn't wipe them away, letting them slide down her cheeks.
Because this time, they were tears of joy.
The joy she had earned, the joy she deserved, joy that was hers in the full light of day.
After the ceremony, Su Qingyuan was surrounded by a swarm of reporters.
The camera flashes nearly blinded her, and the questions surged over her like a tide:
"Ms. Su, what does the gold medal mean to you?"
"Will the Ripple Cut become your patent?"
"What are your thoughts on Su Yurou's 'Undertow'?"
Su Qingyuan answered each one, neither humble nor haughty, neither dodging nor provoking.
The last question came from a Chinese reporter: "Ms. Su, is there anything you'd like to say to Su Yurou? If she happens to be listening right now."
Su Qingyuan was silent for a second, looked into the camera, and said in a calm voice:
"Su Yurou, if you're listening — the Ripple Cut is mine. You can keep using it, but remember this: it's something I ground out over thirty-some moonstones, through countless sleepless nights, with one person's inspiration. You can steal the craft, but you can't steal my time, you can't steal my persistence, you can't steal every drop of sweat I shed in that studio. Any work you make with my technique will always carry my shadow. That's not your light. That's the dark inside my light."
Those words were relayed back home in real time and instantly set every social media platform ablaze.
The hashtags #SuQingyuanGoldMedalSpeech and #SuQingyuanSaysThatsTheDarkInsideMyLight shot up to first and second on the trending list at the same time.
The comments were overwhelmingly in Su Qingyuan's favor:
"So fierce!!! This is the confidence of the real deal!"
"Stolen craft is stolen craft — no amount of spin can wash it clean."
"What's Su Yurou going to do now? Still dare to call herself the originator?"
"That last line of Su Qingyuan's — 'that's the dark inside my light' — devastating. Even when educated people throw shade, they do it with this much class."
When Su Yurou saw those words, she was in a rented room in Nancheng.
She stared at her phone screen, lips pressed into a thin line, her face pale as paper.
Lawyer Fang sent a message: [Don't respond. Don't post anything. Wait for word from me.]
Su Yurou threw her phone onto the sofa and buried her face in both hands.
She'd lost.
She'd lost again.
But she didn't cry.
Because Lawyer Fang had said — "Winning or losing isn't settled in a single hand. As long as you're still at the table, there's a chance to turn it around."
She lowered her hands, picked up her phone, and replied to Lawyer Fang: [Understood. What's the next move?]
Lawyer Fang's reply came quickly: [Wait. Wait for the heat to die down. Wait for Su Qingyuan to slip.]
Su Yurou looked at the line of text and slowly curved her lips.
Wait.
What she was best at was waiting.
All her life, she had waited — waited more than ten years, waited for every concession from Su Qingyuan, every softening of her heart, every time she'd been trampled underfoot.
This time, too, she could wait.
Su Qingyuan, just you wait.
Your light will dim one day.
And my dark will be there, on and on and on.
Paris. Deep night.
Su Qingyuan sat on the balcony of her hotel room, the trophy on the round table beside her, the crystal refracting fine fragments of light in the moonlight.
Lu Shiyan came out from the room, a cup of warm milk in his hand, and held it out to her.
"Not sleeping yet?"
"Can't sleep." Su Qingyuan took the milk and cupped it in her palms. "Too excited."
Lu Shiyan sat down in the chair beside her, and the two of them watched the Paris night side by side. The Eiffel Tower glittered in the distance, like an enormous lighthouse.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"That line I said on the stage today — did you hear it?"
"Which line?"
Su Qingyuan turned her head to look at him, the moonlight falling on his face, casting his profile in something tender and deep.
"You are my daybreak."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, his gaze deep, deep.
Then he reached out, gently took her hand, and laced their fingers together.
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm."
"You're my daybreak too."
Su Qingyuan curved her lips, leaned on his shoulder, and looked at the lights in the distance.
The Paris night was quiet, so quiet you could hear each other's heartbeat.
One beat, then another, steady — like a kind of promise.
[System: The affection level maxed out ages ago, so the System won't speak. But the System would like to say — this is the finest of times. Not a "happily ever after" fairy-tale ending, but the real beginning of "walking on together." All right, the System is truly bowing out now. Carry on, you two.]
