Chapter 18 — Home Again, the Storm Not Yet Over
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626220.html

The flight from Paris to Nancheng cruised smoothly through the air, ten thousand meters above the ground.
In the privacy of her first-class pod, Su Qingyuan curled up in the wide seat, a blanket draped over her, the crystal trophy still clutched in her hands. She hadn't been willing to check it; she'd held it against her chest the whole way, cradling it like a fragile treasure.
Lu Shiyan sat beside her, a document spread open on the tray table in front of him, though his attention was clearly nowhere near it. He turned his head to glance at her and found her eyes still bright, without a trace of sleepiness.
"Still not asleep?" he asked quietly.
"Can't sleep." Su Qingyuan lifted the trophy and held it up to the moonlight beyond the window. The crystal scattered the light into fine, glittering shards that fell across her face. "Lu Shiyan, do you think that once I get back, I'll find out all of this was just a dream?"
Lu Shiyan reached over and gently pinched the back of her hand.
"Does it hurt?"
"No."
"Then it's not a dream."
Su Qingyuan's lips curved. She carefully set the trophy back into the storage compartment beside her seat, then leaned against his shoulder. He slipped an arm around her in perfect understanding, settling her into a more comfortable position.
"Lu Shiyan, you said before that you were looking into the person behind Su Yurou."
"Mm."
"Did you find them?"
Lu Shiyan was silent for two seconds, his fingers tapping lightly against her shoulder. "I found the general direction. That investment firm is called Shengheng Capital. On the surface it operates independently, but trace its ownership deep enough and it has countless threads tying it to Lu Group's old rival—Dingfeng Group."
Su Qingyuan lifted her head from his shoulder and looked at him. "Dingfeng Group?"
"Dingfeng's chairman is named Gu Changfeng. Twenty years ago, Lu Group and Dingfeng were competing in the same arena. In the end, Lu Group came out on top, and Dingfeng was forced to pivot. Gu Changfeng has always believed the Lu family stole his place. All these years the two families have kept up a polite front, but underneath, there's never truly been a ceasefire."
Su Qingyuan slowly digested all of this. She had never once cared about the feuds of the business world before, but now those feuds had surged like an undercurrent, lapping right up to her feet.
"So he used Su Yurou to go after you? No—to go after me? Because I'm yours?"
Lu Shiyan looked down at her, his gaze still and calm. "Gu Changfeng isn't a man who does anything without a return. Helping Su Yurou wasn't only about getting at me. He has a far bigger aim."
"What aim?"
"The Biennale's award carries the weight of a bellwether in the international jewelry industry. If he could win at the Biennale through Su Yurou—or through any designer he controls—he could shift the entire landscape of the domestic jewelry market. Jewelry has always been a major source of profit in Lu Group's culture-and-entertainment division. He wanted to tear an opening in it from the inside."
Su Qingyuan fell silent.
She suddenly realized that the gold medal she'd taken wasn't just her own personal glory—it had also, indirectly, blocked a blade aimed at Lu Shiyan.
Because the gold medal was hers, not Su Yurou's. Gu Changfeng's plan had fallen through.
"So that's why you were so tense earlier about Su Yurou making the shortlist?" she asked.
"It wasn't her making the shortlist that worried me." Lu Shiyan's fingers threaded through her hair, his touch very light. "What worried me was whether I'd lose control if you got pushed down."
Su Qingyuan's heart gave a tremor.
"Lose control?"
"Lose control to the point of… striking back no matter the cost." Lu Shiyan's voice was low, low enough that it seemed meant for her ears alone. "That's exactly what Gu Changfeng was waiting for. He doesn't care whether Su Yurou wins or loses. What he cares about is whether I can stay calm."
Su Qingyuan gazed at him, then suddenly reached out and pressed her hand gently against his chest. Through his shirt, she could feel his steady, powerful heartbeat.
"And now? Are you calm?"
Lu Shiyan caught the hand she'd pressed to his chest and lowered his head to drop a feather-light kiss on her fingertips.
"With you here, very calm."
Su Qingyuan's face slowly flushed. She withdrew her hand, leaned back against his shoulder, and pretended to watch the clouds outside the window.
But the curve at the corners of her mouth simply wouldn't be pressed back down.
---
Nancheng. Touchdown.
The moment she cleared customs, her phone wouldn't stop buzzing. Su Qingyuan opened it to find a barrage of messages from Zhou Wanyin:
[Qingyuan! You're on the cover of the Chinese edition of Vogue! Next month's issue!]
[Cartier has formally sent over a letter of intent for collaboration. I looked it over for you—the terms are very generous!]
[The provisional patent for the Ripple Cut—Lu Group's legal team has already filed it for you. It's entered the PCT process at the international stage.]
[When do you land? Should I come pick you up?]
Su Qingyuan read through them one by one, and just as she was about to reply, her phone buzzed again. This time it was a text from an unknown number:
"Congratulations, Miss Su. But the game has only just begun. Next time, I won't lose again."
No signature. But Su Qingyuan knew exactly who it was.
Su Yurou.
She handed the phone to Lu Shiyan to see. He gave it a glance, his expression unchanged, and handed it back. "She's not wrong—the game really isn't over. But you won't be giving her another chance, either."
Su Qingyuan nodded, deleted the text, and switched off her phone.
At the airport exit, the Lu family's driver was already waiting. Beside the black Maybach, a uniformed chauffeur respectfully pulled open the car door.
Su Qingyuan slid in and only then noticed there was an extra person in the car—Lu Shiyan's special assistant, surnamed Wang, a capable man in his early thirties, a tablet in his hands.
"Mr. Lu, the background check you had me run on Su Yurou's new lawyer—I have the results."
Lu Shiyan took the tablet and scanned it quickly. Su Qingyuan leaned over to look. On the screen was a tangled relationship chart, with Lawyer Fang at its center, several lines branching outward, all of them eventually pointing to the same node—Shengheng Capital.
"Lawyer Fang's wife is the younger sister of a senior executive at Shengheng Capital," Assistant Wang said. "And last year Shengheng Capital had a sum of money flow into an offshore company under Dingfeng Group. It went through several layers of cover, but the trail was still left behind."
Lu Shiyan handed the tablet back to Assistant Wang, his expression mild. "Keep watching them. Don't tip them off."
"Understood."
The car started up, pulled out of the airport, and merged into Nancheng's afternoon traffic.
Su Qingyuan looked out the window at the familiar streetscape and was suddenly struck by a sense of having stepped back into another lifetime. She'd been gone less than a week—nothing about this city had changed, yet she was no longer the same.
"Assistant Wang, would you mind taking me to my studio first?" she said.
Lu Shiyan turned his head to look at her. "You just got off the plane. You don't want to rest?"
"I want to go see it." Su Qingyuan smiled. "I've been away a few days—I've started to miss the place."
Assistant Wang glanced at Lu Shiyan, who gave a slight nod.
The car turned toward the creative park district.
---
The studio door opened, and Su Qingyuan stood in the doorway, stunned.
Not because it had gathered dust, not because it had changed—
It was because it had changed. Changed into something even better than before.
The worktable had been replaced with a larger one, fitted with a brand-new lighting system and a tool rack. The glass display cases in the showcase area had been swapped for professional cabinets with built-in temperature and humidity control. The sofa in the lounge area had been replaced with a more comfortable one, and beside it stood a new little bookshelf, packed full of jewelry-design books and art albums.
On the windowsill, the pot of pothos she'd casually set down before had been replaced with a few delicate succulents and a small pot of white moth orchids. A heat-insulating film had been applied to the windowpanes, blocking the harsh glare without dimming the natural light.
The entire space looked as if someone had carefully redone it from scratch.
Su Qingyuan walked slowly inside, every step soft and light. She turned to look at Lu Shiyan, who was leaning against the doorframe, hands tucked into his trouser pockets, his expression calm.
"You did this?"
"Mm." Lu Shiyan's tone was as casual as if he were remarking that the weather was nice today. "While you were away these few days, I had someone come tidy it up. The old equipment was getting a bit dated—not fitting for a gold-medal designer."
Su Qingyuan walked over to the new worktable and ran her hand across its surface. The wood felt warm and smooth, the edges rounded into gentle arcs—exactly matching the "I like rounded lines" she'd mentioned to him once before.
She turned and walked to the bookshelf in the lounge area, pulling out a book at random. She opened the cover and found a bookmark tucked inside, a single line of small print across it: "For a future master."
The handwriting was clean, elegant, and sharp—Lu Shiyan's hand.
She looked back at him. He was still leaning against the doorframe, his posture relaxed, but there was a sliver of barely perceptible tension at the bottom of his eyes—like he was waiting for her verdict, yet afraid she'd find it all too deliberate.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Did you, over these few days I was gone, memorize every single corner of my studio, and then have someone redo all of it to suit my tastes?"
Lu Shiyan neither denied it nor admitted it. He simply straightened up a little, stepped away from the doorframe, walked over to stand in front of her, and looked down at her.
"You don't like it?"
"I like it." Su Qingyuan's voice came out a little muffled. "But could you please stop moving me to the verge of tears every single time?"
Lu Shiyan reached out and gently ruffled her hair, his voice very soft. "Then cry. I won't laugh at you."
Su Qingyuan tilted her head up to look at him, her eyes rimmed red, but no tears fell.
She rose onto her toes and pecked him lightly on the lips.
Not the cheek, not the forehead. The lips.
It lasted only an instant, but it was enough to throw both their heartbeats into disarray.
Su Qingyuan stepped back, her ears flushed red enough to bleed, and pretended to study the books on the shelf.
Lu Shiyan stood where he was, lifted a hand to touch his own lips, and then, slowly, ever so slowly, he smiled.
"Su Qingyuan."
"What?"
"This kind of thank-you gift—feel free to give it more often from now on."
Su Qingyuan buried her face in the book and mumbled, "In your dreams."
Above the bookshelf, that pot of white moth orchids bloomed perfectly in the afternoon sun.
[System: I said I was retiring backstage, but staying dead silent through a scene like this is genuinely too much to bear. There. I've piped up. Carry on, you two.]
---
Meanwhile, in an office building in the southern part of the city, in Lawyer Fang's office.
Su Yurou sat on the sofa, a cup of coffee gone stone-cold in front of her. She looked at Lawyer Fang, her gaze unnervingly calm.
"So, Shengheng Capital won't be putting in any more money?"
Lawyer Fang pushed up his glasses, his expression awkward. "It's not that they won't invest—they want to hold off for a while. Mr. Gu's side says Su Qingyuan is riding too high right now, and a head-on clash isn't the wise move. He suggests you lie low for a while, wait for the heat to die down, and then look for another opportunity."
"Lie low?" Su Yurou let out a cold laugh. "I've already been lying low for more than twenty years. How much longer am I supposed to lie low?"
Lawyer Fang sighed. "Miss Su, I can understand how you feel, but what Mr. Gu means is—"
"What Mr. Gu means is that this chess piece of mine is no use for now, so put it away and bring it back out the next time it's needed." Su Yurou stood up and picked up her bag. "I understand."
"Miss Su, where are you going?"
Su Yurou didn't answer. She pulled the door open and walked out.
The corridor was deserted, the sound of her high heels striking the floor crisp and lonely.
She stood before the elevator, looking at her own reflection in the elevator doors—gaunt, pale, with shadows beneath her eyes that wouldn't fade.
She reached up to touch her own face, and suddenly she smiled.
"Su Qingyuan, you must be feeling pretty pleased with yourself right now, aren't you?"
"That's fine."
"People who are pleased with themselves are the easiest to trip and fall."
The elevator doors opened. She stepped inside and pressed the button for the ground floor.
The instant the doors closed, her smile vanished, replaced by a cold, almost obsessive certainty.
She would not give up.
Never.
Because to give up would be to admit that these past twenty-odd years had all been wrong.
And she would absolutely never admit that she'd been wrong.
---
That evening, when Su Qingyuan came out of the studio, she found that Lu Shiyan still hadn't left.
His car was parked beneath the osmanthus tree by the door, the window half down, and he was sitting in the driver's seat on a phone call. His tone was even, with the occasional nod—he looked to be handling business.
Su Qingyuan didn't disturb him; she leaned against the studio doorway and waited.
The setting sun had dyed the entire creative park a warm orange. The osmanthus blossoms had withered, but a faint trace of their sweetness still lingered in the air.
She watched the side of his face and suddenly remembered that line the System had once said—"Every exception he makes, every bit of tenderness, patience, and devotion in his whole life, all of it began on that rainy night, and all of it comes home to one Su Qingyuan."
She used to think that line was a little too cloying.
Now she thought it wasn't cloying at all.
Because it was true.
Lu Shiyan hung up the phone, turned his head, and saw her leaning against the doorframe, not knowing how long she'd been waiting.
"Why didn't you call me over?"
"You looked busy." Su Qingyuan walked over, pulled open the passenger door, and got in. "Watching you work so seriously—it's actually quite a good look on you."
Lu Shiyan started the car, the corner of his mouth lifting slightly. "Meaning, ordinarily I don't look good?"
"Ordinarily you look good too, but that kind of good-looking is—mm."
He didn't let her finish. He leaned over, one hand gently cupping her chin, and kissed her.
Not a fleeting brush, not a tentative taste.
It was the kind of kiss that came after waiting a whole day, holding back a whole day, finally getting that moment alone—a kiss laced with possessiveness and tenderness.
Outside the car, dusk was gradually falling.
Inside the car, their breaths tangled together.
After a long while, Lu Shiyan released her, pressed his forehead to hers, his voice low and husky. "Ordinarily I look good too? Go on."
Su Qingyuan leaned against his shoulder, catching her breath, and it took her ages to squeeze out a single line. "…Lu Shiyan, you've turned wicked."
"I learned it from you."
Su Qingyuan wanted to argue, but the curve at the corners of her mouth gave her away.
Dusk grew thicker and thicker, and the streetlamps of the creative park flickered on one by one.
That black Maybach still sat beneath the osmanthus tree, and for a long, long while, it didn't drive away.

Chapter 19 — The Undercurrent Stirs Again, and She Meets It Head-On
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626221.html

The first week after returning home, Su Qingyuan barely rested at all.
News of the "First Light" pre-sale spread like wildfire, boosted by the Biennale gold medal. The instant she posted the pre-order link, the official website of Zhou Wanyin's studio crashed—not because of a technical glitch, but because the flood of simultaneous orders was so massive that the server simply went down.
"It's fixed, it's fixed!" Zhou Wanyin's voice came down the line, brimming with excitement she couldn't suppress. "Qingyuan, do you know how many orders came in during the first five minutes of the pre-sale?"
"How many?"
"Fifty-three million."
The hand holding the phone went still for a moment. "…Fifty-three million?"
"Fifty-three million. In yuan. In five minutes." Zhou Wanyin drew a deep breath. "No independent designer in this country has ever hit a number like that. You broke the record."
Su Qingyuan leaned back in her studio chair, staring up at the ceiling, and didn't speak for a long while.
Fifty-three million. Five minutes.
She thought back to a few months ago, when she'd been a small-time designer who could barely scrape together rent, with a bank balance in the triple digits, looked down on by everyone. And now, a piece she'd designed had generated fifty-three million in sales within five minutes of going live.
This wasn't a dream. This was real.
"Wanyin, can production keep up?"
"It can. The three suppliers Mr. Lu lined up are all up and running. The first batch of orders should ship within two weeks." Zhou Wanyin laughed. "Your Mr. Lu even has your entire supply chain sorted out for you. Shouldn't you treat him to a meal?"
The corners of Su Qingyuan's mouth curved up. "Treating him to a meal is impossible—he grabs the check every single time."
"Then thank him some other way, hmm?"
"Wanyin!"
Zhou Wanyin laughed heartily on the other end. When she'd laughed it out, her tone suddenly turned serious. "Qingyuan, there's something I need to tell you. The last couple of days, people in the industry have been spreading a rumor—that you won the gold medal because Lu Shiyan pressured the Biennale judging committee. They're telling it in convincing detail, claiming someone saw people from Lu Group in Paris making contact with the judges."
Su Qingyuan's smile slowly faded.
"Who started this?"
"No one can trace the source so far, but I have a guess—the people behind Su Yurou. They couldn't beat you on the work itself, so they've started playing games with public opinion." Zhou Wanyin's voice sank. "Do you want to put out a statement?"
Su Qingyuan was silent for a few seconds, then said, "No statement needed. The truth is plain for everyone to see. The judging committee is a top-tier international independent body—it won't change its verdict because someone applies pressure. If anyone has doubts, let them produce evidence."
"That's all well and good, but public opinion is a tricky thing—"
"Wanyin," Su Qingyuan cut her off, her voice calm but resolute, "if I had to issue a statement every time someone threw mud at me, I'd never have time to do anything else for the rest of my life. 'The clean stay clean'—those four words aren't there to comfort yourself. They're there to face the world with."
Zhou Wanyin was quiet for a moment, then let out a soft laugh. "All right. I won't try to talk you into it. You handle it your way."
After hanging up, Su Qingyuan sat by the window, gazing out at the osmanthus tree.
Its petals had nearly all fallen, leaving only bare branches swaying faintly in the autumn wind.
A saying came to mind—"The tree that stands tallest in the forest is the one the wind will break."
She was that tree standing tall above the rest now. The wind had come—from every direction. But she was no longer the fragile little sapling that toppled at the first gust.
Her roots were planted deep.
That afternoon, Su Qingyuan received an unexpected call.
The number was unfamiliar, but the moment she answered, the voice on the other end made her freeze for a heartbeat.
"Ms. Su, this is Lawyer Fang."
Su Yurou's lawyer.
The hand holding the phone tightened slightly, but her voice held steady. "Lawyer Fang. What is it?"
"Ms. Su, I'd like to have a talk with you." Lawyer Fang's tone was courteous—courteous to the point of being excessive. "Regarding the matter with Su Yurou, perhaps we can find a solution that benefits both parties."
"What solution?"
"It's not convenient to discuss over the phone. Could we set up a time to meet in person?"
Su Qingyuan was silent for two seconds. "Lawyer Fang, if you've come to negotiate terms on Su Yurou's behalf, then I can tell you right now—I won't accept any terms. The Ripple Cut is my original technique. Su Yurou used it without authorization. Either she publicly apologizes and stops using it, or I sue. There's no middle ground."
Lawyer Fang paused, his voice still courteous but now carrying a subtle, probing edge. "Ms. Su, have you considered that a lawsuit would also drain your time and energy? Your career is on the rise—why distract yourself over things in the past?"
"Distract myself?" Su Qingyuan let out a soft laugh. "Lawyer Fang, aren't you in the intellectual property field? You should understand better than I do—when a designer's original technique is stolen, that's not a 'thing in the past.' It's a thing of the present, and a thing of the future too. If I don't pursue it now, there'll be a second Su Yurou, a third. I'm pursuing it not for revenge, but to protect myself—and to protect everyone in this industry who does honest, original work."
The line was silent for a long time.
At length, Lawyer Fang sighed. "Ms. Su, I understand. I'll convey your position to my client."
"Good. If there's nothing else, I'll hang up now."
The call ended.
Su Qingyuan set down the phone and realized her hand was trembling slightly. Not from fear—from anger.
She drew several deep breaths, picked up her carving knife, and bent back over the worktable.
The sound of the blade scraping across metal was fine and fragmented, yet unwavering—like a vow that no storm could ever interrupt.
That evening, Lu Shiyan came to pick her up.
Once she was in the car, Su Qingyuan told him about Lawyer Fang's call.
Lu Shiyan listened without responding right away, driving in silence, his fingers tapping the steering wheel twice.
"Lawyer Fang isn't the type to act without certainty," he said, his voice steady and low. "The fact that he called you means Su Yurou's side has realized how serious the problem is. They want to settle—not out of kindness, but because they're afraid of losing."
"I didn't agree to settle." Su Qingyuan watched his profile. "I told him: either Su Yurou publicly apologizes and stops using the Ripple Cut, or I sue."
Lu Shiyan turned his head to glance at her, an emotion in his eyes that was hard to name—not surprise, but the kind of admiration that said "of course you would," with something else pressed beneath it, something like tenderness, something like pride.
"Su Qingyuan, do you know how many people in your position would choose to settle?"
"I know," Su Qingyuan said softly. "Settling is easier, cheaper, faster. But settling means compromise, and compromise means they get to keep going. I don't want to give them any signal that they 'get to keep going.'"
Lu Shiyan reached out and took the hand resting on her knee. He didn't say anything more—he just gripped it, hard.
The strength of that single clasp was worth a thousand words.
The car stopped in front of a restaurant.
Su Qingyuan got out and found that it was a perfectly ordinary hotpot place—not the kind of high-end restaurant you had to book a month in advance, just one of those steaming, bustling little neighborhood hotpot joints you saw everywhere in Nancheng.
She turned to look at Lu Shiyan. He was locking the car, his expression as calm as if to say "I come here all the time."
"How did you know I like hotpot?" Su Qingyuan asked.
"Last time you ordered takeout, I saw you pick the spicy mala broth." Lu Shiyan walked over and took her hand naturally. "Come on, I've eaten here before. The food's good."
Letting him lead her into the hotpot place, Su Qingyuan was still digesting that line in her mind—last time you ordered takeout, I saw you pick the spicy mala broth.
He'd been watching when she ordered takeout. He'd been watching, and he'd remembered. Not only had he remembered, he'd found a good hotpot place and brought her here on purpose.
This feeling—of being quietly watched over, of having her small details remembered—made her heart flutter more than any rose or diamond ring ever could.
The private room in the hotpot place wasn't large, but it was clean. The red-oil broth bubbled and gurgled, steam rising up and flushing both their faces a rosy pink.
Su Qingyuan blanched a slice of tripe—dipping it in and out seven, eight times—then put it in her mouth, and her eyes lit up.
"Good, isn't it?" Lu Shiyan watched her shining eyes, the corner of his mouth lifting.
"It's delicious!" Su Qingyuan blanched another slice and dropped it into his bowl. "Try it."
Lu Shiyan looked down at the tripe in his bowl and slowly smiled. He thought of that private kitchen restaurant before, where she'd also served him food. Back then, their relationship hadn't yet been settled, and there'd been a hint of cautious hesitation in the way she picked up the food for him.
Now, the motion was as natural as if she'd done it countless times.
That change softened some place inside him until it was very, very tender.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Tell me—Gu Changfeng, the man behind Su Yurou. What is it he actually wants?" Su Qingyuan set down her chopsticks and looked at him earnestly. "Does he want Lu Group's share of the jewelry sector? Or something else?"
Lu Shiyan set down his chopsticks, wiped his hands with a napkin, then picked up his teacup and took a slow sip.
"Gu Changfeng went up against the Lu family once when he was young. He lost. That single loss dropped him from a position where he could have stood as the Lu family's equal down into the second tier. For twenty years, he's watched the Lu family grow stronger and stronger while he himself grew more and more marginalized." He put the cup down, his voice flat. "It's not just market share he wants. He wants to win. He wants to prove to everyone—that he, Gu Changfeng, is no lesser than anyone in the Lu family."
Su Qingyuan listened, slowly nodding.
Suddenly she understood.
Gu Changfeng was helping Su Yurou not because Su Yurou had any great talent, but because Su Yurou hated her—and she was Lu Shiyan's woman. Su Yurou's hatred and Gu Changfeng's resentment had twisted together into a single rope, and the target was her—or rather, was Lu Shiyan.
"So what do you plan to do?" Su Qingyuan asked.
"Nothing." Lu Shiyan blanched a slice of beef and set it in her bowl. "He makes a move, I counter it. If he doesn't move first, I won't go stirring up trouble. That's the rule in business—it's not children brawling, where whoever throws the first punch is in the wrong."
Su Qingyuan looked at the beef in her bowl, and the corners of her mouth suddenly lifted. "So you're waiting for him to expose a weakness on his own?"
Lu Shiyan looked at her, a flicker of admiration in his eyes. "You're understanding me better and better."
"Stand by tar and you turn black."
"Stand by cinnabar and you turn red. You've got it backwards."
"I didn't get it backwards," Su Qingyuan said, smiling as she put the beef in her mouth. "Spend long enough with you, and I've learned how to talk in circles too."
Watching the way she smiled, Lu Shiyan suddenly reached over and lightly wiped a little dab of sesame sauce from the corner of her mouth.
The motion was as natural as if he'd done it countless times.
Su Qingyuan froze for a heartbeat, then lowered her head and went on eating her hotpot, pretending nothing had happened.
But her ears had gone red again.
[System: Just popping in for a sec. This scene is too domestic—so domestic the System nearly cried. Could you two please not be this sweet? Never mind, don't answer that, carry on.]
Su Qingyuan silently cursed in her heart: Didn't you say you'd retired to the background?
[System: I come back to check in now and then. Seeing the two of you doing so well puts the System's mind at ease. This time I'm really retiring. Bye-bye.]
Holding back a laugh, Su Qingyuan went on blanching tripe.
After finishing the hotpot, the two of them stepped out of the restaurant. The night wind of Nancheng swept against them, carrying the chill of late autumn.
Su Qingyuan instinctively hunched her shoulders, and Lu Shiyan immediately took off his coat and draped it over her.
"You don't have to—"
"Wear it." Two words, curt, brooking no argument.
Su Qingyuan pulled the coat—still warm with his body heat—closer around her shoulders, and didn't refuse again.
The two of them walked slowly down the street, neither of them speaking. The hotpot place receded further and further behind them, and the streetlights stretched their two shadows long, very long.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"How do you think Gu Changfeng will make his move?"
Lu Shiyan pondered for a moment. "He won't target you directly. Targeting you directly would be too obvious—everyone knows Su Yurou is connected to him. He'll come from the side—through industry channels, say, squeezing your supply chain, or poaching your partners out from under you."
Su Qingyuan frowned. "The supply chain is handled by Lu Group. Can he even touch it?"
"Not directly, but he can poach. Of your three suppliers, one of the bosses has a personal friendship with Gu Changfeng. If he offers better terms, that supplier might tear up the agreement." Lu Shiyan's tone was very calm, as if laying out a contingency he'd already prepared. "But don't worry. I set up a backup plan in advance. If that supplier wants out, another alternate can step in seamlessly within twenty-four hours."
Su Qingyuan stopped walking and turned to look at him.
Under the streetlight, his features were deep and gentle, his eyes reflecting the warm yellow glow.
"Lu Shiyan, exactly how many backup plans have you made?"
"A lot." He looked down at her, his voice very soft. "Enough that you don't need to worry about a single thing."
Su Qingyuan gazed at him, and that feeling of being steadily held up welled in her chest again.
She rose onto her toes and pressed a very, very light kiss to his lips.
"Thank you for the backup plans." She stepped back, her voice soft and laced with a smile. "That's the deposit."
Lu Shiyan reached out, lightly circled her waist, and pulled her back.
"Deposit received," he said, lowering his head, his voice dropping until it seemed meant for her ears alone. "When do you pay the balance?"
Su Qingyuan's face went scarlet in an instant.
"You… you pay the balance first, and then I'll pay."
"All right." Lu Shiyan smiled, his brows and eyes relaxing into a smile like the first crack splitting across a frozen lake in spring. "I'll owe the balance for now. Interest calculated at the highest rate."
Su Qingyuan turned her face away, pretending to study the shop window across the street.
But her hand stayed in his the whole time, fingers interlaced, palm pressed to palm.
Like two hearts, separated only by skin and bone, listening to each other beat.
The night deepened.
In the distance, the lights of Nancheng merged into a single warm sea of glow.
Lu Shiyan's car was parked at the foot of Su Qingyuan's apartment building. The two of them sat in the car for a while, neither willing to be the first to say "I'm heading up."
"What's on your schedule tomorrow?" Lu Shiyan asked.
"Studio in the morning, and in the afternoon Zhou Wanyin's taking me to meet a brand." Su Qingyuan counted on her fingers. "In the evening I might have dinner with Wanyin—not sure what time I'll be back."
"Message me when you're done. I'll come get you."
"If it's too late, don't bother—I'll just hail a cab—"
"I'll come get you," Lu Shiyan repeated, his tone gentle but firm.
Su Qingyuan looked at him and relented. "All right. I'll message you when I'm done."
She pushed open the car door, got out, took two steps, then looked back. Lu Shiyan was watching her through the car window.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Goodnight."
"Goodnight."
Su Qingyuan turned and headed upstairs, every step feeling weightless.
At her door, she pulled out her keys but didn't open it right away. Instead she leaned against the door, listening to her own heartbeat.
One beat, two beats, three beats.
Every beat spoke the same name.
She curved her lips into a smile, opened the door, stepped inside, and turned on the light.
On the windowsill, the white moth orchid was in full bloom under the lamplight.
Su Qingyuan walked over and gently touched a petal, then picked up her phone and sent Lu Shiyan a message:
[Home now. The matter of the balance—we'll talk about it next time we meet.]
The reply came in a flash:
[All right. I'll have the interest ready.]
Su Qingyuan pressed the phone to her chest, gazing out at the night, smiling like she'd been handed all the candy in the world.
Outside the window, the moon over Nancheng was round and bright.
Tomorrow, there would be new storms.
But tonight, there was only moonlight—and two people who slept apart, yet met each other in their dreams.
[System: Truly retired to the background now. One last word—may the two of you, year after year, never let your devotion change.]

========================================

Chapter 20 — The Brand's Arrogance, Her Quiet Composure
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626222.html

The next morning, Su Qingyuan allowed herself a rare lie-in.

After returning to the apartment the night before, she had worked until two in the morning—although the "First Light" collection had already launched, demand for follow-up custom orders far exceeded expectations. Many clients had left comments on the pre-sale page, hoping she would create bespoke designs based on their personal stories.

Su Qingyuan read through every single one of those comments, her heart filling with something warm and overwhelming.

Among them were daughters wanting to gift their mothers, husbands wanting to gift their wives, girls wanting to gift themselves. Behind every story was a beam of light waiting to be kindled.

She made up her mind on the spot: alongside the "First Light" collection, she would open a custom line, taking only three commissions a month, each one personally crafted by her own hand.

After the announcement went out through the official account of Zhou Wanyin's studio, applications passed three hundred within ten minutes.

Su Qingyuan rubbed her bleary eyes, picked up her phone, and found the screen piled with messages.

Zhou Wanyin: [You up? Two o'clock this afternoon, Cartier Greater China headquarters. Don't be late.]

Lu Shiyan: [Good morning. Remember to eat breakfast. There's congee in the kitchen, in the warming cabinet.]

Su Qingyuan stared at Lu Shiyan's message for a stunned moment, then ran barefoot into the kitchen.

On the stovetop sat a white insulated clay pot, quiet and waiting. She lifted the lid and the aroma of century egg and lean pork congee wafted up at her, still warm.

She paused.

When had he come? She hadn't gone to sleep until two the night before—there was no way he'd come this late to deliver congee... unless he'd made a special trip first thing in the morning.

Su Qingyuan ladled out a bowl of congee, sat down at the dining table, and slowly ate.

The congee tasted wonderful—nothing like takeout. The grains were soft and tender, the savory richness of century egg and lean pork pitched just right.

She picked up her phone and sent Lu Shiyan a message:

[Got the congee. When did you come by?]

Lu Shiyan's reply came quickly: [Seven this morning. You were still asleep, so I didn't wake you.]

Su Qingyuan: [You came at seven to drop off congee, then went to work? Don't you need sleep?]

Lu Shiyan: [I slept. Got back last night, handled some things, went to bed at one.]

Su Qingyuan's chest tightened. To bed at one, here at seven to deliver congee—that meant he'd only slept six hours?

She was about to say something more when another message arrived:

[Is the congee good?]

Su Qingyuan looked at the line of text and suddenly felt a sting in her nose. This man was always like this—when he himself hadn't rested properly, what he asked was "Is the congee good?"

[It's good. Thank you.]

Lu Shiyan: [Good is all that matters. You're seeing Cartier this afternoon. Want me to come along?]

Su Qingyuan thought it over and replied: [No need. This is a professional setting, I want to go on my own. If you show up, they'll just assume I'm relying on connections.]

Lu Shiyan: [Alright. Tell me how it goes afterward.]

Su Qingyuan set down her phone, drank the bowl of congee clean, then washed up, tidied the kitchen, and changed her clothes.

She stood before the mirror, studying herself.

A white shirt, black high-waisted wide-leg trousers, simple silver stud earrings—a sample piece from her own "First Snow" collection. Hair in a low ponytail, makeup clean and understated.

She looked sharp, professional, unflashy, yet every detail spoke of quality.

She gave herself a nod in the mirror, picked up her bag, and headed out.

Cartier's Greater China headquarters stood in the heart of Nancheng's most bustling CBD district.

The exterior of the entire building was understated yet luxurious, its dark-gray glass curtain wall mirroring the clouds in the sky. Red silk ribbons were tied around the necks of the two stone lions flanking the entrance—a blend of East and West, imposing without being ostentatious.

Su Qingyuan walked into the lobby. The reception staff had clearly been notified, and a smiling attendant led her upstairs. "Ms. Su, this way please. The brand director is waiting for you on the thirty-eighth floor."

As the elevator rose, Su Qingyuan looked at her own reflection in the mirrored surface and took a deep breath.

Cartier.

One of the world's top jewelry houses.

A few months ago, she wouldn't even have been qualified to set foot in this building. Now she was here as an invited guest.

The elevator doors opened. At the end of the corridor stood a pair of dark wooden double doors. The attendant knocked, pushed them open, and stepped aside to let Su Qingyuan enter first.

Inside was a spacious office, the floor-to-ceiling windows framing Nancheng's skyline. Behind an enormous dark solid-wood desk sat a blonde woman in her forties—Anna Schmidt, Cartier's Greater China brand director, widely known in the industry as the "Iron Lady."

Seeing Su Qingyuan, Anna stood, a professional smile on her face, and extended her hand. "Ms. Su, I've heard a great deal about you."

"Ms. Schmidt, it's a pleasure." Su Qingyuan shook her hand—firm but measured, neither obsequious nor arrogant.

The two of them sat down. Anna's assistant brought in coffee, then withdrew without a sound.

Anna got straight to the point, skipping the pleasantries. "Ms. Su, I've seen all the work in your 'First Light' collection, and I've followed the news of your Biennale award. Frankly, your talent has left a deep impression on me."

"Thank you."

"However," Anna's tone shifted, the smile unchanged but her words now carrying a note of scrutiny, "talent is one thing, and commercial value is another. When Cartier chooses a designer to collaborate with, we look not only at design ability, but also at the designer's stability, their fit with the brand image, and—their resilience to risk."

Su Qingyuan's hand, holding the coffee cup, didn't move. She waited calmly for Anna to finish.

"Some of your recent news," Anna's fingers tapped lightly on the desktop, "including your adoptive father buying marketing accounts to spread rumors, your sister's suspected plagiarism, and your relationship with your boyfriend—President Lu of the Lu Group—these are all talking points in the public eye. For Cartier, talking points can be a good thing, or they can be a risk."

Su Qingyuan set down her coffee cup and met Anna's gaze.

"Ms. Schmidt, I completely understand everything you've said. Risk assessment is a necessary step when a brand chooses its partners. But I'd ask you to distinguish between two things—'news one is passively dragged into' and 'news one actively manufactures.'"

Anna arched an eyebrow slightly.

"My adoptive father spreading rumors, my sister plagiarizing—these were not things I chose. They happened to me because I chose to stand up and protect my own rights. If being 'harmed' makes someone 'a risk,' then that logic is unfair to every victim."

Su Qingyuan's voice wasn't loud, but every word landed steady and sure.

"As for my relationship with Mr. Lu Shiyan—we went public not to drum up hype, but because someone secretly photographed us and tried to use it to hurt us. We chose to respond head-on because we didn't want our private affairs to become leverage in someone else's hands."

Anna looked at her, and the scrutiny in her eyes slowly gave way to something else—curiosity.

"Ms. Su, the way you speak doesn't sound like someone negotiating with a brand for the first time."

"Because I've never had the chance to negotiate with a brand before," Su Qingyuan said frankly. "But I've always known exactly who I am, and what my work is worth."

Anna was silent for a few seconds, then suddenly smiled. This smile was a touch more genuine than the professional one from before.

"Alright, Ms. Su, I'll speak plainly. Cartier wants to work with you—but not as a brand designer. As a 'guest artist.' Once a year, you design a capsule collection for Cartier, fully led by you. Cartier only provides the supply chain and sales channels. Profit split, fifty-fifty."

Something stirred in Su Qingyuan's heart.

Guest artist. Not a designer absorbed into the brand, but an equal, independent collaborator.

That status carried more dignity than a "signed designer," and more of a voice as well.

"The profit split," Su Qingyuan said, "I want to negotiate."

Anna clearly hadn't expected her to negotiate the split outright, and paused. "What were you thinking?"

"Sixty-forty. Sixty to me, forty to you."

The office fell silent for a moment.

Anna set down the pen in her hand and leaned slightly forward. "Ms. Su, do you know that Cartier has never once given a sixty-forty split to any designer it's worked with?"

"I know." Su Qingyuan didn't flinch or look away. "But no other designer has set a record of fifty-three million in pre-sales within five minutes, either."

Anna looked at her, her gaze so sharp it seemed to want to see straight through her.

Su Qingyuan didn't shy from that gaze. Her spine was perfectly straight, her eyes clear and resolute.

After a long while, Anna leaned back into her chair and let out a soft laugh.

"Ms. Su, you really are a lot like your boyfriend."

Su Qingyuan blinked. "What do you mean?"

"Your negotiating style." Anna picked up her coffee cup, a trace of resignation and admiration in her tone. "Neither of you gives an inch."

Su Qingyuan curved her lips but said nothing.

The air in the office shifted from tense to relaxed. Anna picked up the documents on the desk, flipped through a few pages, then closed them again.

"A sixty-forty split—I'll need to discuss it with headquarters. But from what I know of them, they won't agree easily."

"I'll wait to hear from you." Su Qingyuan stood and extended her hand. "Whatever the outcome, today's conversation with you has been enormously valuable to me."

Anna shook her hand—and this time her grip was a little firmer than before.

"Ms. Su, I'll be honest. Before you came in today, my impression of you was 'a young designer who'd risen on connections and luck.' But now—" she let go, the corner of her mouth lifting, "I've changed my mind."

When Su Qingyuan walked out of the Cartier building, the autumn sunlight fell perfectly across her shoulders.

She stood on the steps, tilted her head back, and drew a deep breath of the sky.

Done.

Not that the collaboration itself was settled—but that she had held her ground at the negotiating table.

She hadn't shrunk three inches just because the other party was Cartier, hadn't lost her nerve before Anna's commanding presence, hadn't accepted every condition just because "they're a big brand."

She had negotiated what she ought to negotiate, and held what she ought to hold.

Her phone buzzed.

Lu Shiyan: [Done? How did it go?]

Su Qingyuan: [Done. Cartier wants to work together—guest artist status, one capsule collection a year. I negotiated a sixty-forty split, sixty to me, forty to them. Anna said she needs to talk to headquarters.]

Lu Shiyan's reply came fast: [You negotiated sixty-forty?]

Su Qingyuan: [Mm. Do you think it's too high?]

Lu Shiyan: [Not too high. Your value is worth it. Did she agree?]

Su Qingyuan: [She said she needs to talk to headquarters.]

Lu Shiyan: [I'll have someone quietly put in a word with headquarters. No pressure—just to let them know your 'First Light' pre-sale figures are real, not padded.]

Su Qingyuan looked at the message and couldn't help smiling.

She'd noticed a pattern—whenever she fought it out in a professional arena, Lu Shiyan was always there on the sidelines, silently passing her weapons. He didn't take the field for her; he made sure that when she did, she had a blade in her hand.

[Okay. Thank you.]

Lu Shiyan: [You're welcome. What do you want for dinner? Let's celebrate.]

Su Qingyuan thought for a moment, then typed out a line:

[Something you make.]

The other end was silent for a few seconds.

Lu Shiyan: [I can't cook.]

Su Qingyuan: [I know. But you'll learn. The congee last time was very good.]

The other end fell silent for even longer.

Then Lu Shiyan sent a voice message, his tone carrying a trace of being caught out and a smile he couldn't quite suppress:

"Fine. I'll learn. But you're not allowed to complain that it tastes bad."

Su Qingyuan played the voice message twice and saved it.

She stood on the steps outside the Cartier building, the sunlight on her, smiling like a little girl who'd just been given a promise.

[System: I said I'd stay behind the scenes. But this System truly can't help itself—Lu Shiyan, learning to cook? This man would walk into a kitchen for you. Do you even know that he used to have no idea which way a kitchen door swings open? Alright, System will shut up now. System has shut up.]

Su Qingyuan smiled and slipped her phone into her pocket, walked down the steps, and merged into the hurried crowd of the CBD.

People came and went all around her, suited and brisk, in a rush. No one knew that this young woman in a white shirt with a low ponytail had just pulled off a beautiful negotiation.

And even fewer knew that the man standing behind her was the strongest backing in all of Nancheng.

But she knew.

And she was using her own effort to make herself worthy of that backing—no, not worthy of it. To stand shoulder to shoulder with him.

That evening, when Su Qingyuan returned to the studio, she found a parcel at the door.

A white cardboard box, with no sender information, only a handwritten card in clumsy, crooked script:

"Sister Qingyuan, I'm sorry. —Chen Xiaoman"

Su Qingyuan looked at the name and froze for a moment.

Chen Xiaoman. The girl who had posed as Photographer Lin's assistant and secretly photographed her Ripple Cut technique.

She opened the box. Inside was a stack of photographs and a letter.

The photographs captured a scene of Su Yurou meeting with a middle-aged man. The man was in his fifties, dressed in a dark-gray bespoke suit, his hair graying but his spirit sharp, a high-handed arrogance between his brows that came from long years at the top.

Su Qingyuan didn't recognize the man, but she had a powerful intuition—he was Gu Changfeng.

The photos had been taken from a very concealed angle, as if shot from a distance, but every one was crisp and clear. Su Yurou and the man's expressions, gestures, even the way they shook hands—all of it was perfectly visible.

Su Qingyuan picked up the letter and unfolded it.

The handwriting was still clumsy and crooked, but every stroke was pressed down hard, as though written with great resolve:

"Sister Qingyuan:

My name is Chen Xiaoman. My sister was Su Yurou's college roommate. Su Yurou came to me and said she only needed me to take a few photos, that it wouldn't hurt anyone. She gave me fifty thousand yuan to apply to Photographer Lin's team and secretly photograph your workbench.

I did it. I photographed your work notes and the finished details of 'Daybreak,' and sent the photos to her.

I thought nothing would come of it. I thought it was just 'borrowing,' not stealing.

Later I saw the news, and only then did I learn she had stolen your technique and used it to enter a competition.

I was so afraid. I was afraid you'd sue me, afraid of going to prison. I secretly followed Su Yurou and photographed her with that man. I thought, if I gave these to you, maybe you'd forgive me.

Sister Qingyuan, I know I was wrong. I don't ask for your forgiveness, only that you don't sue me. My mother is ill, and I'm the only one in the family earning money. If I go to prison, there'll be no one to take care of her.

I'm sorry. I'm truly sorry."

Su Qingyuan held the letter, silent for a long time.

The sky outside the window darkened bit by bit. The studio lights were off, and she stood in the dim light like a quiet statue.

She felt no anger.

She even pitied Chen Xiaoman—a young girl lured by money, driven by fear, and in the end tormented by her own conscience.

She picked up her phone and dialed Lawyer Liu.

"Lawyer Liu, this is Su Qingyuan. I'd like to ask about something—if an accomplice voluntarily provides key evidence and admits their wrongdoing, how is that generally handled under the law?"

Lawyer Liu explained the relevant provisions in detail on the other end of the line. When Su Qingyuan had finished listening, she was silent for a moment.

"I understand. Thank you, Lawyer Liu."

After hanging up, she sent Chen Xiaoman a text:

"I've received the photos and the letter. I won't sue you. But what you did was wrong, and I hope you remember this lesson. Don't ever do something against your conscience for money again."

A few seconds later, Chen Xiaoman's reply came—just three words:

"Thank you."

Su Qingyuan set down her phone, put the photographs away carefully, and placed them in a drawer.

These photos were direct evidence of Su Yurou colluding with Gu Changfeng. She wouldn't use them for now, but she had to keep them—at the critical moment, they would be a fatal blow.

[System: The heroine chooses not to sue Chen Xiaoman. Not out of saintliness, but because she's letting it go. "Letting it go" is more powerful than forgiveness. Because "letting it go" means: I won't waste my time hating you. I'm too busy moving forward.]

Su Qingyuan silently said to the System in her heart: thank you for understanding.

[System: Even though the System has retreated behind the scenes, its reading comprehension is still intact. Alright, I won't bother you anymore.]

Su Qingyuan curved her lips, switched on the light, walked to her workbench, and picked up her carving knife.

A new design was waiting for her.

========================================

Chapter 21 — Cartier's Olive Branch, Gu Changfeng's Probe
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626223.html

Chen Xiaoman's photos had been sitting in the drawer for three days.
Su Qingyuan hadn't told a soul—not even Lu Shiyan. It wasn't that she meant to keep it from him; she just needed to think it through first—when, and in what way, these photos should be brought into the light. A trump card stays a trump card precisely because, while it's still in your hand, no one knows it exists.
Over those three days, her life had been packed wall to wall with work.
Orders for the "First Light" series had already broken eighty million, and word came from the supply chain that the first batch of finished pieces would be delivered in five days. Zhou Wanyin could barely contain her grin over the phone, saying it was the fiercest debut she'd seen from a newcomer in her twenty years in the business.
As for Cartier, Anna had stayed silent.
Su Qingyuan didn't push. She knew that for a brand like Cartier, every decision had to pass through layer upon layer of approval. A forty-sixty split was probably a first for them, too. She was waiting—but not passively. During that wait, she finished the first design draft for her bespoke line.
It was a ring. The client was a woman in her thirties who wanted to give it to her mother, a cancer survivor in recovery. The theme was "rebirth." Su Qingyuan used a single small green tourmaline, ringed with a circle of tiny diamond chips—like the glow that surrounds a new sprout breaking through the soil.
The client cried when she saw the design draft. Su Qingyuan didn't cry, but the moment she hit send, her hand trembled ever so slightly.
This was what design meant to her. Not the money, not the fame—it was these tears. These scalding tears, shed because someone had finally been understood, seen, treasured.
On the morning of the fourth day, Anna's call finally came.
"Ms. Su, headquarters has agreed."
Su Qingyuan gripped her phone, her heart skipping half a beat, but her voice stayed steady. "Forty-sixty?"
"Forty-sixty." There was a trace of rueful laughter in Anna's tone. "Headquarters says it's the first time they've ever made an exception for a Chinese designer. They hope you won't make them regret it."
"I won't."
"I'll have the contract sent to your inbox. If you have no objections, we'll sign next Wednesday and launch the capsule collection at the same time. No restrictions on theme, no restrictions on timeline—but we'd like it to release in the spring of next year."
"All right. I'll wait for your contract."
Hanging up, Su Qingyuan sat at her worktable, gazing out the window at that bare osmanthus tree, and let out a long, slow breath.
Cartier. Guest artist. A forty-sixty split.
Three months ago, those three phrases strung together had been something she wouldn't have dared to dream of, even in her dreams.
Her phone buzzed. A message from Lu Shiyan:
[Congratulations. Anna told me about the Cartier deal.]
Su Qingyuan: [How did she put it to you?]
Lu Shiyan: [She said: "Your girlfriend is the hardest designer I've ever had to negotiate with."]
Su Qingyuan's lips curved. [And then?]
Lu Shiyan: [And then I said: "Thank you. I think so too."]
Su Qingyuan laughed out loud. She could just picture the look on Anna's face hearing that—probably much like her own face that day in the elevator, listening to the System relay Lu Shiyan's inner monologue.
Su Qingyuan: [Dinner's on me tonight. A real treat—the kind where I don't let you pick up the tab.]
Lu Shiyan: [All right. I'll be waiting for you to pay.]
She set down her phone and started tidying up her worktable. Today she'd decided to give herself a half-day off—she'd hardly rested since the Biennale. Her body wasn't tired, but her heart needed room to breathe.
Halfway through tidying, a knock came at the door.
Not Lu Shiyan—he had a key and never knocked.
Su Qingyuan went over and opened it. A man in his fifties stood outside.
A custom dark-gray suit, hair gone gray but his bearing vigorous and sharp, with a kind of arrogance in his brow that came from long years at the top. His features were deeply cut—he must have been handsome in his youth—but the years had carved too many calculating lines into his face, turning that handsomeness into a sharpness that set people on edge.
Su Qingyuan recognized him at a glance.
Gu Changfeng.
She'd seen him in Chen Xiaoman's photos, but in person he carried far more menace. It wasn't an overt ferocity—it was a restrained chill, coiling around you soundlessly, like a snake.
"Ms. Su, forgive the intrusion." Gu Changfeng smiled, a perfectly courteous smile, but there was no warmth behind his eyes. "I'm Gu Changfeng. I wonder if you've heard of me?"
Su Qingyuan leaned against the doorframe, with no intention of inviting him in, her tone flat. "Mr. Gu, I've heard the name. What brings you to me?"
Clearly Gu Changfeng hadn't expected this attitude from her—not warm, not flustered, not even curious. He paused, his smile unchanged. "Ms. Su won't invite me in to sit a while?"
"The studio's small; it's hardly suitable for hosting. There's a coffee shop across the way with a nice atmosphere. If you don't mind, Mr. Gu, we can talk there."
Gu Changfeng looked at her, a flicker of appraisal entering his gaze. After a few seconds, he nodded. "All right."
At the coffee shop, Su Qingyuan ordered an Americano, and Gu Changfeng asked for a Longjing—the fact that a coffee shop served Longjing said plenty about how unusual the place was.
The two of them sat facing each other across a small round table.
Gu Changfeng raised his Longjing, took a slow sip, set the cup down, and got straight to the point. "Ms. Su, I've come today to apologize."
Su Qingyuan said nothing, waiting for him to go on.
"I did help Su Yurou with a few things." Gu Changfeng's tone was so candid it didn't sound like a lie. "But that was out of personal connections. Her mother, Liu Xiulan, and I are distant relatives. When she came to me for help, it was awkward to refuse. But I never imagined she'd use the resources I provided to steal your techniques and plagiarize your work."
Su Qingyuan lifted her Americano, took an unhurried sip, set it down, and looked Gu Changfeng in the eye.
"Mr. Gu, you didn't come here today just to apologize, did you?"
Gu Changfeng smiled, and this time the smile was a shade more genuine than when he'd walked in—but only a shade.
"Ms. Su is a sharp one. Then I'll speak plainly. I want to work with you."
Su Qingyuan arched an eyebrow.
"I know your deal with Cartier is already settled." Gu Changfeng's tone carried an air of "I know everything." "But Cartier is an international brand, and their market channels in this country are limited. The Dingfeng Group has a jewelry company under its umbrella—not as high-end as Cartier, but with strong penetration in the country's second- and third-tier cities. If you're willing to work with us, I can offer you better terms than Cartier—a fifty-fifty split, or even forty-sixty, with sixty going to you and forty to me."
Su Qingyuan looked at him, and suddenly smiled.
"Mr. Gu, you just said you came to apologize. But what you've said since doesn't sound like an apology. It sounds like a poaching pitch."
Gu Changfeng wasn't thrown by the remark—if anything, his smile deepened. "Ms. Su, in business, apology and poaching have never been separate things. I admit I misjudged when I helped Su Yurou before, but now I want to set that mistake right. Working with you is correcting a mistake for me, and one more path forward for you. A win-win—why not?"
Su Qingyuan set down her coffee cup and leaned back slightly against her chair.
"Mr. Gu, let me ask you something."
"Please."
"When you helped Su Yurou, did you know her work was stolen?"
Gu Changfeng's smile froze for an instant.
"Did you know whose work she'd stolen?"
His smile slowly retreated.
Su Qingyuan didn't wait for his answer and pressed on. "You knew. Because you had Lawyer Fang teach her how to blur the lines with 'taking inspiration,' how to skirt the edges and dodge legal risk. You didn't 'misjudge'—you knew full well she was stealing, and you helped her steal."
The coffee shop fell quiet for a moment. The customers at the next table seemed to sense the tension and quietly moved to other seats.
Gu Changfeng looked at Su Qingyuan, his gaze turning fathomless.
"Ms. Su, some things lose all meaning once they're said out loud."
"I never intended to have anything meaningful with you." Su Qingyuan stood, took a fifty-yuan note from her wallet, and laid it on the table. "This coffee's on me. Mr. Gu, you came to me looking to 'work together,' not because I'm so very talented, but because Cartier chose me, and you don't want a competitor to monopolize the advantage. When you helped Su Yurou, you never imagined she'd lose this badly. Now you want to swap in a new pawn—sorry, but I'm no one's pawn."
She picked up her bag and turned to leave.
"Ms. Su." Gu Changfeng's voice came from behind her, not loud, but edged with cold. "You may not know this yet, but anything Lu Shiyan can give you, I can give you just the same. And anything Lu Shiyan can't give you, I can give you too. You're clever—you should know that in business, one more friend is better than one more enemy."
Su Qingyuan stopped, but didn't turn around.
"Mr. Gu, you're right—one more friend is better than one more enemy. But a man like you will never be my friend, or anyone's friend. All you have are pawns and discarded pieces."
She walked out of the coffee shop. The autumn sunlight fell warm across her shoulders.
She didn't look back, but she knew Gu Changfeng was surely watching her go.
A man like that had probably never been called out to his face by a girl in her twenties. He might be angry—or he might, on the contrary, want her all the more. Not to have her as a person, but to have her as a "bargaining chip." Her refusal had only made her more valuable in his eyes.
At that thought, Su Qingyuan couldn't help but let out a soft laugh.
Ridiculous.
These men at the top, forever treating everyone as goods to be priced.
But she wasn't.
She never had been.
That evening, Lu Shiyan came to pick her up.
Once she was in the car, Su Qingyuan told him everything about Gu Changfeng's visit, start to finish. When Lu Shiyan had heard it all, his fingers tapped twice lightly against the steering wheel—his habitual gesture when thinking.
"You turned him down without hesitation," he said, his tone betraying nothing.
"What else? Was I supposed to work with him?"
"No. You were right to refuse." Lu Shiyan glanced at her sideways. "But a man like Gu Changfeng won't let it rest after being turned down. He'll come back, just in a different way."
Su Qingyuan leaned back against her seat, watching the neon flow past the window. "If he comes back, I'll refuse again. He can't very well kidnap me."
Lu Shiyan said nothing, but Su Qingyuan noticed his fingers tighten a fraction on the wheel.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Are you worried about me?"
"It's not worry." Lu Shiyan's voice dropped lower. "I'm thinking about how to make sure he never dares come looking for you again."
Su Qingyuan turned to look at him. The shifting light from beyond the window played across his face. His expression was calm, but there was a cold glint deep in his eyes—the kind she'd seen in business news, the look Lu Shiyan wore when facing a rival.
"What do you want to do?" she asked.
"Nothing." His tone warmed back to its usual temperature. "At least, nothing for now. He came today to probe—to test your attitude, and to test my reaction. If I struck back immediately, I'd be playing right into his hands. He wants to see whether I'd lose my head over you."
Su Qingyuan nodded. She understood now. When Gu Changfeng came today, the apology was fake, the poaching was fake—the probing was the real point. He wanted to know whether Su Qingyuan was Lu Shiyan's soft spot, and if she was, just how soft that soft spot was.
"So what's your reaction right now?" she asked.
Lu Shiyan reached out and took the hand she'd rested on her knee, lacing his fingers through hers.
"My reaction is—you're my soft spot, but not my weakness."
Su Qingyuan looked at their joined hands, and somewhere inside her was scalded by those words.
Soft spot and weakness. They sounded like synonyms, but from his mouth they took on entirely different meanings. A soft spot meant caring; a weakness meant making mistakes because you cared. He cared about her, but he wouldn't lose his judgment over her.
This was Lu Shiyan.
Forever clear-headed, forever restrained, forever making her feel that—a sense of security wasn't about how much he gave her, but about the fact that he never lost himself.
The car pulled up outside a restaurant. Not some upscale place—just an ordinary Hunan eatery, red lanterns hanging at the door, an ad for "signature chopped-chili fish head" pasted across the glass window.
Su Qingyuan took a look, then turned to Lu Shiyan. "Since when do you eat spicy food?"
"Since the last time you said you wanted chopped-chili fish head." Lu Shiyan undid his seatbelt and pushed open the door to get out. "I looked it up—this is the most authentic place in Nancheng."
Sitting in the passenger seat, Su Qingyuan watched his retreating figure, and suddenly smiled.
She'd mentioned wanting chopped-chili fish head about two weeks ago. It had been an offhand remark; she'd forgotten it the moment she said it. But he'd remembered. Not only had he remembered—he'd found the most authentic Hunan restaurant in Nancheng and made the trip specially to bring her here.
She pushed open the door, got out, and quickened her steps to catch up to him, slipping her arm through his quite naturally.
Lu Shiyan glanced down at her and said nothing, but the corner of his mouth lifted ever so slightly.
The private room in the Hunan restaurant was small but very clean. When the chopped-chili fish head arrived, its red oil bubbling, Su Qingyuan's eyes lit up.
"Is it good?" Lu Shiyan watched her.
Su Qingyuan picked up a piece of fish, put it in her mouth, and hissed in a breath at the heat—but her eyes shone as though someone had switched on a light behind them. "It's delicious! Hurry, try it."
Lu Shiyan picked up his chopsticks, took a small piece, and ate it slowly. His expression didn't change, but Su Qingyuan noticed the tips of his ears had gone faintly red—from the heat of the chili.
"Can't you handle spicy food?" she asked.
"I can."
"Then why are your ears red?"
"It's warm in here."
Su Qingyuan bit back a laugh and didn't call his bluff. She poured him a glass of ice water and pushed it in front of him. He glanced at her, picked it up, and took a big gulp, and the red at the tips of his ears slowly faded.
The two of them ate and chatted. Nothing profound—just little everyday things: the studio's new orders, the terms of the Cartier contract, a project Lu Group had been negotiating lately. In the past, Su Qingyuan would have thought "this has nothing to do with me," but now she listened intently, because this was his life. Just as he listened intently to the story behind every one of her pieces.
After the meal, Su Qingyuan went to settle the bill of her own accord. This time, Lu Shiyan didn't fight her for it. He leaned against the counter and watched her take her credit card from her wallet and hand it to the cashier, a contented light in his eyes—not because she'd paid, but because she'd finally stopped "fighting" him over the tab, and had simply, naturally, taken the task into her own hands.
"All paid." Su Qingyuan tucked the card back into her wallet and turned to him. "Let's go."
The two of them walked out of the Hunan restaurant, the night wind sweeping into their faces. The late-autumn wind had grown cold, and Su Qingyuan hunched her shoulders. Lu Shiyan immediately took off his coat and draped it over her shoulders. This time she didn't say "no need"—she gathered the coat closer, tilted her head to glance at him, and smiled.
"What is it?" he asked.
"Nothing." She buried her face in the coat's collar and said in a muffled voice, "It just feels like I've known you for a very long time."
Lu Shiyan reached out, slipped an arm around her shoulders, and drew her closer to his side.
"Not long," he said, his voice very low. "But there's a whole lifetime ahead of us."
Su Qingyuan leaned against his shoulder, watching the streetlights stretch their two shadows long, so long, overlapping into one—like a painting that would never fade.
A whole lifetime ahead.
Those words sounded so lovely.
Back at the foot of her apartment building, Su Qingyuan didn't go up right away. She stood at the entrance and turned to look at Lu Shiyan.
"Gu Changfeng said something today that I keep turning over in my mind."
"What did he say?"
"He said, 'Anything Lu Shiyan can give you, I can give you just the same. And anything Lu Shiyan can't give you, I can give you too.'" Su Qingyuan looked into his eyes. "And I wanted to tell him right then—what you give me isn't money, isn't resources, isn't opportunities. What you give me is the feeling of being seen. All my life, no one ever truly saw me. You're the first."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, saying nothing. The light of the streetlamp fell into his eyes, like shattered stars.
"Gu Changfeng can't give me this." Su Qingyuan's voice was soft, but earnest. "Because he doesn't see me—he only sees my value. But you see me—not Su Qingyuan the designer, not Su Qingyuan, Lu Shiyan's girlfriend, just Su Qingyuan."
The night wind went still.
Lu Shiyan reached out and gently cupped her face, his thumb tracing slowly across her cheekbone, as though sketching a painting he could never look at enough.
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm."
"The first time I saw you wasn't before that rainy night."
Su Qingyuan went blank. "What?"
"Three months ago, at the Nancheng Design Association's annual gala. You didn't have an entry pass; you stood in the corridor outside the venue, watching the exhibition inside through the glass doors." Lu Shiyan's voice was very, very low, like he was telling a secret he'd kept hidden for a long time. "I was standing inside the doors at the time, and I saw you. You were wearing a sweater washed pale with age, holding a sketchbook in your hands, drawing. You drew with such focus, completely unaware that someone inside the glass doors was watching you."
Su Qingyuan's eyes went wide. She didn't remember that scene. Three months ago, she had indeed gone to that gala—not as an invited guest, but to deliver a document to a designer client. While she stood in the corridor waiting for the client to come out, she really had watched the exhibition inside through the glass doors, and she really had sketched a few strokes in her sketchbook.
But she didn't remember anyone inside watching her.
"How long did you watch me?" she asked.
"A long time." Lu Shiyan's thumb stilled on her cheekbone. "Long enough that my assistant thought something was wrong with me. A man who never attended social functions, standing before a glass door, watching for ten minutes."
A sudden sting rose in Su Qingyuan's nose.
"Then why didn't you come find me back then?"
"Because of your eyes." Lu Shiyan's voice dropped even lower. "There was something in your eyes—not longing, not envy, but 'one day, I'll be standing in there too.' That look was too pure. I didn't want to disturb it."
Su Qingyuan's tears finally fell.
So before the rainy night, they had already met.
So when he'd said "tell me once you're certain," it hadn't been politeness—he really had waited for her a long, long time.
From the glass door three months ago, to the headlights of that rainy night, to the helping hand in the hotel lobby, to the silent company at the salon, to the key to the studio, to the coffee on the eighty-eighth floor, to the awards ceremony in Paris, to tonight's chopped-chili fish head—
He had been waiting all along.
Waiting for her to walk out, waiting for her to stand tall, waiting for her to turn around and see that there was someone who, from a very, very long time ago, had already been watching her.
"Lu Shiyan, you really are too much."
"Mm."
"Why didn't you tell me sooner?"
"Because if I'd told you sooner, you'd have thought I was fishing for credit."
Su Qingyuan laughed through her tears. She rose onto her tiptoes, wound both arms around his neck, and buried her face in the crook of his neck.
"Lu Shiyan, thank you for waiting for me."
Lu Shiyan tightened his arms and gathered her whole self into his embrace.
"You're welcome." His voice was low and tender against her ear. "Now that the waiting's over, it was all worth it."
Beneath the streetlight, the shadows of the two of them, locked in an embrace, fell across the ground like one complete circle.
With no gap.
[System: I said I'd retire behind the scenes, but to miss an iconic scene like this would be an insult to the System. Three months ago, before that glass door, he already saw you. He waited for you for three months, from autumn into winter, from when you were a nobody to when you blazed with light. What he waited for wasn't "the day you'd succeed"—it was "the day you'd be ready to be loved." All right, the System is truly retiring now. This time for real. You two carry on loving each other. The System is off to cry.]

========================================

Chapter 22 — On Both Sides of the Glass Door, Old Scores Settled Anew
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626224.html

After that night, Su Qingyuan felt as though life had taken on a soft-focus filter.
It wasn't that things had gotten easier—work was still hectic, and challenges still came one after another—it was that the way she looked at the world had changed. Before, it had been "I have to prove myself"; now it was "I know who I am." Between those two mindsets lay the sense of security that came from being steadily held up, for three whole years (counting from that first glance in front of the glass door), by one particular person.
The Cartier contract was officially signed on Wednesday morning.
The signing was held in a conference room at Cartier's Greater China headquarters—small, but very formal. Anna attended on behalf of the brand, and Su Qingyuan sat alone on the other side of the long table—she'd brought no lawyer, because she had already read every clause of the contract word by word three times over, and every figure, every definition was etched into her memory.
Anna signed her name on the contract and slid it across. Su Qingyuan took the pen and wrote the three characters of her name, "Su Qingyuan," in the space for the second party.
The instant the nib touched the paper, she remembered that just a few months ago, the most formal document she'd ever signed had been a rental lease. Now she was signing a partnership agreement with a top-tier international jewelry brand. Anna stood and extended her hand. "Ms. Su, here's to a happy collaboration." Su Qingyuan clasped her hand. "Here's to a happy collaboration."
There were no media at the signing, no champagne, no flowers. Anna said Cartier's style was "celebrate after the deal is done." Su Qingyuan liked that style—no fuss, no showing off, letting the results speak.
When she walked out of the Cartier building, Lu Shiyan's car was parked at the entrance. He hadn't gone up, because "that was your occasion, not mine." Su Qingyuan opened the door and climbed in, handing him a copy of the contract to look over. Lu Shiyan took it, flipped through it, nodded, and handed it back.
"Signed?" he asked.
"Signed."
"Congratulations."
Just one word. But Su Qingyuan could hear the weight in it—it wasn't a pleasantry, he was genuinely happy for her.
The car headed toward the creative park. Su Qingyuan settled back into her seat, then suddenly remembered something. "Oh, right—any movement from Gu Changfeng lately?"
Lu Shiyan's fingers tapped twice lightly on the steering wheel. "He's bidding on a commercial real estate project in Nancheng recently, and Lu Group is in the running too. His earlier attempt to sound you out is probably connected to that bid."
"Connected how?"
"He wants to know whether, if I got distracted—say, distracted over something to do with you—his chances of landing that plot would go up."
Su Qingyuan frowned. "So he wants to use me to keep you in check?"
"Not 'wants to.' He's 'currently trying.'" Lu Shiyan's tone was flat, like a man describing an equation he'd already solved. "He came to see you, to find out what kind of person you are. If you were easily provoked, easily swayed by the terms he dangled, he'd have used you to make trouble. But you turned him down, and you did it cleanly. So now he knows two things: first, you're not his pawn; second, my read on you wasn't wrong—you won't become my weakness."
Su Qingyuan let that settle for a moment, then asked the question she'd been wanting to ask all along. "If… and I mean if, if I hadn't turned him down back then—what would you have done?"
Lu Shiyan didn't answer right away. The car stopped at a red light, and he turned to look at her, his gaze very deep.
"You wouldn't have," he said.
"I said if."
"There's no if." The light turned green, and he faced forward again as the car moved on. "Su Qingyuan, I understand you—more deeply than you think. You wouldn't work with him, not because he's Gu Changfeng, but because you don't work with people who don't respect originality. That's your bottom line, and it has nothing to do with who I am."
Su Qingyuan fell silent.
He was right. Her refusal had nothing to do with Lu Shiyan; it had only to do with herself. She would never allow anyone to trample on originality, and Gu Changfeng helping Su Yurou steal her craft was, in itself, a red line that could never be crossed. That line would not shift by a hair, no matter what terms the other side offered.
She turned her head to look at Lu Shiyan's profile, then suddenly said, "Lu Shiyan, have you ever noticed that you understand me better than I understand myself?"
The corner of Lu Shiyan's mouth lifted slightly. "Not better. I've just been watching longer."
Watching longer.
From that glass door onward, he had watched her for three months. In those three months, what he'd seen was her at her most disheveled, her most unremarkable, her least "successful." But it was precisely those moments that made up the "Su Qingyuan" he understood—a woman who would draw even while standing in a corridor on the other side of a glass door, a woman the whole world had rejected yet who had never rejected herself.
Su Qingyuan drew her gaze back and looked at the streetscape rushing past the window. Outside, the sunlight was just right.
That afternoon, when Su Qingyuan returned to her studio, she found an unexpected person standing at the door.
Chen Xiaoman.
She was wearing a faded gray hoodie, jeans, and canvas shoes, her hair tied carelessly behind her head, and she looked far thinner than she had the last time, when she'd "posed as an assistant." Her head was lowered, her fingers clutching the hem of her clothes, not daring to look at Su Qingyuan.
"Qingyuan jie…" Her voice was tiny, like the whine of a mosquito.
Su Qingyuan glanced at her, said nothing, and took out her key to unlock the door. "Come in."
Chen Xiaoman froze for a second, clearly not expecting Su Qingyuan to let her inside. She hesitated for a few seconds, then followed her in.
The furnishings of the studio made Chen Xiaoman's eyes light up for an instant—the pieces displayed in the cases, the tools and design sketches scattered across the worktable, the moth orchids blooming just right on the windowsill—but she quickly lowered her head, not daring to look long. Su Qingyuan sat down at the worktable and gestured to the chair across from her. "Sit."
Chen Xiaoman sat down gingerly, hands on her knees, like a grade-schooler waiting to be lectured.
"You didn't come today to ask me to forgive you, did you?" Su Qingyuan asked.
Chen Xiaoman shook her head. "No. I came… to return the money."
She pulled an envelope out of her hoodie pocket, set it on the worktable, and pushed it across. The envelope was bulging, looking like it held a fair amount of cash.
"The fifty thousand Su Yurou gave me—I haven't spent a cent of it. The money for my mom's treatment was money I earned myself, working. Not this money. This money I've never dared to touch; it felt like it was burning my hands. Today I've made up my mind—I'm giving it back to you. I know fifty thousand can't buy back your craft, but it's the only thing I can do."
Su Qingyuan looked at the envelope but didn't reach for it.
"How is your mother?"
Chen Xiaoman's eyes reddened all at once. "She… passed away last week."
Su Qingyuan's heart clenched.
