"I'm sorry."
"Don't be." Chen Xiaoman's tears fell, but she didn't sob aloud; she just wiped them away clumsily with her sleeve. "Before she went, she told me a person has to be able to face their own conscience. She never knew I did something like that. If she had, she would have been so disappointed."
The studio was quiet for a long while.
Su Qingyuan stood, walked over to the lounge area, pulled a few tissues from the bookshelf, and handed them to Chen Xiaoman. Chen Xiaoman took them, covered her face, and her shoulders trembled faintly.
"Chen Xiaoman." Su Qingyuan's voice wasn't loud, but it was very clear. "Take the money back. It's not that I won't accept it—it's that you need it more than I do. Your mother is gone; from here on you have to walk your own road. Keep this fifty thousand and make a good life for yourself."
Chen Xiaoman lifted her head from behind the tissues, her eyes red, and looked at Su Qingyuan.
"Qingyuan jie, I…"
"I don't forgive you." Su Qingyuan cut her off, her tone calm. "What you did was wrong, and I won't say 'it's fine.' But I won't pursue legal action against you. Not because I pity you, but because you handed over the evidence of your own accord and admitted your mistake. In legal terms that's called a 'mitigating circumstance'; in human terms it's called 'knowing your wrong and being able to change.' But I want you to understand—'not being pursued' doesn't mean 'you did the right thing.' The road ahead, you need to think clearly about how you want to walk it."
Chen Xiaoman nodded hard, and her tears fell again.
She stood, tucked the envelope back into her pocket, bowed deeply, then turned toward the door. When she reached it, she stopped and looked back at Su Qingyuan.
"Qingyuan jie, that man—Gu Changfeng—he's no good. Su Yurou working with him won't end well. You… you should be careful."
"I know. Thank you."
Chen Xiaoman left. The instant the door closed, the studio fell quiet again.
Su Qingyuan sat at her worktable, looking at the closed door, silent for a long time.
She didn't feel she'd done some great act of kindness. She just felt that—Chen Xiaoman wasn't worth her time to hate. Hatred was a kind of drain, and her energy needed to be saved for creating, for the people who loved her, for the things that were worth it.
Her phone buzzed.
Lu Shiyan: 【There's a dinner tonight, a few of Lu Group's business partners. Do you want to come along? It's not a social obligation, just a meal. They want to meet you.】
Su Qingyuan looked at the message, a little surprised. Lu Shiyan had never let her take part in his business socializing before; he always kept her world and his world clearly separate. Inviting her himself today—what did it mean?
【Why the sudden urge to bring me?】
Lu Shiyan: 【Because Gu Changfeng might be there. It's not a coincidence—someone arranged it. Rather than have you alone in the studio, better to have you at my side.】
Su Qingyuan understood.
With Gu Changfeng there, Lu Shiyan didn't feel easy about her being alone. Not because he didn't trust her abilities, but because a man like Gu Changfeng was capable of any tactic. At his side was the safest place to be.
【All right. What time? Where?】
Lu Shiyan sent an address and a time, followed by one more line: 【No need to dress up specially. You're perfect as you are.】
Su Qingyuan looked down at herself—white shirt, black trousers, canvas shoes, hair in a ponytail, no makeup. She gave a little laugh; this man could even say "no need to dress up" with such unshakable conviction. But she still changed into a dress and put on light makeup. Not for Gu Changfeng—for Lu Shiyan. She wanted him to know she was willing to put a little thought into his world.
Seven in the evening, Nancheng's most exclusive private club.
Su Qingyuan walked into the lobby on Lu Shiyan's arm and immediately felt the eyes turning toward them from every direction. Most of the people here wore tailored suits and gowns, champagne in hand, their smiles polished and aloof. Their eyes landed on Su Qingyuan with scrutiny, curiosity, and a hint of "what makes her think she can stand at Lu Shiyan's side."
Su Qingyuan didn't shy away from those looks. She lifted her chin slightly, a polite, faintly distant smile at the corner of her mouth, her steps unhurried. She hadn't worn an evening gown, only a simple black floor-length dress, but its cut traced her figure just right—understated, yet powerful.
Lu Shiyan turned his head to glance at her and said in a low voice, "You changed your clothes."
"Mm."
"You look beautiful."
Just two words, but the tips of Su Qingyuan's ears went faintly red.
Deep in the lobby, in a corner by the window, several sofas formed a semi-open, private space. A few middle-aged men were already seated there, and seeing Lu Shiyan approach, they all rose.
"President Lu."
"President Lu is here."
Lu Shiyan gave a slight nod, not shaking each hand, simply stepping aside to let Su Qingyuan sit first, then taking the seat beside her. The gesture was small, but everyone present noticed it—Lu Shiyan let this woman sit first. What that meant, the shrewd people in the room understood perfectly.
"This must be Ms. Su? I've heard so much about you." A round-faced man seated across from them smiled and extended his hand. "I'm Zhao Zhicheng of Hengtong Group, an old friend of President Lu's."
Su Qingyuan clasped his hand with a polite smile. "Hello, President Zhao."
The others beside him introduced themselves in turn. Su Qingyuan responded to each, neither obsequious nor aloof. She noticed that Gu Changfeng was not among those present. She glanced at Lu Shiyan; his expression was very calm, and he gave a slight shake of his head—not shaking his head to say "he's not coming," but to say "no rush, he'll come."
Sure enough, a dozen-odd minutes later, a faint stir came from the lobby entrance.
Su Qingyuan turned to look. Gu Changfeng was walking in through the door. He wore a tailored navy-blue suit, his hair combed without a single strand out of place, and beside him followed a young woman—not Su Yurou, but a woman she didn't recognize, about twenty-five or twenty-six, in a wine-red gown, her makeup exquisite, her smile polished.
Gu Changfeng's gaze swept the lobby and landed precisely in Lu Shiyan's direction. Then he smiled, with an air of "just as I thought," and walked straight over.
"President Lu, it's been a long time." Gu Changfeng extended his hand, his face full of smiles, like an old friend who hadn't been seen in years.
Lu Shiyan stood and clasped his hand, his own smile equally polished. "President Gu, it has been a while."
The two men's hands clasped together—the pressure, the duration, the angle all just right, like a carefully choreographed performance. But Su Qingyuan could feel a subtle tension in the air, like two strings stretched to their limit: whoever let go first would lose.
Gu Changfeng released his hand and turned his gaze to Su Qingyuan. His smile didn't change, but a hint of scrutiny had entered his eyes. "Ms. Su, we meet again."
Su Qingyuan gave a slight nod, not rising and not offering her hand. "Mr. Gu."
The young woman beside Gu Changfeng glanced at Su Qingyuan, a flash of hostility in her eyes—Su Qingyuan caught it, but paid it no mind.
"And this is?" Lu Shiyan looked at the woman.
"My newly hired special assistant, Ms. Lin." Gu Changfeng introduced her with a smile. "Ms. Lin, this is President Lu of Lu Group, and his girlfriend—Ms. Su Qingyuan, the newly crowned Biennale gold medalist."
Assistant Lin smiled and held out her hand. "Ms. Su, I've heard so much about you. I read the coverage of your 'First Light' collection—it's truly beautiful."
Su Qingyuan clasped her hand and felt that the woman's palm was a little damp—nervousness? Or something else? She didn't dwell on it, let go, and smiled politely.
Everyone took their seats again. Gu Changfeng sat across from Lu Shiyan, the wide tea table between them. Assistant Lin sat beside him, quietly lowering her head, like an exquisite ornament.
A server brought fresh tea and refreshments. Gu Changfeng picked up his teacup, took a slow sip, then set the cup down and looked at Lu Shiyan.
"President Lu, that plot of land in the city's south—Lu Group's bidding on it too?"
Lu Shiyan picked up his teacup and took an unhurried sip. "We are."
"So am I." Gu Changfeng smiled. "Looks like we'll be opponents once again."
Lu Shiyan set down his cup, his tone flat. "Competition is what drives progress in business. President Gu, this isn't the first time we've been opponents, and it won't be the last."
The two exchanged a glance, and that one glance held more than any words could—probing, contesting, declaring war, conceding; every emotion flowed through in that single instant, then was drawn back in again.
Su Qingyuan sat quietly beside Lu Shiyan, not interjecting. She noticed Gu Changfeng's gaze sweeping over her from time to time, like a snake flicking its tongue in the dark. Outwardly she betrayed nothing, but inwardly she was wondering—what exactly did this man want from her? Or rather, what did he want from Lu Shiyan?
Halfway through the dinner, Su Qingyuan got up to go to the restroom.
The corridor was carpeted thick, and her footsteps were completely absorbed, so quiet it was like walking on clouds. The restroom door was dark wood; she pushed it open and went in, and had just turned on the faucet when she heard the sound of high heels behind her.
In the mirror she saw Gu Changfeng's Assistant Lin walk in.
Assistant Lin stood beside her, turned on a faucet, and pretended to wash her hands. But her eyes stayed on Su Qingyuan the whole time, through the mirror.
"Ms. Su, President Gu asked me to pass along a message." Assistant Lin's voice was very low, low enough that only the two of them could hear.
Su Qingyuan turned off her faucet and looked at her in the mirror. "What message?"
"He said that last time at the café, he remembered what you said. But he wanted to tell you—beyond pawns and discarded pieces, there's another role, called 'the one who moves the pieces.' If you don't want to be a pawn, you can be the one who plays the game. He's willing to play the game together with you."
Su Qingyuan turned around and looked into Assistant Lin's eyes.
"How long have you been with Gu Changfeng?" she asked.
Assistant Lin blanked for an instant. "What?"
"How long have you been with Gu Changfeng? Not a working relationship—that kind of relationship." Su Qingyuan's tone was very calm, as if she were asking about the weather.
Assistant Lin's face changed—from pale to flushed, from flushed to pale.
"I… I don't know what you're talking about."
"Your lipstick." Su Qingyuan pointed at the corner of her mouth. "The color isn't the same as when you arrived. When you came in it was a true red; now it's more of a rose. There was no time to touch up your makeup midway through the dinner, so the only possibility is—someone, somewhere outside this restroom, smudged your lipstick. And before you came into the restroom, the only place you'd been was at Gu Changfeng's side."
Assistant Lin instinctively raised a hand and touched the corner of her mouth, her face deathly pale.
Su Qingyuan looked at her, her tone neither mocking nor pitying. "You're relaying his message for him; he didn't come himself, because he knows I won't listen to him. But has he ever considered—sending you to deliver the message, and if I caught hold of something to use against him, how would he treat you then?"
Assistant Lin said nothing, her lips trembling faintly.
"Go back and tell Gu Changfeng," Su Qingyuan dried her hands with a tissue and tossed it into the trash, "the role of 'the one who moves the pieces'—I'll handle that myself, I don't need him to teach me. And I don't need him to do it 'together with me.' He should mind his own pieces and just not cross the line."
She pushed the door open and walked out of the restroom, leaving Assistant Lin alone in front of the mirror.
In the corridor, Lu Shiyan was leaning against the wall, waiting for her. Seeing her come out, he straightened up. He didn't ask why she'd taken so long, only held out his hand.
Su Qingyuan placed her hand in his palm and let him hold it.
"Let's go," he said.
"Okay."
The two walked back to the lobby side by side, the long, quiet corridor behind them—like the long road they'd walked together, from the abyss to the clouds.
By the time the dinner ended, it was nearly ten o'clock.
When Gu Changfeng left, he shook hands with Lu Shiyan and gave Su Qingyuan a nod, his smile as polished as ever. Assistant Lin followed behind him, head lowered, not daring to look at Su Qingyuan.
Su Qingyuan watched their departing backs and suddenly thought that Gu Changfeng was a truly pitiful man. He had money, status, and resources, but not a single person who followed him out of genuine feeling. Assistant Lin feared him, Su Yurou used him, those business partners stood in awe of him—but not one of them loved him.
He thought power could buy everything, but the very thing he couldn't buy was exactly what Lu Shiyan had—someone willing to walk side by side with him.
"What are you thinking about?" Lu Shiyan's voice pulled her back to reality.
"I'm thinking how lucky I am." Su Qingyuan turned to look at him and smiled.
"Lucky how?"
"Lucky enough to have met you."
Lu Shiyan looked at her smiling face, the light in his eyes as gentle as moonlight.
"It's not luck," he said, his voice low. "It's fate."
The night of Nancheng spread out behind them, the lights of ten thousand homes like a warm, glimmering sea.
Su Qingyuan leaned against his shoulder, gazing at that sea of lights, her heart very still, and very full.
【System: This chapter has no Su Yurou, no face-slapping. But there's a thing called "calm beneath the undercurrent." Gu Changfeng's probing, Assistant Lin's message, Lu Shiyan's restraint, Su Qingyuan's clarity—all the groundwork has been laid. Next, the storm is coming. But when the storm comes, the two of them are standing together. The System really has retired. This time it's for real. Don't believe me? Just check the next chapter and see whether the System is still around.】

========================================

Chapter 23 — Before the First Snow, Before the Storm
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626225.html

The design work for Cartier's capsule collection turned out to be more complicated than Su Qingyuan had anticipated.
It wasn't the difficulty of the creation itself—her inspiration had never once run dry—but the friction between the brand's requirements and her own personal style. On the third day after the contract was signed, Anna sent over a detailed set of design guidelines, an exhaustive document running more than a dozen pages, covering everything from gemstone selection to formal language, from price range to target demographic, each dimension annotated with explicit "recommendations."
Su Qingyuan read through the guidelines and fell silent for a long while.
The guidelines themselves weren't wrong. Cartier was a hundred-year-old house, and every set of its design guidelines was the distilled product of countless market figures, consumer insights, and accumulated brand equity. Following them would minimize market risk to the greatest possible degree. But the problem was this—she wasn't a Cartier employee, she was a guest artist. And the value of a guest artist lay precisely in bringing the brand something it didn't already have, not in replicating what it already possessed.
She set the guidelines aside, picked up her sketchbook, and laid the tip of her pencil against the paper—but she didn't rush to draw. Instead she closed her eyes for a moment.
She was turning over a single question: had Cartier come to her because she could draw a rose in the Cartier style, or because she could draw a rose that only Su Qingyuan could draw?
The answer was obvious.
She opened her eyes and began to draw.
By the time the first sketch was finished, the sky outside the window had already gone dark. She looked at the lines on the paper—lines that resembled neither the traditional Cartier nor entirely her own "First Light" style—hesitated for a few seconds, then snapped a photo with her phone and sent it to Anna, along with a single line:
"This is my direction. It may not fully align with the guidelines. But I believe this is the reason Cartier came to me."
After sending it, she set the phone face-down on the table and kept drawing. She didn't like waiting for replies; in the time spent waiting, she chose to work.
An hour later, Anna's reply arrived. Not text—a voice message. Su Qingyuan tapped it open. There was an emotion in Anna's voice she had never heard from her before—not satisfaction, not dissatisfaction, but something stirred, something faintly taut.
"Ms. Su, this direction of yours—I don't understand it."
Su Qingyuan paused.
"I don't mean that in a bad way." Anna was speaking much more slowly than usual, as though weighing each word. "I've worked at Cartier for fifteen years. I've seen the portfolios of countless designers, and I've never seen anything like this. It doesn't look like Cartier—but it makes me feel that Cartier should become this. I need a little time to take it in. Give me two days."
Su Qingyuan listened, and the corner of her mouth curved.
"I don't understand it" might be an even higher compliment than "it's beautiful." Because "beautiful" was within expectation, while "I don't understand it" was beyond it. And what lay beyond expectation often meant new possibility.
She didn't wait two days. The next morning, Anna's call came.
"Headquarters has seen your sketch." Anna's tone was completely different from the day before, carrying an excitement she couldn't quite suppress. "The creative director said one thing—'Let her draw. Don't put any limits on her.' Ms. Su, you've won."
Su Qingyuan held the phone, listening to Anna's voice, and a scalding wave of emotion welled up in her chest.
It wasn't "won against Cartier." It was "won against doing things strictly by the book." She had proven that a designer's greatest value lay not in obedience, but in creation.
"Thank you, Anna. And thank headquarters for their trust."
"Thank me for what? This is your own talent." Anna paused, then laughed softly. "Oh, right—headquarters asked, does the capsule collection have a name? If not, they'd like to call it 'Light Traces'—your light, Cartier's traces. What do you think?"
Su Qingyuan repeated the name silently to herself. Light Traces. Light was her core language; trace was the byword for Cartier's century of craftsmanship. Two words, writing two names side by side.
"Perfect. Let's call it 'Light Traces.'"
Hanging up, Su Qingyuan stood at the window, gazing out at the bare osmanthus tree, and let out a long breath. The white mist of her breath condensed into a small cloud in the cold air, then scattered. She suddenly realized—winter in Nancheng was on its way.
Her phone buzzed again. This time it wasn't Anna.
Lu Shiyan: [Something's come up with the bid. I may not be able to pick you up tonight. The driver will take you home. Stay safe.]
Su Qingyuan looked at the message, her fingers tightening slightly. The trouble with the bid—she didn't need to ask to know who it was tied to: Gu Changfeng. She replied: [Okay. You handle things, I'll be fine. Tell me when it's over.]
Lu Shiyan replied with a single word: [Mm.]
That "Mm" left her faintly uneasy. Lu Shiyan was never a man who made her feel "uneasy." He was always certain, always composed, always making her feel everything was firmly under control. But today that "Mm" lacked the certainty, the warmth, he usually carried. Su Qingyuan set down her phone, paced two laps around the studio, then picked up her bag and decided to head home on her own. No need to trouble the driver.
By the time she stepped out of the creative park, the sky had gone completely black. The late-autumn night wind poured down her collar, cold enough to make her hunch her neck. The street outside the park was nearly empty of pedestrians, only a few streetlamps glowing in lonely isolation.
She was just about to head toward the intersection when a black van suddenly pulled to a stop in front of her.
The door slid open, and someone sat inside.
Su Yurou.
Su Qingyuan halted, looking at that gaunt, pale face in the car, the obsessive cold light at the bottom of those eyes. She didn't step back, and she didn't panic.
"Su Qingyuan, get in. Let's talk." Su Yurou's voice was very calm—calm to the point of being eerie.
"No." Su Qingyuan's tone was equally calm. "If you have something to say, say it. If not, I'm leaving."
Su Yurou looked at her, then suddenly smiled. That smile reminded Su Qingyuan of when they were children—it was the exact expression Su Yurou wore every time, right before she put on her pitiful act in front of the adults. First the smile, then the rims of her eyes reddening, then the tears falling, and then everyone deciding that Su Qingyuan had bullied her.
"You're still like this. You never give me a chance." Su Yurou's voice softened, carrying a note of self-mockery. "Ever since we were little, you've been better than me at everything. Better at drawing, better at design, even Mom and Dad—adoptive parents though they were—liked you more. Do you know how much I envied you?"
Su Qingyuan said nothing, looking at Su Yurou as though looking at a shadow from long ago, already blurred by time.
"I stole your designs not because I couldn't make my own, but because I wanted you to know—you're no genius either. The things you make, I can make them too." The rims of Su Yurou's eyes reddened, but no tears fell. "But every time, you'd climb back up. Every time I thought you were finished, you'd climb back up again. Su Qingyuan, you really are infuriating."
The night wind blew Su Yurou's hair into disarray. She sat in the car like a caged beast that had been trapped too long and had finally given up the struggle.
"Are you finished?" Su Qingyuan asked.
Su Yurou looked at her, her lips moving as if she wanted to say something, but in the end she only shook her head.
"I'm finished. I'm leaving."
The door slid slowly shut. The black van pulled away into the night, its taillights shrinking into two blurred red dots in the distance.
Su Qingyuan stood beneath the streetlamp, watching the car vanish around the corner, and in her heart there was no hatred, no sympathy—only a strange feeling, something like "turning a page." Su Yurou hadn't come to apologize, nor to provoke. She had come to say one thing—I'm still here. I won't disappear. Don't think that just because you've won, you can forget me.
Su Qingyuan drew back her gaze and turned to walk toward the intersection.
I won't forget you. But I won't let you affect me ever again.
The driver came after all. The one Lu Shiyan had sent—a black sedan, pulling up punctually at the park gate. Su Qingyuan climbed into the back seat, told the driver the address, then leaned back against the seat and sent Lu Shiyan a message.
[Su Yurou just came to see me. At the park gate, in a car. Said a few things, then left. I'm fine.]
This time the reply came fast. Not text—a call.
"What did she say?" There was a tightness in Lu Shiyan's voice.
Su Qingyuan recounted roughly what Su Yurou had said. When he'd finished listening, Lu Shiyan was silent for a few seconds.
"Her coming wasn't Gu Changfeng's idea. It was her own."
"I know." Su Qingyuan said softly. "She came to say goodbye—not to make peace with me, but to wrestle with herself. She just wanted me to know that she's still alive, still breathing, still hasn't admitted defeat."
The other end of the line fell silent again for a few seconds. Then Lu Shiyan said something that made Su Qingyuan's heart burn.
"The bid on my end—the results come tomorrow afternoon. No matter how it turns out, tomorrow evening, we'll have dinner together. Just the two of us."
"Okay."
Hanging up the call, Su Qingyuan gazed at the neon flowing past the car window, and the corner of her mouth slowly curved upward.
No matter how it turns out. What those words meant was—win, and we celebrate together; lose, and we shoulder it together. She liked the word "together."
The next afternoon, Su Qingyuan waited for word in her studio. She didn't ask Lu Shiyan, afraid of disturbing him. But her heart hung suspended the whole time, like a taut string, so tense she couldn't even hold her carving knife steady.
At 3:17, her phone buzzed.
Not Lu Shiyan—a message from Zhou Wanyin:
[Qingyuan! Look at the news! The results of the bid for that plot in the south of the city are out!]
Su Qingyuan tapped open the news link. The headline was in bold black type:
"Bidding for the South City Plot Settled: Lu Group Defeats Dingfeng and Other Rivals to Secure the Land!"
She stared at the headline, her heartbeat suddenly surging, then slowly, slowly settling back into place.
Lu Group had won. He had won.
A few seconds later, Lu Shiyan's message came, just four words:
[Won. Wait for me.]
Su Qingyuan looked at those four words and suddenly felt her eyes go hot. Not because he'd won, but because of "wait for me"—win or lose, he would have come to say "wait for me." Win, and it was to celebrate; lose, and it was to lean on. To him, her being there was the destination.
She replied with one word: [Okay.]
Then she stood up, tidied her worktable clean, changed her clothes, and waited by the window.
Waited for that beam of headlights to light up the studio door.
At dusk, Lu Shiyan's car pulled up punctually beneath the osmanthus tree.
When Su Qingyuan walked out, he was already standing beside the car, suit jacket draped over his arm, shirt cuffs rolled up to his forearms, looking far more relaxed than usual—not slack, but the perfectly measured ease of a man who'd just set down some heavy burden.
When he saw her, he didn't say "I won," didn't say "let's celebrate." He simply pulled open the car door and said one thing: "Get in. I'm taking you somewhere."
Su Qingyuan didn't ask where. She obediently got in.
The car drove out of the creative park, threaded through Nancheng's bustling streets, growing more and more remote, until at last it climbed a mountain road she had never traveled before. The sky had already darkened; the streetlamps along the mountain road were sparse and scattered, the headlights illuminating the road ahead like a single moving shaft of light.
"Where are we going?" Su Qingyuan finally couldn't help asking.
"The summit." Lu Shiyan held the wheel with one hand and reached the other over to clasp hers. "You'll know once we get there."
Twenty minutes later, the car stopped at a scenic overlook at the mountain's summit.
Su Qingyuan pushed open the door and stepped out, and in an instant the sight before her struck her speechless.
All of Nancheng unfurled at her feet, the lights of ten thousand homes merging into a single warm sea of light, the distant river surface reflecting the city's glow like a flowing silver galaxy. Along the skyline, the last trace of sunset had not yet fully faded; the violet-red glow and the city's lights shimmered against each other, beautiful to the point of unreality.
"This place…" Su Qingyuan's voice softened. "How did you find it?"
"Back when the pressure got heavy, I used to drive up here alone." Lu Shiyan stood at her side, his gaze resting on the distant city. "But before, I came alone, at night, looked for a while, then left. Today, I came with two."
Su Qingyuan turned her head to look at him. The night wind had tousled his hair a little, and the line of his profile looked especially gentle in the city's lights.
"Back when you watched alone, what were you thinking about?" she asked.
"I was thinking—in a city this vast, when would there ever be someone who'd make me want to bring her here." Lu Shiyan turned his head to look at her, the light at the bottom of his eyes brighter than the ten thousand lights below them. "Now there is."
Su Qingyuan's nose stung, but she didn't cry. She leaned against his shoulder, looking at the city beneath their feet, and said softly, "Lu Shiyan, do you think someday we'll become two of those lights too?"
"No." Lu Shiyan lowered his head, his lips pressed to the crown of her hair, his voice muffled. "We'll be two lamps. The kind nestled right against each other."
Su Qingyuan's mouth curved, and she said nothing more.
The wind at the summit was a little strong, but with Lu Shiyan's coat draped over her shoulders, she wasn't cold at all. In the distance, the city's lights grew brighter and brighter, like a field of stars sprouting up from the ground.
They stayed at the summit for a long time—long enough that Su Qingyuan's legs went a little numb—before returning to the car.
On the way down the mountain, Lu Shiyan drove very slowly. Not because the road was bad, but because he didn't want this moment to end too soon.
"The bid—what's the reaction been from Gu Changfeng's side?" Su Qingyuan asked.
"He lost. He won't let it rest." Lu Shiyan's tone returned to the steadiness of his working hours. "But every time he loses, his resources shrink a little more. Dingfeng isn't his alone; there are other shareholders on the board. He's suffered setbacks in both the jewelry sector and the real estate sector now, and the other shareholders have already begun to question his decisions."
"How will he strike back?"
"I don't know." Lu Shiyan's fingers tapped lightly twice against the steering wheel. "But no matter how he strikes back, I'm prepared. And besides—" he glanced sideways at her, "—I have you."
That single glance sent Su Qingyuan's heart racing.
"What good am I? I don't understand corporate warfare."
"You don't need to understand it." Lu Shiyan drew his gaze back, the corner of his mouth lifting slightly. "As long as you're here, I won't lose."
Su Qingyuan turned her face toward the car window, pretending to watch the night scenery outside. Her reflection on the window glass showed a face whose curving lips simply refused to be pressed back down.
[System: Sneaking in for a quick word. There was no face-slapping in this chapter, no catfights—but there's a thing called "the calm before the storm." Gu Changfeng lost the bid, Su Yurou has shown new movements, and the Cartier project has been officially named "Light Traces." All the threads are drawing together. In the next chapter, or the one after, there will be a major conflict. But you two don't need to be afraid—because the two of you are standing side by side. All right, the System is really shutting up now. For real this time.]
The car stopped at the foot of Su Qingyuan's apartment building.
Su Qingyuan didn't get out right away. She sat in the passenger seat, looking at the streetlamps beyond the windshield, and suddenly said, "Lu Shiyan, do you think it'll snow tomorrow?"
Lu Shiyan checked the weather forecast and said, "Tomorrow's overcast, minus two to five degrees. Nancheng's first snow usually doesn't come until December."
"That's still a month away." Su Qingyuan sounded a little disappointed.
"Can't wait?"
"It's not that I can't wait…" She paused, her voice dropping lower. "I just want to watch the first snow with you."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, his gaze deep as the night.
He reached out, gently caught her chin, and turned her face toward him. Then he lowered his head and kissed her.
Not a fleeting, tentative kiss—a tender, lingering kiss that carried a promise. It lasted a long time, long enough that they both lost track of the hour.
When they parted, Su Qingyuan's lashes trembled faintly, her lips flushed red, her eyes bright.
"When the first snow comes," Lu Shiyan said, his forehead pressed to hers, his voice low and husky, "we'll watch it together."
"Okay."
Su Qingyuan pushed open the car door, walked two steps, then turned back.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Tonight's view from the summit—it was beautiful."
"Mm."
"But you're more beautiful than the view."
With that she spun around and ran, dashing through the building entrance and vanishing into the stairwell.
Lu Shiyan sat in the car, looking in the direction she'd disappeared, and slowly, slowly began to smile.
He picked up his phone and sent her a message:
[Su Qingyuan, what did you just say? I didn't catch it.]
Su Qingyuan's reply came fast—just one emoji: []
Looking at that emoji, Lu Shiyan laughed out loud. He started the car and drove out of the complex. Outside the window, Nancheng's night wind was chilly, but his heart was warm. From the inside out, from the past to the future, all of it was warm.
Inside the apartment, Su Qingyuan leaned against the door panel, both hands covering her face, her ears red enough to bleed.
What had she just said? You're more beautiful than the view.
God, how had she let that out of her mouth. So unbearably sappy. So unlike her.
But that last message Lu Shiyan had sent—she read it over and over, unable to bear deleting it.
That was the most understated "me too" she could think to give.
Outside the window, Nancheng's night was quiet and deep.
Tomorrow, there would be new challenges. But tonight, there was only a heart pounding away, and a scalding tenderness, caught and held steady.

========================================

Chapter 24 — Light Traces Bloom, and an Old Acquaintance Returns
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626226.html

Light Traces Bloom, and an Old Acquaintance Returns
After the bid, Nancheng's business world went quiet for a few days.
That quiet wasn't normal. It was the kind of suffocating stillness that comes before a storm. Su Qingyuan could feel it. Lu Shiyan still came to pick her up every day, still ate with her, still handled documents on the sofa in her studio—but the frequency of his phone calls had gone up, and his tone had turned flatter than usual. So flat it was almost devoid of any emotion at all, which was, if anything, the dangerous signal.
Su Qingyuan didn't ask. She knew that if he wanted to tell her, he would. And if he didn't, asking would only burden him with an explanation he didn't want to give.
She poured her focus into the "Light Traces" collection.
The freedom Anna had given her exceeded all her expectations—that one line from the creative director, "Let her draw, don't put any limits on her," was like a key that unlocked a door she'd never walked through before. And behind that door, Su Qingyuan found an entirely new version of herself.
The "Light Traces" collection was different from "First Light." "First Light" had been an autobiography—the process of struggling in the dark, breaking out of the cocoon, meeting the light, becoming the light. The emotion ran thick; every detail carried the warmth of her own self. But "Light Traces" was a dialogue—her dialogue with Cartier, with a century of craftsmanship, with that narrow seam between "classic" and "innovation."
She kept the core language of "light," but shifted her expression from "intense" to "restrained."
The first piece was a ring. Its center stone was an extraordinarily rare, ultra-pale pink diamond, so close to colorless that the pink only surfaced—faint, almost imperceptible—under certain light. She crafted a minimalist platinum band, free of any superfluous ornament, carving only a single, razor-fine groove along the inner edge of the band, so that when light passed through, it cast a faint shadow—and that was where the name "Light Traces" came from.
The second was a necklace. Its center stone was a flawlessly cut white diamond, set in a way that was almost "incomplete"—the diamond wasn't fully encased in metal but left half-suspended, as if it might fall at any moment. Yet in the instant of that fall, light would refract out from the bottom of the diamond and settle on the wearer's collarbone.
The third was a pair of drop earrings—two teardrop-shaped morganites, designed asymmetrically. The left ear was a whole, full teardrop; the right was a "cross-section," sliced away by a third to reveal the internal structure. Wholeness and incompleteness side by side, like two ways of telling the same story.
Three pieces, three expressions of light. Not "dazzling" light, but light that simply "existed"—understated, unclamoring, yet you knew it was there.
Su Qingyuan sent the design drafts for all three pieces to Anna, and this time attached no written explanation at all.
Anna's reply came far faster than before—just one line: "Headquarters says we can start production early. Spring launch. Are you ready?"
Su Qingyuan answered: "I'm ready."
She didn't ask whether "headquarters was satisfied." Anna's tone had already given her the answer.
The osmanthus tree outside the window was completely bare now, but the sunlight was still lovely, falling through the stripped branches onto the worktable like gold scattered across the floor.
Su Qingyuan put the design drafts away and went to fetch a glass of water. As she reached the pantry, her phone buzzed.
An unknown number. She picked up, and on the other end was someone she'd never expected.
"Qingyuan, it's me. Lin Haoyu."
Su Qingyuan's fingers tightened slightly, but her voice didn't waver. "What is it?"
"I… I want to see you. There's something I need to say in person. I'm not asking you to take me back—I know that's impossible now. It's something else. Something important. About Su Yurou and Gu Changfeng."
Su Qingyuan was silent for a few seconds.
"Where do you want to meet?"
"You decide."
"The café outside the creative park. Half an hour."
"Okay. Thank you for being willing to see me."
Su Qingyuan hung up and stood in the pantry, looking at the sunlight outside, and took a deep breath.
Lin Haoyu. It had been a long time since that name had crossed her mind. Back in that hotel lobby, she'd told him, "I don't pick up the garbage I've thrown out a second time"—that was the last time she'd spoken to him. Later he'd secretly photographed her and Lu Shiyan's relationship announcement and sold the pictures to a gossip account; Lu Shiyan had sued him, and his company had fired him too. After that, she'd heard nothing more of him.
And now he'd appeared out of nowhere, saying it was "about Su Yurou and Gu Changfeng."
Su Qingyuan picked up her bag and walked out of the studio.
At the café, Lin Haoyu was already waiting.
The moment Su Qingyuan saw him, she froze for a second.
He'd changed a great deal. Not for the better—he'd aged. A man barely in his twenties, looking well into his thirties. His hair was a tangled, untended mess; he wore a pilled gray sweater; his eyes were sunken, his cheekbones jutting—the whole of him like a tree drained dry of every drop of water.
When he saw Su Qingyuan walk in, Lin Haoyu shot to his feet, too abruptly, knocking over the coffee cup in front of him. Dark brown liquid spilled across the table. He scrambled to wipe it up, flustered and clumsy to the point of utter wretchedness.
"It's fine," Su Qingyuan said to the server coming over. "Could you bring him another cup, please."
She sat down and looked at Lin Haoyu. He looked at her too, his gaze laced with too many tangled emotions—regret, envy, self-reproach, and a sliver of lingering attachment he couldn't even admit to himself.
"You've changed a lot," he said, his voice hoarse.
"So have you." Su Qingyuan didn't bother with pleasantries. "You said there was something important. What is it?"
Lin Haoyu drew a deep breath, pulled a USB drive from his pocket, set it on the table, and pushed it toward her.
"On this drive are some chat records between Gu Changfeng and Su Yurou. Not all of them. One time Su Yurou got drunk and logged into her social account on my phone, then forgot to log out. I copied the chat logs."
Su Qingyuan looked at the USB drive but didn't reach for it.
"Why are you giving me this?"
Lin Haoyu lowered his head, staring at the now-dried coffee stain on the table, his voice very low. "Because I want to do one right thing. In this life, I've done too many wrong things to you. I want to make up for it, just once—even if it can't ever be made up."
The café went quiet for a few seconds. Someone at the next table was murmuring, and the coffee machine hissed steam.
"Lin Haoyu, do you know what it means to give me these?" Su Qingyuan's voice was very calm. "It means a complete break with Su Yurou. Once she finds out, she won't let you off."
"She stopped being willing to let me off a long time ago." Lin Haoyu gave a bitter laugh. "After she got out, she came to me once. Not to reconcile—to threaten. She said if I told anyone about her and Gu Changfeng, she'd make sure I couldn't survive in Nancheng. I was scared then. But I'm not scared now. Because I've got nothing left to lose."
Su Qingyuan looked into his eyes and saw something there resembling "relief." Not letting go—accepting. Accepting that he'd lost, accepting that he'd been wrong, accepting that there was no going back.
"I'll take the drive." Su Qingyuan reached out, took the USB, and slipped it into her pocket. "But I don't promise I'll use it. And I don't promise that if I do, I'll cover for where it came from."
"That's all right." Lin Haoyu raised his head and looked at her. "Use it however you want. I'm not asking for your forgiveness, and I'm not asking to atone. I just… want to make myself feel like I'm not a thoroughly rotten person."
Su Qingyuan said nothing. She didn't know whether Lin Haoyu counted as a "rotten person." He'd done many wrong things—betrayal, harm, secret photos, selling her out. But he had also, back when she was at her poorest, bought her a few meals—even if those meals had later become bargaining chips, "I treated you so many times, how are you going to pay me back." Human nature was too complicated to be summed up in two words like "good person" or "rotten person."
"I'm leaving." Su Qingyuan stood up.
"Qingyuan." Lin Haoyu called out to stop her, his voice trembling slightly. "Is he good to you?"
Su Qingyuan stopped walking but didn't turn around.
"Very."
"That's good, then." Lin Haoyu's voice sank lower. "That's good, then."
Su Qingyuan walked out of the café, sunlight settling warm on her shoulders. She touched the USB drive in her pocket and didn't look back. Behind her, Lin Haoyu sat by the café window, watching her figure vanish through the gates of the creative park, then lowered his head and buried his face in both hands.
He didn't cry. He'd long since forfeited the right to.
Su Qingyuan returned to the studio and plugged the USB into her computer.
There were a lot of chat records—hundreds of pages, fragmentary, spanning from the period of Su Yurou's detention to after her release. Su Qingyuan skimmed through quickly, and the more she read, the more her heart turned cold.
Gu Changfeng wasn't "helping" Su Yurou. He was "using" her. Every single thing—from arranging Lawyer Fang, to instructing her to blur the lines of plagiarism with "reference," to teaching her how to go head-to-head with Su Qingyuan at the Biennale—was all Gu Changfeng pulling strings behind the scenes. Su Yurou was just one of his chess pieces, a piece he could discard at any moment.
But the most crucial thing in the chat logs wasn't any of that.
There was one exchange, dated three days before the Biennale's final verdict was announced.
Su Yurou: "If Su Qingyuan takes the gold, what do we do?"
Gu Changfeng: "She won't."
Su Yurou: "How can you be so sure?"
Gu Changfeng: "I had someone put a word in with the judging committee. Not to make her lose—to make her win less cleanly. All it takes is a hint of a rumor that 'Lu Shiyan applied pressure,' and her gold medal gets discounted. People won't remember how good her work was; they'll only remember that 'she got there on a man.'"
Su Yurou: "And if it gets traced back to you?"
Gu Changfeng: "It won't. The person who passed the word has already left the country."
Su Qingyuan stared at this exchange, her fingers slowly tightening.
During the Biennale, there had indeed been a rumor that "Lu Shiyan pressured the judging committee." At the time she'd assumed Su Yurou had made it up herself—she'd never imagined Gu Changfeng was behind it. He wasn't helping Su Yurou win; he was making sure she couldn't win. Whether or not Su Qingyuan took the prize, he meant to splash a layer of filth across her trophy.
Su Qingyuan leaned back in her chair, gazing at the ceiling, and let out a long breath.
This man was darker than she'd imagined.
She picked up her phone and sent Lu Shiyan a message: [Lin Haoyu just came to see me and gave me this. Sending you a screenshot.]
She sent over the screenshot of that key exchange.
Lu Shiyan's reply came fast—not text, but a call.
"Gu Changfeng started laying his groundwork even earlier than you or I thought," he said, his voice deep. "He had his fallback ready before the Biennale. A plan for winning, a plan for losing. He never lets himself be in a position with 'no cards left to play.'"
"So what do we do?" Su Qingyuan asked.
"Nothing for now." Lu Shiyan's tone returned to its usual steadiness. "These chat records can't be used directly as evidence in court—the source is illegitimate, and Su Yurou's account isn't Lin Haoyu's. But they can be used elsewhere."
"Where?"
"Public opinion," Lu Shiyan said. "What Gu Changfeng fears most isn't the law—it's public opinion. His Dingfeng Group is preparing for an IPO right now. If news that he's linked to a plagiarism case breaks at exactly this juncture, investors will question his integrity. The listing could be shelved."
Su Qingyuan fell silent. She didn't really understand IPOs and investors and all that, but she could hear it—Lu Shiyan already had a plan.
"When are you planning to use these?"
"No rush." A trace of cold edged into Lu Shiyan's voice. "We wait for him to make the first move. Whoever moves first loses."
Su Qingyuan remembered something he'd said before—the rules of the business world weren't like a children's fight, where whoever throws the first punch is in the wrong.
"All right. I'll keep the drive safe."
"Su Qingyuan."
"Mm?"
"When Lin Haoyu gave you the drive, did he attach any conditions?"
"No. He said he wanted to do one right thing."
The other end was silent for a moment. Then Lu Shiyan said something that took Su Qingyuan by surprise: "He may genuinely want to change. But whether he changes is his business, and whether you forgive him is yours. Whatever you choose, I'm on your side."
Su Qingyuan held the phone, and a wave of warmth rose in her chest. He wasn't the kind of person who'd say "you should forgive him" or "you shouldn't forgive him." He handed the choice over to her, completely and entirely, and then said—whatever you choose, I'm on your side.
That was the source of the feeling of being held, steady and secure.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Got it. Are you picking me up tonight?"
"I am. Wait for me."
Su Qingyuan hung up, unplugged the USB drive, and locked it in a drawer. Then she walked to the window and pushed it open. Cold air rushed in, dispelling the heavy, stagnant air of the studio. In the distance, the cloud layer over Nancheng's skyline hung thick and grayish-white, as if it were about to snow.
She thought of what she'd said on the mountaintop the night before—"I just want to watch the first snow with you."
Maybe it would be soon.
That evening, when Lu Shiyan came to pick her up, he didn't look well.
Not unwell toward her—it was the kind of weariness that comes right after handling a thorny matter. After getting in the car, Su Qingyuan didn't rush to ask. Instead, she took a thermos out of her bag and handed it to him.
"What's this?"
"Red date and ginger tea. It's cold out—drink something warm."
Lu Shiyan took it, unscrewed the lid, and drank a mouthful. The bite of the ginger and the sweetness of the red dates melted on the tip of his tongue, warming a path from his throat all the way down to his stomach. He turned his head to glance at her, and the weariness in his eyes was replaced by something tender.
"When did you make this?"
"This afternoon. There were tea bags in the studio; I brewed it." Su Qingyuan's tone was offhand, as though she were speaking of something trivial. "You don't drink ginger tea, but your voice was a little hoarse today—you might have caught a chill. Ginger tea drives off the cold."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, and suddenly he smiled. Not the usual restrained, reined-in faint smile, but the kind that wells up from the bottom of the heart after someone has remembered a detail about you—a smile that can't be suppressed no matter how hard you try.
"Su Qingyuan, you're becoming more and more like me."
"Like you how?"
"Like the things I'd do."
Su Qingyuan paused, then understood his meaning—remembering every word the other person said, noticing every detail about them, and then taking care of things before they'd even spoken. Wasn't that exactly what he'd been doing for her all along?
"You rub off on people you're close to," she said, turning her face away, pretending to look out the window.
"You're calling me the good influence again."
"You are."
Lu Shiyan smiled, started the car, and pulled out of the creative park.
After they'd driven for a stretch, Su Qingyuan suddenly said, "Lu Shiyan, what do you think Gu Changfeng will do next?"
Lu Shiyan tapped his fingers lightly twice on the steering wheel—a habit of his when he was thinking.
"He'll go after your weakest point."
"My weakest point?"
"Not you yourself." Lu Shiyan turned his head to glance at her. "Your supply chain. Orders for your 'First Light' collection have already passed eighty million, supported by three suppliers. If one of them runs into trouble, delivery gets delayed. Delays mean unhappy clients, unhappy clients mean damage to the brand. And brand damage means the Cartier partnership takes a hit too."
Su Qingyuan's heart sank.
"You said before that one supplier's boss has a private connection to Gu Changfeng. That one?"
"Mm. Hengsheng Jewelry, the boss's surname is Jiang. He and Gu Changfeng have known each other for over twenty years." Lu Shiyan's tone was very calm, as though discussing a problem he'd already solved. "But I've already prepared a backup plan. If Hengsheng runs into trouble, the alternate supplier can step in within twenty-four hours. Capacity, craftsmanship, delivery cycle—all benchmarked against the originals. There won't be any gap."
Su Qingyuan looked at his profile, and that feeling of being held, steady and secure, surged up in her again.
"When did you put together the backup plan?"
"The day you signed the contract with Zhou Wanyin."
"That day again?" Su Qingyuan couldn't help laughing. "Have you made the day I signed that contract into your start button?"
The corner of Lu Shiyan's mouth lifted slightly. "More or less."
The car stopped outside a restaurant. Not a hotpot place, not a Hunan restaurant, but a Japanese place Su Qingyuan had never seen before, with a very small storefront. Pushing the door open, inside there was only a single long counter, behind which stood a middle-aged man in a white chef's coat. Seeing Lu Shiyan, he gave a slight bow.
"Mr. Lu, your seats are ready."
Lu Shiyan nodded and led Su Qingyuan to sit at the counter. There was no menu; the chef took one look at Lu Shiyan and began quietly preparing the ingredients.
"This is my private haunt," Lu Shiyan said in a low voice. "In all of Nancheng, you're the only person I've ever brought here."
Su Qingyuan's heart skipped a beat. A private haunt. The only person he'd ever brought.
The first course was sashimi—the medium-fatty belly of bluefin tuna, melting the moment it touched her tongue, the rich fat-aroma bursting on the tip of it. Su Qingyuan's eyes lit up, but she forced herself to hold back, not wanting to seem too unworldly. Watching her work so hard to stay composed, the smile in Lu Shiyan's eyes deepened.
"Is it good?"
"It's all right." Su Qingyuan picked up a second piece, twice as fast as the first.
"All right?"
"Really, it's all right." She picked up a third piece.
Lu Shiyan didn't call out her bluff. He lifted his cup and slowly drank a mouthful of sake. In the lamplight, the lines of his profile were cold and gentle all at once, like a painting composed with great care.
As Su Qingyuan ate, she suddenly set down her chopsticks and looked at him.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"Have you ever thought about—if one day everything were over—no Gu Changfeng, no Su Yurou, no bids, no lawsuits—what would you want to do?"
Lu Shiyan set down his cup and gave it serious thought.
"Take you to see the aurora."
Su Qingyuan went still.
"The aurora?"
"You said that when you were little, you saw a photo of the aurora in a book, and you thought it was the most beautiful light in the world." Lu Shiyan looked at her, his gaze soft as moonlight. "You said, 'If one day I could see the aurora with my own eyes, I'd have no regrets in this life.'"
Su Qingyuan opened her mouth, wanting to say something, but her throat felt as though something were lodged in it.
How long ago had she said that? Ten years? Fifteen? She didn't even remember saying it. But he did. He didn't just remember—he'd placed it into a plan for the future.
"Lu Shiyan, just how many of my memories have you stolen?"
"Not stolen." He poured her a cup of sake. "Collected. Every word you've ever said, I've collected it."
Su Qingyuan lifted her cup and took a big swallow, using the burn of the sake to press down the heat rising in her eyes.
"And you?" she asked. "Is there something you've always wanted to do but never have?"
Lu Shiyan looked at her and stayed silent for a long while.
Then he said, "Yes."
"What?"
"Wait."
"Wait for what?"
"Wait for you."
At last, Su Qingyuan's tears fell.
Not tears of sorrow, but the kind that—when someone loves you in the quietest, most patient, most certain way, loves you so much that you forget the whole world and remember only that single word, "wait"—come welling up from the bottom of the heart, scalding, unstoppable.
"Lu Shiyan, you really are a detestable man."
"Mm."
"You make me cry every single time."
"Mm."
"Can you stop waiting for me? I'm already here."
Lu Shiyan reached out and gently wiped the tears from her face.
"I know you're here." His voice was very low, very soft, like a night wind passing through a pine forest. "But I'll still wait. Wait for when you're tired and lean on my shoulder, wait for when you want to talk and I'm listening, wait for when you look back—and I'm always there."
The chef quietly set the next course on the counter, then withdrew soundlessly to the kitchen at the back.
In the whole space, only the two of them remained.
Su Qingyuan sniffled, swiped roughly at her face with her sleeve, lifted her cup, and clinked it against his.
"Then it's settled. The aurora."
"It's settled."
"No backing out."
"No backing out."
The two of them touched cups, the sake rippling faintly in the glasses, reflecting the warm amber light overhead.
Outside the window, Nancheng's night wind howled past.
The forecast said the temperature would drop tonight.
But Su Qingyuan knew—her winter would not be cold.
[System: The chapter ends here, and the System doesn't know what to say. Lin Haoyu's USB drive, Gu Changfeng's dirty trick, Lu Shiyan's backup plan, the promise of the aurora. Every thread is moving forward, every foreshadowing is drawing together. But what breaks the System most is that one word—"wait." When he said "wait," he wasn't waiting for you to become something. He was waiting for you to be ready to be loved. And he waited until it came. And so did the two of you. All right, the System is going off to cry. See you next chapter.]

Chapter 25 — Supply-Chain Warfare: Her Thunderous Counterstrike
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626227.html

Supply-Chain Warfare: Her Thunderous Counterstrike
The promise made at the Japanese restaurant was like a seed that took root in Su Qingyuan's heart.
The aurora. She had been only a teenager when she said those words, tucked away in the cramped attic of the old Su family house, flipping through a tattered travel magazine. Outside the window was Nancheng's grey, overcast sky; inside, her foster mother Liu Xiulan's voice nagging at her to go cook. She had curled up in the corner, staring at the photo of the aurora over and over, and silently told herself one thing — in this life, I have to go see it, just once.
Later she grew up, and the crushing weight of life buried that wish in the deepest recesses of her memory, until even she had forgotten it.
But he remembered.
When Su Qingyuan arrived at the studio the next day, she was still in good spirits. She brewed a cup of tea, sat down at her workbench, and got ready to keep polishing the samples for the "Light Traces" collection. The orders for "First Light" had already entered mass production; the first batch of finished pieces had shipped just yesterday, and customer feedback was excellent. Social media was flooded with posts showing them off.
She opened Weibo and saw one comment pinned to the very top:
"Got my 'First Snow' earrings — they're ten thousand times more beautiful in person than in the photos. Su Qingyuan, thank you for giving me the best gift on my thirtieth birthday. I always used to feel that nice things weren't meant for me. The moment I put these earrings on, I felt — I'm worth it."
Su Qingyuan read it three times, set down her phone, and drew a deep breath.
This was exactly why she did what she did.
At ten in the morning, the phone rang. Not her cell — the studio's landline. Only business partners had that number.
"Miss Su, this is Old Jiang from Hengsheng Jewelry." There was a trace of unnatural unease in the voice on the other end. "There's something I need to tell you about."
Su Qingyuan gripped the receiver, her heart giving a small lurch, but her voice stayed steady. "Go ahead, Mr. Jiang."
"Things over at Hengsheng have... hit a snag. Several of our production lines have to halt for environmental compliance inspections, so the timeline may slip. That batch of orders for your 'First Light' collection — I might not be able to deliver on schedule."
Su Qingyuan's fingers tightened slightly.
"Mr. Jiang, was this environmental inspection notice issued out of nowhere today?"
"Yes. We only got the paperwork this morning."
"And how long do you expect the delay to be?"
"At least... a month."
A month. Su Qingyuan closed her eyes, her mind racing. The first batch of the "First Light" collection had already shipped, but the second and third batches were still in production, with a promised delivery time of fifteen days. A month's delay would mean several thousand customers waiting forty-five days. In the jewelry industry, a delivery delay was a serious blow to a brand.
"Mr. Jiang, tell me the truth — is this environmental inspection a real reason, or did someone tell you to say it?"
The line went silent.
"Miss Su, I..."
"Is it Gu Changfeng?"
Silence again. Then Mr. Jiang sighed, his voice very low. "Miss Su, I'm sorry. I owe Mr. Gu a favor. He asked me to help him out this one time, and I couldn't refuse. I know it's wrong, but I... I really had no choice."
Su Qingyuan opened her eyes, her voice frighteningly calm. "Mr. Jiang, you owe Gu Changfeng a favor — so why are you using my customers to pay it back?"
"I—"
"Have you thought about what those thousands of customers will think of me when they wait forty-five days and still don't get their goods? They'll think Su Qingyuan can't be trusted, that the 'First Light' collection is a scam. What you're destroying isn't a batch of orders — it's a brand."
Mr. Jiang didn't answer. All that came down the line was heavy breathing.
"I understand, Mr. Jiang." With that, Su Qingyuan hung up.
She sat at her workbench, looking out at the grey sky, and took three deep breaths. The first pushed down her anger, the second her panic, the third let her settle into calm.
Then she picked up her phone and dialed Lu Shiyan.
"Hengsheng's a problem. Gu Changfeng got Mr. Jiang to delay a month, using environmental inspections as the excuse."
Lu Shiyan's voice was steady, without the slightest ripple. "The backup supplier is already in place. How many pending orders do you have?"
"Second batch, three thousand two hundred pieces; third batch, four thousand one hundred. Promised delivery is fifteen days from now."
"Send me the order data and the technical specs. I'll have the backup supplier start scheduling production this afternoon. The line switchover will be done within twenty-four hours — there won't be any delay."
That set most of Su Qingyuan's mind at ease. "How does the backup supplier's craftsmanship compare to Hengsheng's?"
"Higher. Hengsheng is top-tier domestically; the backup is a top-tier international contract manufacturer that's produced for several luxury brands. Costs will run a bit higher, but I'll cover the difference."
"You don't need to cover it." Su Qingyuan's tone was firm. "This is a cost of the 'First Light' collection — it should be on me. Give me the supplier's contact, and I'll negotiate with them myself."
There was a pause on the line. Then Lu Shiyan said something that warmed her right to the core. "All right. You negotiate. Whatever you can't close, I'll make up."
He wasn't the kind of man who said, "You can't handle it, so I'll take over." He was the kind who said, "You go first, I'll be right behind you, and if you can't hold on, you've got me." That kind of trust was more precious than any protection.
After hanging up, Su Qingyuan immediately contacted the backup supplier — a factory called "Zhenyi" in Shenzhen that specialized in contract work for top-tier international jewelry brands. The person in charge, surnamed Chen, was a woman in her forties who spoke crisply and to the point.
"Miss Su, Mr. Lu already gave us a heads-up. Send over your technical files and we'll start prototyping this afternoon. Once the samples are confirmed, mass production can launch in parallel."
"Director Chen, about the cost—"
"Mr. Lu said to work to your budget, and he'd cover the difference."
"No." Su Qingyuan cut her off. "I'll cover the difference. Quote me a real price. If I can accept it, I'll sign; if not, we'll keep talking. I don't want anyone thinking Su Qingyuan gets things done on subsidies."
The line was silent for a second, and then Director Chen laughed. "Miss Su, you're just like Mr. Lu said. He told me you'd say exactly this. Fine — I'll send the real price to your email, and after you've looked it over, we'll talk."
Su Qingyuan hung up, opened her computer, and began organizing the technical files.
Outside, the sky grew darker and darker, the cloud layer pressing low, as if it were about to snow. In the studio there was nothing but the clatter of her keyboard and the occasional rustle of a page turning.
Her phone buzzed. A message from Lu Shiyan:
[Gu Changfeng went after Hengsheng — he won't stop at just this one point. He may make a move on the public-opinion front too. Be ready.]
Su Qingyuan replied: [I know. Let him come.]
When she said "let him come," there was no bluster in her heart. Because she held trump cards — the chat records Lin Haoyu had given her, plus her own complete documentation of her creative process. If Gu Changfeng dared to sling mud in the court of public opinion, she'd dare to throw the evidence in his face.
Sure enough, at three in the afternoon, a wave of orchestrated chatter began appearing on Weibo.
The hashtag #TheInsideStoryOfSuQingyuansCartierDeal# quietly climbed onto the trending list. The gist of it: Su Qingyuan had only landed the Cartier collaboration because Lu Shiyan pressured Cartier's headquarters; Cartier China had been unwilling at first, but under the commercial pressure of the Lu Group, they'd had no choice but to accept.
No hard proof, no screenshots — just one blurry "insider tip-off" chat log. But that's how public opinion works: it doesn't need evidence, only a "maybe."
Su Qingyuan's comment section was immediately flooded with voices full of doubt:
"Just as I thought — she's relying on a man after all."
"That gold medal was probably won by Lu Shiyan's pressure too, huh? How dull."
"And here I thought she had real talent. Turns out it's all backers behind the scenes."
"Cartier really has no backbone, ditching the brand's bottom line for a business deal?"
But plenty of people spoke up for her too:
"Do you have any proof? You're treating one chat log as gospel truth?"
"Su Qingyuan's 'First Light' collection is right there in front of you — is that level of craftsmanship something you can squeeze out by 'pressure'?"
"The Biennale gold medal was judged by an international panel. Lu Shiyan's arm isn't long enough to reach all the way to Paris, is it?"
The two camps quarreled endlessly.
Su Qingyuan looked at the comments and felt no anger, no grievance — only a clarity so calm it bordered on cold. She knew this chatter wasn't something netizens had stirred up on their own; it was an organized troll army. Gu Changfeng was testing her reaction — seeing whether she'd panic, whether she'd cry, whether she'd silently endure it like she used to.
She wouldn't anymore.
She opened Weibo and drafted a long post, but didn't rush to send it. Instead she checked it over three times, making sure every single word would hold up. Then she sent Lu Shiyan a message: [I want to post a Weibo responding to the chatter. Take a look.]
Lu Shiyan read it and replied: [Post it. I'll have the PR team back you up.]
Su Qingyuan drew a deep breath and pressed send.
"About the rumors circulating lately, I only have a few things to say:
1. The Biennale gold medal was decided by independent votes from twelve international judges. The entire judging process was recorded and can be verified. I did not — and do not need to — pressure anyone.
2. The Cartier collaboration was one I pitched myself, design proposals in hand. I negotiated every clause of the contract one by one — a sixty-forty split, sixty to me, forty to them. This is the first time Cartier has ever offered such terms to a Chinese designer. If that's the result of 'pressure,' then it's my design proposals that did the pressuring.
3. My 'First Light' collection — from concept to finished product, every sketch, every revision, every step of craftsmanship — is documented with timestamps. I have already retained a lawyer to reserve the right to pursue legal action against those spreading rumors.
4. Finally, I want to say thank you to everyone who supports me. To those who don't believe in me — I don't need you to. Time will prove everything.
That's all."
After the long post went out, the tide in the comment section began to turn.
"She's so fierce! Straight-up posting the contract terms?"
"Sixty-forty? Sixty to her, forty to Cartier? Damn, that's a first for Cartier, isn't it?"
"The Biennale judging process can be verified — haters, zip it."
"I believe in her. Anyone who can make 'First Snow' doesn't need to rely on a man."
But some haters kept up their stubborn front: "Got the guts to post the judging records, then? What good is just saying it 'can be verified'?"
Su Qingyuan didn't reply to that comment. She didn't need to spar with every hater. She only needed to lay out the facts; the rest, she'd leave to time.
Meanwhile, Zhou Wanyin reposted her Weibo with the caption: "I've been involved in the 'First Light' collection from day one. Qingyuan's talent doesn't need anyone's endorsement. I'll stake my career on it."
A few minutes later, Cartier's official account also posted a brief message: "We chose to collaborate with Ms. Su Qingyuan because of her work. There is no other reason."
The two reposts landed like two resounding slaps across the face of the rumor-mongers.
Looking at Cartier's official statement, Su Qingyuan felt a warmth well up inside her. She knew the statement wasn't entirely the brand's own doing — Lu Shiyan must have done some work behind the scenes — but the content of the statement was true. Cartier really had chosen her because of her work. Without that factual foundation, no amount of "work" would have mattered.
Within a few hours, the tide of public opinion reversed completely. The trending hashtag changed from #TheInsideStoryOfSuQingyuansCartierDeal# to #SuQingyuanResponds#, and then to #SuQingyuansSixtyFortySplit#. By evening, the tone of the comment section had shifted entirely:
"Sis is so badass!"
"As of today, I'm a fan of Su Qingyuan's career!"
"Even Cartier came out to back her — what do the haters have left to say?"
Su Qingyuan closed Weibo and rubbed her aching eyes.
It wasn't that she didn't care about public opinion. She did — but she'd learned not to lose herself in that caring.
The studio door swung open. Lu Shiyan walked in, carrying an insulated bag.
"You haven't had dinner yet, have you?" He set the bag down on the table in the lounge area. "Brought some congee and side dishes."
Su Qingyuan looked at him, and suddenly her nose stung. Not the sting of grievance — the kind that comes from fighting a hard battle out in the world, then coming home to find someone left a light on for you, and brought hot congee besides.
"You saw it?" She walked over and sat down on the sofa.
"I saw it." Lu Shiyan ladled out the congee and set it in front of her. "That Weibo post you put up — it was good. I read it three times."
Su Qingyuan picked up the congee and took a sip. Century egg and lean pork congee — the same taste as last time. He'd made it.
"Did you learn another dish?" she asked.
"Mm. Congee doesn't count as a dish." Lu Shiyan sat down across from her. "But it's better than last time. Try it."
Su Qingyuan took another sip — it really was better than last time. The grains were softer and stickier, the seasoning better balanced.
"Lu Shiyan, did you secretly sign up for a cooking class?"
"No. Learned it from videos."
"You can learn this well just from videos?"
"Talent." Lu Shiyan said the word without batting an eye, and Su Qingyuan nearly choked on her congee.
She set down her bowl, looked at him, and suddenly laughed. "You — you've got a talent for everything. Talent for congee, talent for negotiation. Even the people spreading rumors know your name is useful — when they smear me, they don't say 'Su Qingyuan relies on a man,' they say 'Su Qingyuan relies on Lu Shiyan.' Which means in their minds, your name is synonymous with 'backer.'"
Lu Shiyan looked at her, his gaze gentle. "Does that bother you?"
"Bother me how?"
"Bother you, people saying you 'rely on me.'"
Su Qingyuan thought about it seriously, then shook her head. "No. Because I know I don't. What others say can't change the facts. And besides—" she paused, her voice softening, "if relying on you means I take a few less detours, I don't mind being talked about. Because I've already walked enough crooked roads."
Lu Shiyan reached out and took her hand where it rested on the table, his thumb slowly tracing circles on the back of it.
"Su Qingyuan, you're stronger than I thought."
"It's not strength." Su Qingyuan clasped his hand back. "It's that I'm not afraid anymore. I used to be afraid people would say I relied on connections, so I tried desperately to prove myself. Now I'm not afraid, because I know who I am. You just let me know it a little faster — without you, I'd have figured it out eventually anyway. It would only have been slower."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, the light in his eyes as deep as night.
"Then from now on, can I keep 'letting you know it a little faster'?"
Su Qingyuan laughed, her eyes curving into crescents.
"You can. But not too much. I'm afraid if I get used to it, I won't be able to quit it."
"Then don't quit."
The two of them looked at each other, and both laughed.

Outside, the sky had gone completely dark. The Nancheng wind howled, and the congee in the insulated bag was still steaming. Su Qingyuan leaned back against the sofa, pulled Lu Shiyan's hand over to rest on her knee, then leaned against his shoulder.
"Lu Shiyan."
"Mm."
"What do you plan to do about the Hengsheng situation?"
"Nothing." Lu Shiyan's voice was light. "Mr. Jiang chose to help Gu Changfeng, so he has to bear the consequences. Hengsheng has lived off the Lu Group's contracts for five years. Now that he's torn up our agreement, none of the Lu Group's business will ever work with him again. With his factory losing its biggest client, it won't last half a year."
Su Qingyuan was silent for a few seconds. She didn't pity Mr. Jiang. An adult's choices are all his own to pay for.
"And Gu Changfeng?"
"His move against Hengsheng this time was to probe the resilience of your supply chain. Now that he's found you have a backup plan, and that you switched over this fast, he won't go after the supply chain next time." Lu Shiyan's fingers slid through her hair. "He'll switch to another method."
"What method?"
"I don't know. But he'll definitely strike again. His IPO plan was thrown off by losing that bid — he needs a new opening." Lu Shiyan paused. "And in his eyes, you're my opening."
Su Qingyuan straightened up off his shoulder and looked into his eyes.
"Then I won't be his opening."
Lu Shiyan looked at her, waiting for her to go on.
"I'll be his end point." Su Qingyuan's voice was quiet, but every word was crystal clear. "Every time he tries to use me to get at you, he'll slam into a wall. And that wall isn't me — it's my work, my bottom line, my principles. Those are things he can't break through."
Lu Shiyan looked at her for a long, long while. Then he leaned in and dropped a feather-light, infinitely tender kiss on her forehead.
"That wall is mine too."
Su Qingyuan closed her eyes, feeling the warmth of that kiss.
Outside, the wind grew stronger. The weather forecast said there might be sleet tonight.
But inside the studio, the heat was on, the congee was still warm, and the two of them leaned against each other like two trees standing side by side — roots intertwined underground, branches touching in the wind.
Nothing could blow them down.
[System: This chapter, the female lead takes on public opinion head-on, Lu Shiyan's backup supplier slots in seamlessly, and both Cartier and Zhou Wanyin step up to vouch for her. The face-slapping is solid, the pacing satisfying, and the sweetness sneaks up on you. Gu Changfeng's supply-chain attack is perfectly neutralized, and the public-opinion war is beaten back by one Weibo post from the female lead plus a brand statement. But Gu Changfeng won't take this lying down — next chapter he may switch directions. Also, Su Yurou hasn't appeared in a while; it's time for her to come on stage. The System awaits the next chapter.]

========================================

Chapter 26 — Yurou's Desperate Gamble, Lu Shiyan's Thunderbolt Tactics
https://www.xbanxia.cc/books/417510/72626228.html

The Hengsheng affair was put to rest faster than anyone had expected.
The Zhenyi factory completed its production-line switchover within twenty-four hours, and the first batch of replacement products had a sample ready by the third day. Su Qingyuan flew to Shenzhen to inspect the goods herself, and the moment she opened the sample box, the worry that had been hanging over her finally settled back into place. Zhenyi's craftsmanship was a full cut above Hengsheng's—the precision of the diamond settings, the fineness of the metal polishing, even the heft and texture of the packaging box—all of it hit the level of an international top-tier brand.
"Director Chen, how much higher is the cost on this batch of samples compared to Hengsheng?" Su Qingyuan asked.
Director Chen quoted a figure. Su Qingyuan ran the numbers in her head, and at that cost the profit margin on the "First Light" collection would drop by nearly ten percentage points. Ten percentage points was no small thing for an order of this volume.
"Director Chen, can the cost come down? Not by cutting quality—by streamlining the process."
The look in Director Chen's eyes shifted. Most designers, hearing that costs had gone up, either gritted their teeth and accepted it or switched to a cheaper supplier. Very few would say "streamline the process"—which meant Su Qingyuan wasn't just a designer. She understood production, understood supply chains, understood how to control costs without sacrificing quality.
"It can. Give me a week and I'll rework the production schedule. Some steps can run in parallel; some can be outsourced to our long-term partner workshops. Quality won't drop, and I can bring the cost down five points."
"Five points isn't enough. I want eight."
Director Chen was silent for a moment, then suddenly laughed. "Miss Su, you're really a lot like Director Lu. Back when he was negotiating the OEM agreement with us, he said the exact same thing—'Eight points, not one less.'"
Su Qingyuan blinked, then curved her lips. "And did he get them in the end?"
"He did. Which is why we can sit here talking today." Director Chen stood up and extended a hand. "Eight points—I'll try. No guarantees, but I'll give it my best."
"Thank you, Director Chen."
On the flight back from Shenzhen, Su Qingyuan sat by the window with a tablet in her hands, scrolling through the production-progress report for the "Light Traces" collection. Cartier's supply chain was far more mature than the one she'd cobbled together herself—every link had a standardized process and strict timelines, leaving her nothing to worry about.
A strange feeling came over her. She used to think she had to do everything herself, because there was no one she could lean on. Now she had Lu Shiyan, she had Zhou Wanyin, she had partners like Director Chen—and yet she was busier than ever. It wasn't that there was more to do. It was that there was more she could do.
The plane broke through the cloud layer, and sunlight poured in, lighting up the whole cabin.
She picked up her phone and sent Lu Shiyan a message: [On the flight back to Nancheng. Should land around three this afternoon.]
Lu Shiyan replied quickly: [I'll come get you.]
Su Qingyuan: [Don't you have a meeting this afternoon?]
Lu Shiyan: [Pushed it.]
Su Qingyuan looked at those two words—"pushed it"—and curved her lips. She remembered a saying she'd once heard: to tell whether someone truly cares about you, don't look at the special things they do for you—look at the important things they give up for you. Lu Shiyan's meetings were never ordinary meetings. The only person who could make him push one aside to pick her up from the airport was, probably, her.
When the plane landed, a light rain was falling over Nancheng.
The late-autumn rain was chilly, pattering against the cabin windows and drawing long, thin streaks of water down the glass. Su Qingyuan walked out into the arrivals hall and spotted Lu Shiyan at a single glance.
He stood by the exit in a black overcoat and a gray scarf, holding a black long-handled umbrella. He looked like he'd stepped straight out of a magazine; travelers passing by all gave him a second glance, but no one dared approach—because his expression said "keep your distance."
But the instant he saw Su Qingyuan, that "keep your distance" expression shattered. He came toward her and tilted the umbrella over her, leaving half his own shoulder out in the rain.
"Didn't you say you pushed the meeting? Why are you still in a suit?" Su Qingyuan looked at his rain-dampened shoulder and reached out to brush it off.
"Came straight over after the meeting." Lu Shiyan wrapped an arm around her shoulders and headed for the parking lot. "Couldn't push it, so I moved it online. Ran it from the car."
Su Qingyuan leaned into his embrace, listening to the steady beat of his heart amid the sound of the rain, and suddenly all her Shenzhen weariness melted away.
In the car, Lu Shiyan didn't start the engine right away. Instead he reached into the back seat and handed her a paper bag.
"What's this?"
"Bought it at the airport. You said last time you wanted croissants."
